Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Vowing a Year's Fast and the Prohibited Days (Inter-Madhhab Dispute)
Ruling on making up fasts on prohibited days when vowing a year's fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vowing a year's fast regarding prohibited days, explain the dispute with Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i, and apply the ruling to cases with and without specification of consecutiveness.

Core Idea
A vow to fast a year includes prohibited days but they must be broken and made up consecutively.

This lesson addresses a nuance in the law of vows (nazr). When someone vows to fast an entire year, the prohibited days (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and days of Tashriq) fall within that period. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a vow that specifies the year and one that only stipulates consecutiveness. Learn how the prohibition interacts with the obligation of the vow, and why Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i disagree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the vow scenario
Determine whether the vow specifies a year or only stipulates consecutiveness. This affects the ruling on makeup.
If the year is specified, the vow includes all days. If unspecified but with mutaba'ah, the same applies because consecutiveness inevitably includes the prohibited days.
2
Apply the rule of breaking and making up
The person must break the fast on the prohibited days and make them up later. This fulfills the obligation of the vow while respecting the prohibition.
The makeup is required because the fast on a prohibited day is deficient due to the prohibition.
3
Understand the condition of mutaba'ah
If consecutiveness is stipulated, the makeup must be consecutive as much as possible to honor the condition.
If mutaba'ah is not stipulated, the makeup does not need to be consecutive.
4
Analyze the dispute
Compare the Hanafi position with that of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who argue the vow is invalid on prohibited days because the prohibition is absolute.
The Hanafi response: the prohibition is tanzih (dislike), not tahrim (prohibition), and the need to fulfill the vow overrides it, but the fast remains deficient.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafi requires makeup; the opposing view may consider the entire vow flawed or require re-do.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, but the ikhtilaf is legitimate.

Source Text

اس سال روزہ کی نذر مانی تو یوم الفطر، یوم انحر اور ایام تشریق کے روزے نہ رکھے اور قضاء پوری کرے وَلَوْ قَالَ لِلَّهِ عَلَى صَوْمُ هَذِهِ السَّنَةِ أَفْطَرَ يَوْمَ الْفِطْرِ وَيَوْمَ النَّحْرِ وَأَيَّامَ التَّشْرِيْقِ وَقَضَاهَا لأنَّ النَّذَرَ بِالسَّنَةِ الْمُعَيَّنَةِ نَذَرُ بِهذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ وَكَذَا إِذَا لَمْ يُعِينُ لكِنَّهُ شَرِطَ التَابُعَ لأَنَّ الْمُتَابَعَةَ لَا تَعِرَى عَنْهَا لَكِنْ يَقْضِيهَا فِى هَذَا الفَصَّل مَوْصُولَةً تَحْقِيفًا لِلتَتابع بِقَدْرِ الإِمْكَانِ وَيَتَاتَّى فِى هَذَا خِلَافُ زُفْرَ وَ الشَّافِعِي لِلنَّهَى عَنِ الصَّوْمِ فِيهَا وَهُوَ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَلَا لَا تَصُومُوا فِى هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ فَإِنَّهَا أَيَّامُ اكْلِ وَشُرْبِ وَبِعَالٍ وَقَدْ بَيَّنَا الْوَجْهَ فِيهِ وَالْعُدْرَ عَنْهُ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَشْتَرِطِ التَّتَّابُعَ لَمْ يَجُزُهُ صَومَ هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ لِأَنَّ الْأَصْلَ فِيهَا يَلْتَرَمُهُ الْكَمَالُ وَالْمُؤَدَّى نَاقِصَّ لِمَكَانِ النَّهْي بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا عَيَّنَهَا لِأَنَّهُ الْتَزَمَ بِوَصْفِ التَّقْصَانِ فَيَكُونُ الأداء بالوصف المُلتزم
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نذر کرنے والے نے کہا کہ اللہ کے واسطے مجھ پر اس سال کے روزے ہیں تو یوم فطر، یوم نحر اور ایام تشریق میں افطار کرے اور ان کی قضاء کرے کیونکہ متعین سال کی نذر کرنا ان ایام کی بھی نذر ہے اور ایسے ہی جب متعین نہ کیا ہو لیکن پے در پے روزے رکھنے کی شرط لگا دی کیونکہ (ایک سال کے ) پے در پے روزے ان ایام سے خالی نہ ہوں گے۔ لیکن اس صورت میں ان کی قضاء متصلاً کرے تا کہ بقدر امکان تابع متحقق ہو جائے۔ اور اس میں امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا اختلاف پیدا ہوگا کیونکہ ان ایام میں روزے سے ممانعت وارد ہوئی ہے اور وہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ قول ہے کہ آگاہ رہو کہ ان ایام میں روزے نہ رکھو کیونکہ یہ ایام کھانے پینے اور عورتوں کے ساتھ جماع کرنے کے ہیں اور ہم نے اس میں وجہ بیان کر دی ہے اور اس سے عذر بھی بیان کر دیا ہے اور اگر اس نے پے در پے کی شرط نہ لگائی تو ان ایام کا روزہ اس کو کافی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس نے اپنے اوپر جو لازم کیا ہے اس میں کامل ہونا اصل ہے اور ان ایام میں جو ادا کیا وہ ناقص ہے کیونکہ نہی موجود ہے برخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ ان ایام کو متعین کر لیا ہو کیونکہ اس نے وصف نقصان کے ساتھ التزام کیا ہے۔ پس ادا کرنا اس وصف کی ساتھ حاصل ہو جائے گا جو اس نے الزام کیا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے ایک سال کے روزوں کی قضاء کی تو اس کی دوصورتیں ہیں یا تو اس کو متعین کر دیا ہوگا
If someone vows a fast of this year, then he breaks fast on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq, and makes them up. And if he says 'Lillahi alayya sawmu hadhihi al-sanah' (For Allah upon me is the fast of this year), he breaks fast on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq and makes them up because the vow of a specified year includes a vow of these days. Similarly, if he did not specify but stipulated consecutiveness (tutaba'), because the consecutiveness over a year cannot be free from these days. But he makes them up continuously in this section to actualize the consecutiveness as much as possible. In this, there is a difference of opinion of Zufar and al-Shafi'i due to the prohibition of fasting in these days, which is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Beware, do not fast in these days, for they are days of eating, drinking, and conjugal relations.' We have already explained the reason and the excuse for it. And if he did not stipulate consecutiveness, fasting these days does not suffice him because the origin in what he has obligated upon himself is completeness, and what is performed is deficient due to the prohibition. Unlike when he specified them (i.e., specified the days), because he undertook with the description of deficiency; so performance with the undertaken description is achieved. Translation: And if someone who makes a vow said 'Lillahi alayya sawmu hadhihi al-sanah', then he breaks fast on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq and makes them up because the vow of a specified year is a vow of these days. Similarly, if he did not specify but stipulated consecutiveness, because the consecutiveness (over a year) will not be free from these days. But he makes them up continuously in this case so that consecutiveness is realized as much as possible. In this, there arises a difference of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i because of the prohibition against fasting in these days, and that is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Beware, do not fast in these days, for they are days of eating, drinking, and conjugal relations.' And we have already explained the reason and the excuse for it. And if he did not stipulate consecutiveness, fasting these days is not sufficient for him because the origin in what he has obligated upon himself is completeness, and what is performed is deficient due to the prohibition. Contrary to the case when he specified these days (i.e., made them part of the vow), because he undertook with the description of deficiency; so performance is achieved with the description he undertook. Explanation: The case is that if a person vowed the fasts of a year, there are two possibilities: either he specified it (meaning the year) or not.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on a vow to fast a full year, addressing the prohibited days (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and the days of Tashriq). The Hanafi position is that when a person vows to fast a specific year, these prohibited days are included in the vow, but the person must break the fast on those days and make them up later. If the vow is for an unspecified year but with a condition of consecutive fasting (tutaba'), the same ruling applies because consecutiveness over a year inevitably includes the prohibited days. However, the makeup must be done consecutively to preserve the mutaba'ah as much as possible. There is a dispute with Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i, who argue that fasting on these days is absolutely prohibited and cannot be made up because the prohibition invalidates the fast entirely. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition is not absolute for the one who has vowed; it is a prohibition of tanzih (dislike) that can be overridden by the need to fulfill a vow. The passage also distinguishes between a vow specifying the prohibited days (in which case the vow is valid with deficiency) and a general vow without specification (where the fast on those days is deficient and must be made up). This shows the Hanafi approach of istihsan, balancing the prohibition against the necessity of fulfilling the vow.

Key Terms
ایام تشریق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following Eid al-Adha (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) when fasting is prohibited.
تابع (پے در پے) (tutaba' / mutaba'ah): Consecutiveness in fasting; the requirement that the fasts be observed one after another without interruption.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed or invalid fast; here, the makeup of the prohibited days after the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person vows to fast a specific year (e.g., 1445 AH), what must he do regarding the days of Eid al-Fitr and Tashriq?
A) He must fast on them because the vow includes all days of the year.
B) He must break the fast on those days and make them up later consecutively.
C) The vow is invalid because it includes prohibited days.
D) He may choose to fast or not fast on those days.

Key Takeaway
When vowing a year's fast, prohibited days are included but must be broken and made up; the Hanafi school allows this by deeming the prohibition as tanzih overridden by the vow.

Sawm — Fasting

Vowing to Fast a Year: Ruling on Prohibited Days and the Dispute
Ruling on fasting Eid and Tashreeq days when vowing a year's fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vowing to fast a year that includes prohibited days and explain how it differs from the position of Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
A vow to fast a full year obligates making up prohibited days — the vow stands, but the fasts on those days are invalid and must be replaced.

This lesson examines a nuanced area of fasting vows: when someone vows to fast an entire year, what happens to the five days when fasting is prohibited (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and the three Tashreeq days)? The Hanafi school holds that the vow is valid and includes these days, but one must break fast on them and make them up later. This ruling contrasts with Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, who consider the vow invalid for those days. We will explore the reasoning behind each position and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenarios
The passage describes three distinct cases: (1) vowing a specific year, (2) vowing an unspecified year with the condition of consecutiveness, and (3) vowing an unspecified year without any condition. Note the different outcomes for each.
Focus on the conditions that trigger make-up obligations.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling for Each Scenario
For case (1) and (2): break fast on the five prohibited days and make them up later. For case (3): the five days' fasts are invalid, and a total of 35 make-up days are required (5 for prohibited + 30 for Ramadan).
The rule 'what is obligated perfectly cannot be performed deficiently' applies.
3
Analyze the Hadith Prohibition
The hadith 'Beware, do not fast on these days' is cited by the opponent. The Hanafis reconcile this by explaining that the prohibition does not invalidate the vow; rather, the vow makes those days subject to make-up.
The Hanafi response is elaborated in the first issue of the section.
4
Compare the Opposing View
Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that the vow is void for those days because the prohibition is absolute, so no make-up is required. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.

کی نذ کرنا ان پانچ ایام کے روزوں کی بھی نذر ہے اس لئے یہ پانچ ایام بھی سال میں داخل ہیں۔ اور اگر ان پانچ ایام میں بھی روزے رکھ لئے تو ادا ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ جیسے لازم کئے تھے ویسے ہی ادا کر لئے ہاں اس صورت میں اس شخص پر رمضان کی قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اس نذر سے رمضان کے اندر نذر کے روزے لازم نہ ہوں گے کیونکہ رمضان، غیر رمضان کے روزوں کی لیاقت نہیں رکھتا ہے۔ اور اگر سال متعین نہیں کیا بلکہ مطلقاً ایک سال کے روزوں کی نذر کی ہے تو اس کی بھی دوصورتیں ہیں یا تو تابع کی شرط ذکر کی ہوگی یا ذکر نہ کی ہوگی یعنی یا تو یوں کہا ہو گا کہ میں ایک سال کے روزے پے در پے رکھوں گا یا پے در پے کی شرط نہیں ذکر کی ہوگی اگر تابع کی شرط ذکر کی ہے تو اس کا حکم وہی ہو گا جو معین سال کا حکم ہے کیونکہ پے در پے ایک سال کے روزوں کی نذر کرنا ان ایام خمسہ سے خالی نہیں ہے لیکن اس صورت میں یہ بات ضروری ہے کہ ان پانچ روزوں کی قضا نذر کے روزوں سے متصلا ہی کرے یعنی جب سال پورا ہو تو اگلے ہی دن سے ان پانچ روزوں کی قضا نذر کے روزوں سے متصل ہی کرے یعنی جب سال پورا ہو تو اگلے ہی دن سے ان پانچ روزوں کی قضا کرے تا کہ بقدر امکان تابع اور تسلسل پایا جائے ان پانچ روزوں کی قضاء میں امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا اختلاف پیدا ہو گا یعنی ان دونوں حضرات کے نزدیک ان ایام خمسہ کی قضا واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ حدیث ألا لا تَصُومُوا الحدیث میں ان ایام خمسہ میں روزہ رکھنا ممنوع ہے لہذا ان ایام کی نذر ہی درست نہیں ہے اور جب نذر صحیح نہیں تو ان کی قضاء بھی واجب نہ ہوگی لیکن ہماری طرف سے ان ایام میں صحت نذر کی وجہ اور پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب فصل کے پہلے مسئلہ میں گذر چکا ہے ملاحظہ فرما ئیں ۔ اور اگر نہ تو سال کو متعین کیا ہے اور نہ تابع کو شرط قرار دیا ہے تو ان پانچ ایام میں روزہ رکھنا جائز نہ ہوگا یعنی ان ایام میں روزہ رکھنے سے نذر ادا نہ ہوگی بلکہ اس پر ۳۵ دن کے روزوں کی قضا کرنا واجب ہوگا پانچ تو ان ایام کے اور تمیں رمضان کے۔ ان ایام کے پانچ روزوں کی قضاء تو اس لئے واجب ہے کہ اس نے اپنے اوپر جوروزے لازم کئے ہیں ان میں اصیل یہ ہے کہ وہ کامل ہوں تو گویا اس پر کامل روزے واجب ہوئے ہیں اور ان ایام میں جو پانچ روزے رکھے ہیں وہ حدیث ہی کی وجہ سے ناقص ہیں اور قاعدہ ہے مَا وَجَبَ كَامِلا لَا يَتَاً دى ناقصا یعنی جو شئی علی سبیل الكمال واجب ہوئی ہو وہ ناقص ادا کرنے سے ادا نہ ہوگی پس جب ان ایام خمسہ میں کامل روزے ادا نہ ہوئے تو انکی قضاء واجب ہوگی اس کے برخلاف اگر اس نے سال متعین کر دیا ہو اور اس شخص نے ان ایام خمسہ میں بھی روزے رکھ ئے تو ادا ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ سال متعین کرنے کی وجہ سے ان پانچ ایام میں جو روزے لازم ہوئے ہیں وہ ناقص ہیں اور ناقص ہی اس نے ادا کر دیے اور قاعدہ ہے ماوجب ناقصاً جازان بتا دی ناقصا یعنی جو روزے ناقص واجب ہوئے ہیں تو ان کو ناقص ادا کرنا جائز ہے بہر حال رمضان کے تمیں روزوں کی قضاء اس لئے واجب ہے کہ جب سال متعین نہیں کیا تو مطلقا بارہ ماہ کے روزے لازم ہوئے اور ان بار و ماہ میں رمضان داخل نہیں کیونکہ رمضان کے دنوں میں غیر رمضان کے روزوں کی کوئی گنجائش نہیں ہے اس لئے نذر کے روزے بارہ ماہ کی مقدار کرنے کے لئے رمضان کے عوض ایک ماہ یعنی تمیں دن کے روزوں کی قضاء لا زم ہوگی۔
If [someone] vows to fast this year, he should not fast on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashreeq, and he should make them up. And if he says, 'For Allah, upon me is the fast of this year,' he breaks fast on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashreeq, and makes them up, because vowing a specific year includes vowing these days. Similarly, if he does not specify but stipulates consecutiveness, because consecutive days cannot be free from these days. But in this case he should make them up consecutively, to achieve consecutive order as much as possible. And in this there is a disagreement of Zufar and al-Shafi'i due to the prohibition of fasting on these days. It is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Beware, do not fast on these days, for they are days of eating, drinking, and conjugal relations.' And we have explained the reasoning and the excuse regarding it. And if he does not stipulate consecutive order, then fasting these days is not sufficient for him, because the original requirement in what he obligated is perfection, and what is performed is deficient due to the prohibition. Unlike the case where he specified them, because he obligated them with the attribute of deficiency, so the performance is with the attribute obligated. Explanation of the case: If a person makes up a year's fast, there are two scenarios: either he specified it, e.g., he said 'I will fast this year,' or he did not specify, e.g., he said 'I will fast a year.' If he makes up a specified year's fast, a year's fast is obligatory upon him, but he breaks fast on the day of Fitr, Nahr, and Tashreeq and makes them up later, because vowing a specified year includes vowing these five days. If he fasts on these five days, they will count, because he fulfilled as he obligated. However, in this case, making up Ramadan is not obligatory because the vow does not necessitate fasting the days of Ramadan, as Ramadan is not suitable for non-Ramadan fasts. And if the year is not specified but he absolutely vowed a year's fast, then there are two sub-cases: either he mentioned the condition of consecutiveness or not. If he mentioned the condition of consecutiveness, the ruling is the same as for a specified year, because vowing a consecutive year's fast cannot be free from these five days. But in this case, it is necessary that he makes up these five days consecutively from the next day after the year completes, so that consecutive order is achieved as much as possible. In making up these five days, there is disagreement of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i. In their view, making up these five days is not obligatory because fasting on these days is prohibited by the hadith 'Beware, do not fast...' so the vow is not valid, and if the vow is not valid, making up is not obligatory. But on our part, the reason for the validity of the vow and the answer to the hadith have passed in the first issue of the section. And if he neither specified the year nor stipulated consecutive order, then fasting on these five days is not permissible, i.e., the vow is not fulfilled by fasting them; rather, he must make up 35 days: five for these days and thirty for Ramadan. The making up of the five days is obligatory because what he obligated upon himself is originally perfection, so perfect fasts are obligatory, and the five fasts he performed are deficient due to the prohibition. The rule is: 'What is obligated perfectly cannot be performed deficiently.' So since perfect fasts were not performed on these five days, making them up is obligatory. In contrast, if he specified the year and fasted these five days, they count because he obligated them with the attribute of deficiency, and the rule is: 'What is obligated deficiently may be performed deficiently.' In any case, making up thirty days for Ramadan is obligatory because when he did not specify the year, an absolute twelve months of fasts are obligatory, and Ramadan is not included among them because Ramadan days cannot accommodate non-Ramadan fasts. Therefore, to complete the quantity of a year's fast, he must make up one month (thirty days) in place of Ramadan.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding the vow (nadhr) to fast an entire year. The author details the Hanafi position and the disagreement with Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i. The central issue is that when one vows to fast a whole year, the prohibited days (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and the three days of Tashreeq) are included in that year. According to Hanafis, the vow is valid and includes these days in the sense that one must break fast on them and make them up later. This is because the prohibition on fasting these days is abrogated in the context of a vow? Actually, the Hanafi position is that the prohibition is lifted when the vow is made, as per the principle that a vow to perform an act of worship overrides the general prohibition? The commentary explains that if the year is specified, the vow obligates fasting even on these five days, but since fasting them is prohibited, one must break fast and make them up. If the year is not specified but consecutive order is stipulated, the same applies. If neither specified nor stipulated, then the five days' fasts are not valid because the original obligation is for perfect fasts, and these are imperfect due to the prohibition, so they must be made up. Additionally, since the absolute year includes all twelve months, and Ramadan cannot be used for non-Ramadan fasts, one must make up 30 days for Ramadan. The disagreement with Zufar and al-Shafi'i is that they consider the vow to fast these prohibited days invalid altogether, so no make-up is required. The Hanafi response is based on the principle that the vow can be valid even for prohibited acts if the prohibition is not absolute? Actually, the commentary references earlier discussion for the full response.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship, here specifically fasting
تابع (tābi‘): Consecutiveness of fasting days, i.e., fasting one day after another without break
ایام تشریق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The three days following Eid al-Adha (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah)
قضاء (qaḍā’): Making up a missed fast after its due time

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone vows to fast a specific year without any additional conditions, what is the ruling when the day of Eid al-Adha arrives?
A) He must fast that day as part of the vow.
B) He must break fast on that day and make it up later.
C) The vow is automatically invalidated for that day.
D) He may choose to fast or not, as it is optional.

Key Takeaway
A vow to fast a full year includes the prohibited days; they must be broken and made up, and in some cases, additional make-up days for Ramadan apply.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
12 min
Vowing to Fast an Entire Year: Prohibited Days and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Rulings on nazr for a full year with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on vowing to fast a full year, including the treatment of the five prohibited days, and evaluate the disagreement with Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of the vow on those days.

Core Idea
A vow to fast a year includes prohibited days; the Hanafi school holds the vow valid and requires make-up despite the general prohibition.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a detailed scenario on nazr (vow) to fast an entire year. It explores multiple cases: when the year is specified, when it is unspecified with or without a condition of consecutiveness. A central dispute arises over the five days when fasting is prohibited (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and three days of Tashreeq). The Hanafi school maintains that the vow is valid on these days because the prohibition applies to voluntary fasts, not obligatory ones like nazr. Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i disagree, citing the general hadith prohibiting fasting on those days, and thus deem the vow invalid and qada unnecessary. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and practical consequences of each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three main scenarios
The passage discusses three cases: (1) a specified year is named (e.g., 'this year'), (2) an unspecified year with a condition of consecutiveness (taba'ah), (3) an unspecified year without consecutiveness. Identify the key difference in each scenario.
The specified year and unspecified-with-consecutiveness cases are treated similarly.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each scenario
For each scenario, determine the ruling on fasting the five prohibited days and whether qada is required. Use the two legal maxims (qawāʿid) cited in the passage: 'What is due as complete cannot be performed deficiently' and 'What is due as deficient may be performed deficiently'.
In scenario 1 & 2, the fasts on prohibited days are deficient from the start; if performed, they fulfill. In scenario 3, the fasts are due as complete, so deficient performance does not fulfill.
3
Present the opposing view (Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i)
The opposing school argues that the vow is invalid on prohibited days because of the hadith 'Do not fast on these days.' Since the vow is invalid, no qada is required. Understand their dalīl.
The hadith is general; the dispute is over whether it includes nazr.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between obligatory (wājib) and voluntary (nafl) fasts. The prohibition is for nafl; nazr makes fasting obligatory, so the vow is valid. The fasts on those days are deficient due to the prohibition, hence qada is required in scenario 3.
This response was already established earlier in the chapter according to the commentary.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilāf)
Compare the outcomes: Hanafis require qada for the five days (plus thirty for Ramadan in scenario 3); the opposing school requires no qada and considers the vow invalid from the start. Identify which position is muftā bihī.
The muftā bihī is the Hanafi position.

و
یمبین کا ارادہ تھا تو کفارہ یمین لازم ہے
قَالَ وَعَلَيْهِ كَفَّارَةُ يَمِين إِنْ أَرَادَ بِهِ يَمِينًا وَ قَدْ سَبَقَتْ وُجُوهُهُ
ترجمہ کہا کہ نذر کرنے والے پر کفارہ یمین واجب ہے اگر اس نے کلام سے نذر کا ارادہ کیا ہو اور اس کی صورتیں سابق میں گذر
چکی ہیں ۔
تشریح
iہے کہ جو کلام نذر کے لئے بولا گیا ہے اگر اس نے اس سے یمین کی نیت کی ہو تو حانث ہونے کی صورت میں اس پر
کفارہ یمین واجب ہو گا اور اس کی چھ صورتیں سابق میں گذر چکی ہیں۔
In this manner: he said 'I will fast this year' without specifying the year, for example he said 'I will fast for one year'. If he has made up the specified one year's fasts, then one year's fasts are not obligatory upon him, but he should break fast on the day of Fitr, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashreeq, and afterwards make them up, because vowing to fast a specified one year also includes vowing to fast those five days, so these five days are included in the year. And if he does fast on these five days, they will be fulfilled, because he fulfilled as he obligated. Yes, in this case qada of Ramadan is not obligatory upon him, because this vow does not obligate fasts of vow during Ramadan, for Ramadan is not fit for non-Ramadan fasts. And if he did not specify the year but vowed absolutely to fast a year, then there are two cases: either he mentioned the condition of consecutiveness or not, i.e., he said 'I will fast a year consecutively' or he did not mention consecutiveness. If he mentioned the condition of consecutiveness, then its ruling is the same as the specified year, because vowing to consecutively fast a year cannot be free of those five days. But in this case it is necessary that the qada of those five days be immediately after the vow's fasts, i.e., when the year is complete, from the very next day he should make up those five days, so that according to possibility, consecutiveness is found. In the qada of these five days, there is a difference between Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i — according to both of them, qada of these five days is not obligatory, because of the hadith 'Ala la tasumu' which prohibits fasting on these five days, so the vow for these days is not valid, and when the vow is not valid, their qada is also not obligatory. But our side (Hanafis) has already passed the reason for validity of vow on these days and the answer to the presented hadith in the first issue of the chapter; please refer. And if he neither specified the year nor stipulated consecutiveness, then fasting on these five days is not permissible, i.e., fasting on these days will not fulfill the vow, rather he must make up 35 days: five for these days and thirty for Ramadan. Qada of five days for these days is obligatory because the fasts he obligated upon himself are fundamentally complete, so complete fasts are due, and the five fasts he fasted on these days are deficient due to the hadith, and the rule is: 'What is due as complete cannot be performed deficiently' — so since complete fasts were not performed on these five days, their qada is obligatory. In contrast, if he specified the year and this person fasted on these five days, then they are fulfilled, because due to specifying the year, the fasts obligated on these five days are deficient, and he performed them as deficient, and the rule is: 'What is due as deficient may be performed deficiently'. In any case, qada of thirty days for Ramadan is obligatory, because when the year was not specified, twelve months of fasts are absolutely obligated, and Ramadan is not included in those twelve months, because during Ramadan there is no scope for non-Ramadan fasts. So to make up the measure of twelve months, in lieu of Ramadan, qada of one month i.e. thirty days is obligatory.
And if he intended a vow, then expiation of an oath is obligatory. He said: And upon him is expiation of an oath if he intended an oath by it, and its forms have preceded. Translation: He said that expiation of an oath is obligatory on the one vowing if he intended an oath by the speech, and its forms have passed earlier. Explanation: This is that the speech spoken for a vow, if he intended an oath by it, then upon breaking it, expiation of an oath is obligatory, and its six forms have passed earlier.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary on the rulings of nazr (vow) to fast for an entire year. The author explains several scenarios: First, if a person specifies a particular year and vows to fast it, the five prohibited days (Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and three days of Tashreeq) are included in the year. He must break fast on those days and make them up later because the vow covered them. If he does fast on those days, it is valid because his intent was the specified year. However, Ramadan is not included because one cannot fast non-Ramadan fasts during Ramadan. Second, if the year is unspecified but the vow includes a condition of consecutiveness (taba'ah), the ruling is the same as a specified year; he must break the prohibited days and make them up consecutively after the year. There is a disagreement with Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, who hold that the vow on prohibited days is invalid due to the prohibition (hadith), so no qada is required. The Hanafi position, already established earlier in the chapter, is that the vow is valid because the prohibition is for nafl, not for obligatory fasts like nazr. Third, if the year is unspecified and no condition of consecutiveness is made, then fasting on the prohibited days does not fulfill the vow; he must make up five days for those plus thirty for Ramadan, totaling 35 days. The reasoning uses two qawa'id: 'What is due as complete cannot be performed deficiently' and 'What is due as deficient may be performed deficiently'. The passage also briefly mentions that if the wording of the vow was intended as an oath (yamin), then upon breaking it, kaffarah yamin is due, and the six forms have been discussed earlier.

Key Terms
نذر (nazr): A vow to perform an act of worship that is not obligatory, making it binding upon oneself.
تابع (taba'ah): Consecutiveness; the condition of fasting days consecutively without interruption.
قاعدة (qa'idah): A legal maxim. Here: 'What is due as complete cannot be performed deficiently' and its counterpart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person vows to fast a year without specifying and without mentioning consecutiveness. He fasts on the day of Eid al-Adha. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The fast is valid, and he does not need to make it up.
B) The fast is invalid, and the vow itself is invalid for that day.
C) The fast does not fulfill the vow; he must make up that day plus thirty days for Ramadan.
D) He must break the fast immediately and make it up later.

Key Takeaway
A vow to fast a full year includes the prohibited days; the Hanafi school upholds the vow's validity and requires qada in the unspecified case, using the legal maxims to differentiate between complete and deficient obligations.

Fasting on the Day of Nahr: Is Qada Required if Broken?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada after breaking a prohibited fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on breaking a fast on a prohibited day and explain the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding qada.

Core Idea
Starting a fast on a prohibited day makes you a sinner; breaking it requires no qada in the relied-upon view.

Imagine you begin fasting on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, a day when fasting is strictly prohibited. Then you break your fast. Is it necessary to make up that day? This seems like a logical question, but the Hanafi school has an internal disagreement rooted in the nature of shuru' (beginning) and its legal effects. The passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents this dispute and resolves it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that fasting on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) is haram. The passage says 'he began the day of Nahr as a fasting person' – this is a prohibited act from the outset.
The prohibition is established by consensus; the issue is what happens after starting such a fast.
2
State the dispute and Zahir al-Riwayah position
The passage states that according to Zahir al-Riwayah (Abu Hanifa), nothing is due upon the person – no qada. The reasoning: by merely beginning the fast, the person is immediately called a 'fasting person' and thus becomes a violator of the prohibition, so nullification is obligatory and preservation is not needed.
Note the key phrase: 'بِنَفْسِ الشُّرُوعِ فِى الصَّوْمِ يُسَمَّى صَائِمًا' – by the mere beginning of fast, he is named a fasting person.
3
Present the Nawadir position and its basis
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in al-Nawadir hold that qada is obligatory. Their dalil: starting a voluntary fast makes it binding like a vow (nazr), and they analogize it to beginning prayer in a disliked time, where breaking it requires qada.
The Sahibayn's view is recorded in Nawadir, which is a secondary source.
4
Analyze the farq (distinction) between fasting and prayer
Abu Hanifa's distinction: In fasting, one is legally considered a fasting person immediately upon intention and is thus a violator. In prayer, one is not considered a 'praying person' until completing one rak'ah, so no immediate violation occurs—preservation of the prayer is possible, hence qada is required if broken.
This is the core of the talil (reasoning). The passage also notes that Abu Hanifa says no qada even in the prayer case, but the first view is more apparent.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its implication
The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah states 'al-azhar huwa al-awwal' – the more apparent is the first view (no qada). Thus, the relied-upon position for fatwa is that no qada is required for breaking a fast on a prohibited day.
The thamarah al-khilaf: practically, the Sahibayn's view would require a makeup day; Abu Hanifa's view does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَصْبَحَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ صَائِمًا ثُمَّ أَفَطَرَ لَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَةٍ فِي التَّوَادِرٍ أَنَّ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءِ لِأَنَّ الشُّرُوعَ مُنْزِمُ كَالنَّدَرِ وَصَارَ كَالشُّرُوعِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ فِي الْوَقْتِ الْمَكْرُوهِ وَالْفَرْقِ لِأُ بِي حَنِيفَةَ وَهُوَ ظَاهِرُ الروايةِ أَنَّ بَنَفْسِ الشُّرُوعِ فِى الصَّوْمِ يُسَمَّى صَائِمًا حَتَّى يَحْنَتَ بِهِ الْخَالِفُ عَلَى الصَّوْمِ فَيصِيرُ مُرْتَكِبًا لِلنَّهَى فَيَجِبُ إِبْطَالُهُ فَلَا تَجِبُ صِيَانَتُهُ وَوُجُوبُ الْقَضَاءِ يُبْتَنى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يَصِيرُ مُرْتَكِبًا لِلَّهِي بِنَفْسِ النَّدْرِ وَهُوَ الْمُوجِبُ وَلاَ بِنَفْسِ الشَّرُوعِ فِى الصَّلَاةِ حَتَّى يُتِمَّ رَكْعَةً وَلِهَذَا لَا يَحْنَتْ بِهِ الْحَالِفُ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَتَجِبُ صِيَانَةِ الْمُؤَدَّى وَيَكُونُ مَضْمُونَا بِالْقَضَاءِ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَحِبُّ الْقَضَاء فِى فَصْلِ الصَّلَاةِ أَيْضًا وَالْأَطْهَرُ هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ وَاللهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَابِ
He began the day of Nahr as a fasting person then broke it: nothing is due upon him. And from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in al-Nawadir that qada is due upon him, because beginning (shuru') is binding (munzamm) like a vow, and it becomes like beginning prayer in a disliked time. And the distinction for Abu Hanifa, and it is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), is that by the mere beginning of fast, he is called a fasting person such that one who takes an oath to not fast becomes a breaker (hanith) by it, so he becomes a committer of the prohibition, thus its nullification is obligatory, so its preservation is not obligatory, and the obligation of qada is built upon that. And he does not become a committer of the prohibition by the mere vow, which is the obligator, nor by the mere beginning of prayer until he completes a rak'ah, and for this reason the one who takes an oath to not pray does not break the oath by it. So preservation of the performed act is obligatory, and it becomes guaranteed by qada. And from Abu Hanifa that qada is not obligatory in the case of prayer as well, and the more apparent is the first. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who begins a fast on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), which is one of the prohibited days for fasting, and then breaks it. According to Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon narrations of Imam Muhammad), no qada is required. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The reasoning: by merely intending and beginning the fast, one is considered a fasting person (so that if someone had taken an oath not to fast, he would break that oath). Consequently, he becomes a violator of the prohibition (since fasting on this day is haram), so it becomes obligatory to nullify the fast, and preservation of such a fast is not required. Therefore, no qada is due because the act itself is invalid from the start. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), in a narration from al-Nawadir, hold that qada is obligatory because beginning a voluntary fast makes it binding (like a vow), and breaking it requires compensation. They analogize it to beginning prayer in a disliked time, where if one breaks it, qada is due. Abu Hanifa distinguishes by noting that in prayer, one is not considered a 'praying person' until completing one rak'ah, so no violation occurs immediately; thus preservation is required. Imam Abu Hanifa also reportedly said that qada is not obligatory in the prayer case either, but the more apparent position is the first one (no qada for fast on prohibited day). The relied-upon position for fatwa is thus that no qada is due.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known and authoritative narrations transmitted by Imam Muhammad from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
شروع (shuru'): The act of beginning or entering into a devotional act, like fasting or prayer.
حانث (hanith): One who breaks an oath (yamin) by doing the sworn-against act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, if someone begins fasting on the Day of Nahr and then breaks it, what is the ruling?
A) He must complete the fast.
B) He must make up (qada) the fast later.
C) Nothing is due upon him; no qada.
D) He must pay kaffarah (expiation).

Key Takeaway
When a fast is begun on a prohibited day, breaking it does not necessitate qada because the act itself is invalid and preservation is not required.

Qada for Breaking Voluntary Fast on Yawm al-Nahr: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada for breaking voluntary fast on Yawm al-Nahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that no qada is required for breaking a voluntary fast on Yawm al-Nahr and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-argument.

Core Idea
If an act is prohibited from the start, its annulment is required, not its completion—hence no qada.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the obligation of qada (makeup) when a voluntary fast is broken on Yawm al-Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah). Imam Abu Hanifa's position in Zahir al-Riwayah is that no qada is required, while Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) report in al-Nawadir that qada is obligatory. The source passage presents the reasoning behind each view, centering on the legal distinction between acts that immediately constitute a prohibited violation and those that only become prohibited after a minimal portion is performed. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of qada for voluntary acts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa from Zahir al-Riwayah: if one starts a voluntary fast on Yawm al-Nahr and breaks it, nothing is required (no qada).
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) narrate in al-Nawadir that qada is obligatory. Note that this is a legitimate but less authoritative opinion.
Al-Nawadir contains rare transmissions.
3
Follow the opposing proof
Trace the Sahibayn's reasoning: commencing a voluntary fast makes it binding (lazim) like a vow, so invalidating it requires qada. They analogize to starting a voluntary prayer in a disliked time.
The analogy is based on the idea that commencement creates a binding obligation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine Abu Hanifa's distinction: for fasting, by merely starting, one is immediately called a fasting person (sa'im), thus the prohibition is violated at once. Annulment (ibṭāl) of the prohibited act is required, not preservation. Qada is built on the obligation to complete; here completion is not required, so qada is not required. For prayer, one is not called a praying person until one rak'ah is complete, so if invalidated before that, preservation is required and qada is necessary.
The key difference is the immediacy of the designation 'fasting person' vs. 'praying person'.
5
Determine the thamarah and tarjih
The practical consequence: with no qada required, the person simply breaks the fast without further obligation. The text declares Abu Hanifa's view as azhar (more apparent) and it is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah, so it is the mufta bihi.
Tamarah al-khilaf: the actual difference in ruling for the individual.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ کہا کہ نذر کرنے والے پر کفارہ یمین واجب ہے اگر اس نے کلام سے نذر کا ارادہ کیا ہو اور اس کی صورتیں سابق میں گذر چکی ہیں ۔

أَصْبَحَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ صَائِمًا ثُمَّ أَفَطَرَ لَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَةٍ فِي التَّوَادِرٍ أَنَّ عَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءِ لِأَنَّ الشُّرُوعَ مُنْزِمُ كَالنَّدَرِ وَصَارَ كَالشُّرُوعِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ فِي الْوَقْتِ الْمَكْرُوهِ وَالْفَرْقِ لِأُ بِي حَنِيفَةَ وَهُوَ ظَاهِرُ الروايةِ أَنَّ بَنَفْسِ الشُّرُوعِ فِى الصَّوْمِ يُسَمَّى صَائِمًا حَتَّى يَحْنَتَ بِهِ الْخَالِفُ عَلَى الصَّوْمِ فَيصِيرُ مُرْتَكِبًا لِلنَّهَى فَيَجِبُ إِبْطَالُهُ فَلَا تَجِبُ صِيَانَتُهُ وَوُجُوبُ الْقَضَاءِ يُبْتَنى عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يَصِيرُ مُرْتَكِبًا لِلَّهِي بِنَفْسِ النَّدْرِ وَهُوَ الْمُوجِبُ وَلاَ بِنَفْسِ الشَّرُوعِ فِى الصَّلَاةِ حَتَّى يُتِمَّ رَكْعَةً وَلِهَذَا لَا يَحْنَتْ بِهِ الْحَالِفُ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَتَجِبُ صِيَانَةِ الْمُؤَدَّى وَيَكُونُ مَضْمُونَا بِالْقَضَاءِ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَحِبُّ الْقَضَاء فِى فَصْلِ الصَّلَاةِ أَيْضًا وَالْأَطْهَرُ هُوَ الْأَوَّلُ وَاللهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَابِ
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے یوم نحر میں روزہ دار ہو کر صبح کی پھر افطار کر لیا تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے اور امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد سے نوادر میں مروی ہے کہ اس پر قضاء واجب ہے کیونکہ روزہ شروع کرنا نذر کی طرح اس کے ذمہ لازم کرنے والا ہے اور نیا ایسا ہو گیا جیسے مکروہ وقت میں نماز شروع کرنا اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وجہ فرق اور یہیں ظاہر الروایہ ہے یہ ہے کہ روزہ کو شروع کرتے ہی اس کو روزہ دار کہا جاتا ہے حتی کہ اس سے روزہ نہ رکھنے کی قسم کھانے والا حانث ہو جائے گا تو شروع کرنے سے نبی کا مرتکب ہوا اس لئے اس کو باطل کرنا واجب ہوگا پس اس کی حفاظت واجب نہیں ہے اور وجوب قضاء اس پر مبنی ہے اور نفس نذر کی وجہ سے نہی کا مرتکب نہیں ہوتا اور نڈر ہی واجب کرنے والی ہے اور نہ نماز کے نفس شروع سے (نہی کا مرتکب ہوتا یہاں تک کہ ایک رکعت پوری کرلے اور اسی وجہ سے اس سے نماز قسم کھانے والا حانث نہ ہوگا پس سے روایت ہے کہ نماز کی کی حفاظت واجب ہے اور وہ قضاء کرنے کا ضامن ہوگا اور ابو حنی صورت میں بھی قضا ، واجب نہیں ہے اور اول اظہر ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ایام منہی عنہا میں سے کسی دن روزہ کی نیت کر کے روز ہ شروع کیا پھر اس کو فاسد کر دیا تو اس پر اس روزہ کی قضا واجب نہیں ہے یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے اور صاحبین سے نوارد کی روایت یہ ہے کہ اس پر قضاء واجب ہے۔ صاحبین کی دبیل یہ ہے کہ نفلی روزہ شروع کرنے سے لازم ہو جاتا ہے پس جب شروع کرنے سے لازم ہو گیا تو فاسد کرنے کی صورت میں اس کی قضا و لا زم ہوگی جیسے کسی نے ایام منہبیہ کے کسی روزہ کی نذر کی تو یہ روزہ اس دن کے علاوہ میں واجب ہو جائے گا اور جیسے کسی نے وقت مکروہ میں نفل نماز شروع کر کے فاسد کر دی تو اس پر اس نماز کی قضاء واجب ہو جائے گی اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے مذہب کے مطابق یوم نحر کے روزے کی نذر اور یوم نحر میں روزہ شروع کرنے کے درمیان اور یوم نحر میں روزہ شروع کرنے اور اوقات مکروہہ میں نماز شروع کرنے کے درمیان وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ روزہ شروع کرتے ہی آدمی صائم کہلاتا ہے حتی کہ اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں نفلی روزہ نہیں رکھوں گا پھر اس نے یوم نحر میں روزہ کی نیت سے روزہ شروع کر دیا تو شروع کرتے ہی حانث ہو جائے گا پس معلوم ہوا کہ یوم نحر میں جوں ہی اس نے روزہ شروع کہا از وہ صائم روز و ر کھنے والا ہو گیا اور یہ معلوم ہی ہے کہ یوم نحر ان پانچ ایام میں سے ایک ہے جن میں روزہ رکھنے کی ممانعت کی گئی ہے پس یوم تحر میں روزہ شروع کرتے ہی یہ شخص فعل منہی عنہ کا مرتکب ہو گیا ہے اور چونکہ فعل منہی عنہ کا ابطال واجب ہے اس لئے اس روزہ کا اتمام اور اسکی حفاظت واجب نہ ہوگی اور جب اس روزہ کا اتمام اور پورا کرنا واجب نہ رہا تو اس کی قضاء بھی واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ وجوب قضا روجوب اتمام پر بنی ہوتا ہے یعنی جس چیز کا اتمام واجب ہے فاسد کر دینے سے اس کی قضاء واجب ہو گی اور جس کا اتمام واجب نہیں اس کو اگر فاسد کر دیا جائے تو اس کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی پس ثابت ہوا کہ یوم نحر میں نفلی روزہ شروع کرنے کے بعد اگر فاسد کر دیا گیا تو اس کی قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی اور رہا یوم نحر کے روزے کی نذر کرنا تو نفس مذر سے فعل منہی عنہ کا مرتکب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یوم نحر میں روزہ رکھنا ممنوع ہے روزہ کی نذر کرنا ممنوع نہیں ہے اور یہ بھی مسلم ہے کہ نذر کے روزے کو واجب کرنے والی نذر ہے پس موجب صوم نذر ہے اور نفس نذار ے فعل منہی عنہ کا ارتکاب کرنا لازم نہیں آتا تو اس نذر کو پورا کرنا واجب ہے مگر چونکہ یوم نحر میں روزہ رکھنا گناہ ہے اس لئے اس نذر کے روزے کو کسی دوسرے دن ادا کرے۔
اسی طرح اوقات مکروہہ میں نماز شروع کر کے فاسد کر دینے کی صورت میں بھی قضاء واجب ہے کیونکہ نماز شروع کرتے ہی اس کو نمازی نہیں کہا جاتا بلکہ نماز کا اطلاق اس وقت ہوگا جبکہ ایک رکعت پوری ہو جائے یعنی ایک رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کر دیا ہو یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کہا کہ میں نفل نماز نہیں پڑھوں گا پھر اس نے نفل نماز کو شروع کیا تو محض شروع کرنے سے حانث نہ ہوگا پس جب وقت مکروہ میں نفل شروع کیا اور ابھی رکوع سجدہ نہیں کیا تو یہ نماز نہ کہلائے گی اور جب اس پر نماز کا اطلاق نہ ہوا تو اس وقت مکروہ فعل منیبی عنہ کا مرتکب بھی نہ ہوا اور جب فعل منہی عنہ کا مرتکب نہ ہوا تو مودی (یعنی جو حصہ ادا کیا گیا) کی حفاظت واجب ہے اور چونکہ جس کی حفاظت اور اتمام واجب ہوتا ہے فاسد کر دینے سے اس کی قضاء واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس مؤدی کو اگر فاسد کر دیا تو اس کی قضاء واجب ہوگی اس تقریر سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر وقت مکروہ میں نفل نماز شروع کی اور ایک رکعت پوری کرنے کے بعد یعنی سجدہ کرنے کے بعد اس کو فاسد کر دیا تو اس کی قضاء واجب نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ ایک رکعت پوری ہونے کے بعد اس پر نماز کا اطلاق ہو جائے گا اور اس وقت مکروہ میں نما جز پڑھنا ممنوع ہے تو اس کا ابطال واجب ہوا اور جس کا ابطال واجب ہو فاسد کرنے سے اس کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اس صورت میں قضا واجب نہ ہوگی ۔
حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ اوقات مکروہہ میں نماز نفل شروع کر کے فاسد کر دینے کی صورت میں بھی قضا ، واجب نہ ہوگی لیکن امام صاحب کا قول اول زیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب جمیل احمد عفی عنہ۔
He said: And upon him is the expiation of an oath if he intended by it an oath, and its forms have preceded. Translation: He said that upon the one who makes a vow, the expiation of an oath is obligatory if he intended by the speech a vow, and its forms have passed earlier. Explanation: That is, the speech spoken for a vow, if he intended by it an oath, then upon breaking it, the expiation of an oath is obligatory, and its six forms have passed. One who became a fasting person on the morning of the Day of Nahr then broke his fast: nothing is upon him. And from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in al-Nawadir: that upon him is qada, because commencing makes it binding like a vow, and it becomes like commencing prayer in the disliked time. And the distinction for Abu Hanifa, and it is the apparent (zahir) of the riwayah: that by the mere commencement of fasting, one is called a fasting person, such that the one who swears against fasting becomes a breaker of the oath by it, so he becomes a committer of the prohibition, so its annulment becomes obligatory, so its preservation is not obligatory, and the obligation of qada is built upon it. And one does not become a committer of the prohibition by the mere vow, and it is the obligator, nor by the mere commencement of prayer until one completes a rak'ah, and for this reason the one who swears concerning prayer does not break the oath by it, so preservation of what is performed becomes obligatory, and it is guaranteed by qada. And from Abu Hanifa that qada is not obligatory in the case of prayer as well, and the first is more apparent. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The form of the issue is that if someone intended a fast on one of the prohibited days and started it, then invalidated it, then qada is not obligatory upon him; this is Zahir al-Riwayah. And from the Sahibayn in al-Nawadir: that qada is obligatory. Their evidence is that a voluntary fast becomes binding by commencing; so when it becomes binding by commencing, then in case of invalidation, its qada becomes obligatory, like if one vowed a fast on a prohibited day, that fast becomes obligatory on another day, and like if one started a voluntary prayer in a disliked time and invalidated it, then qada becomes obligatory. And according to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, the distinction between the vow of a fast on Yawm al-Nahr and commencing a fast on Yawm al-Nahr, and between commencing a fast on Yawm al-Nahr and commencing prayer in disliked times, is that upon commencing the fast, one is immediately called a fasting person, such that if one swore 'I will not fast a voluntary fast' and then started a fast on Yawm al-Nahr, he becomes a breaker of the oath immediately. So it is known that as soon as he started the fast, he became a fasting person. And it is known that Yawm al-Nahr is one of the five days in which fasting is prohibited. So upon commencing the fast on Yawm al-Nahr, this person has committed a prohibited act. And since annulment of a prohibited act is obligatory, therefore completing and preserving this fast is not obligatory. And if completing is not obligatory, then qada is not obligatory, because the obligation of qada is built upon the obligation of completion. So it is established that if a voluntary fast on Yawm al-Nahr is invalidated after starting, qada is not obligatory. As for vowing a fast on Yawm al-Nahr, by the mere vow one does not commit a prohibited act, because fasting on Yawm al-Nahr is prohibited, but vowing a fast is not prohibited. And it is also accepted that what makes the vowed fast obligatory is the vow. So the obligator is the vow, and by the mere vow, committing a prohibited act does not necessarily follow, so fulfilling that vow is obligatory. But since fasting on Yawm al-Nahr is a sin, he should fulfill that vowed fast on another day. Similarly, in the case of starting prayer in a disliked time and invalidating it, qada is obligatory, because upon commencing prayer, one is not called a praying person; rather the term 'prayer' applies when one complete rak'ah is completed, i.e., when one has performed a rak'ah with sajdah. This is why if someone said 'I will not pray a voluntary prayer' and then started a voluntary prayer, merely starting does not make him a breaker of the oath. So when he started a voluntary prayer in a disliked time and has not yet done ruku' and sujud, it is not called prayer, and when the term 'prayer' does not apply, then he has not committed a prohibited act. And when he has not committed a prohibited act, preservation of what was performed (al-mu'adda) is obligatory. And since preservation and completion are obligatory, if he invalidates it, qada becomes obligatory. From this exposition it is known that if one started a voluntary prayer in a disliked time and invalidated it after completing one rak'ah, i.e., after sajdah, then qada is not obligatory, because after completing one rak'ah the term 'prayer' applies, and praying in that disliked time is prohibited, so its annulment becomes obligatory, and when annulment is obligatory, invalidating it does not make qada obligatory. So in this case, qada is not obligatory. There is a riwayah from Imam Abu Hanifa that even in the case of starting voluntary prayer in a disliked time and invalidating it, qada is not obligatory, but the first saying of Imam Sahib is more apparent. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad 'Anhu.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on breaking a voluntary fast on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The core issue is whether qada (makeup) is required when one starts a voluntary fast on a prohibited day and then invalidates it. The passage begins by stating the ruling: if one becomes a fasting person on the morning of Yawm al-Nahr and then breaks the fast, nothing is obligatory upon him. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and is considered Zahir al-Riwayah. However, there is a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad in al-Nawadir that qada is obligatory. Their reasoning (dalil) is that commencing a voluntary fast makes it binding (lazim), similar to a vow; therefore, when invalidated, qada becomes necessary. They analogize this to commencing a voluntary prayer in a disliked time; if one invalidates it, qada is required. Abu Hanifa responds with a detailed distinction (farq). For fasting, the moment one intends and begins the fast, one is immediately called a 'fasting person' (sa'im). This is evidenced by the fact that if someone swore not to fast and then started a voluntary fast, he would break the oath immediately. Since Yawm al-Nahr is a day when fasting is prohibited, starting the fast constitutes committing a prohibited act. When an act is prohibited, its annulment (ibṭāl) is obligatory, not its preservation or completion. Therefore, since completion is not required, qada (which is built upon the obligation of completion) is also not required. For the vow of fasting on Yawm al-Nahr, the vow itself is not prohibited; what is prohibited is actually fasting on that day. So the vow creates an obligation, but since the day is prohibited, the person must fulfill the fast on another day. For prayer, the distinction is that one is not called a 'praying person' merely by starting; rather, the term 'prayer' applies only after completing one rak'ah (including sajdah). Therefore, if one starts a voluntary prayer in a disliked time but invalidates it before completing one rak'ah, no prohibited act has been fully committed, so preservation of the act is required, and qada becomes obligatory. If one completes one rak'ah and then invalidates, then the prayer has been fully termed, and the prohibition applies; thus annulment (not preservation) is required, and qada is not obligatory. The passage ends by noting a riwayah from Abu Hanifa that even for prayer, qada is not required, but the first position (that qada is required when invalidated before one rak'ah) is considered more apparent (azhar).

Key Terms
یوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The Day of Slaughter, i.e., the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, one of the five days in which fasting is prohibited.
قضاء (qadaʾ): Making up a missed or invalidated obligatory act of worship after its prescribed time.
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known, transmitted rulings from Imam Abu Hanifa through his students, primarily found in the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa's position in Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling if someone starts a voluntary fast on Yawm al-Nahr and then breaks it?
A) He must make qada because the fast became binding upon commencement.
B) He must make qada only if he intended a vow.
C) He does not need to make qada because the fast was prohibited and its annulment was required.
D) He must give kaffarah (expiation) and make qada.

Key Takeaway
When a voluntary act is started on a prohibited day or time, the obligation of qada depends on whether the act is immediately deemed prohibited or only after a minimum portion; for fasting, mere commencement triggers the prohibition, so annulment is required, not qada.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Qada for Invalidated Nafl Acts in Prohibited Times
Explains qada ruling for nafl fast on Yawm al-Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when qada is and is not wajib for a nafl act started in a prohibited time, and apply the Hanafi criterion of obligation of completion.

Core Idea
Qada depends on whether completion was wajib – forbidden acts need not be completed.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi ruling: if you start a nafl act (fast or prayer) in a prohibited time and then invalidate it, does it require qada? The answer depends on when the act becomes a 'forbidden act.' For a fast on Yawm al-Nahr, you become a fasting person immediately, making it a forbidden act – so completion and qada are not obligatory. For a prayer in makruh time, you are not a 'praying person' until one rak'ah is complete; before that, it is not a forbidden act, so qada is wajib. After one rak'ah, it becomes a forbidden act and qada is not wajib. We will also explore a minority narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that differs on the prayer case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its time
Determine the specific nafl act (fast or prayer) and whether the time is prohibited or makruh. The text focuses on Yawm al-Nahr for fast and makruh times for prayer.
Yawm al-Nahr is one of five days when fasting is haram.
2
Assess when the act becomes a 'forbidden act'
Analyze at what point the act acquires the ruling of being a forbidden act (fi'l manhi 'anhu). For fast: immediately upon intention. For prayer: only after completing one rak'ah.
This is the key distinction in the Hanafi argument.
3
Apply the rule: completion wajib only if act is not forbidden
If the act is a forbidden act from the start, completion is not wajib; if it is not yet a forbidden act, completion is wajib.
The text uses an oath example to prove the fast's immediate effect.
4
Derive qada obligation from completion obligation
Qada is wajib only if completion was wajib. If completion was not wajib, qada is not wajib.
This is the core principle: qada follows completion obligation.
5
Consider the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa's first opinion (the mufta bihi) holds qada wajib for prayer before one rak'ah; a narration from him says it is not wajib. The author prefers the first.
The practical difference: whether to make up the prayer or not.

کتاب الصوم
قضا و لا زم ہوگی جیسے کسی نے ایام منہبیہ کے کسی روزہ کی نذر کی تو یہ روزہ اس دن کے علاوہ میں واجب ہو جائے گا اور جیسے کسی نے وقت مکروہ میں نفل نماز شروع کر کے فاسد کر دی تو اس پر اس نماز کی قضاء واجب ہو جائے گی اور امام ابوحنیفہ کے مذہب کے مطابق یوم نحر کے روزے کی نذر اور یوم نحر میں روزہ شروع کرنے کے درمیان اور یوم نحر میں روزہ شروع کرنے اور اوقات مکروہہ میں نماز شروع کرنے کے درمیان وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ روزہ شروع کرتے ہی آدمی صائم کہلاتا ہے حتی کہ اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں نفلی روزہ نہیں رکھوں گا پھر اس نے یوم نحر میں روزہ کی نیت سے روزہ شروع کر دیا تو شروع کرتے ہی حانث ہو جائے گا پس معلوم ہوا کہ یوم نحر میں جوں ہی اس نے روزہ شروع کہا از وہ صائم روز و ر کھنے والا ہو گیا اور یہ معلوم ہی ہے کہ یوم نحر ان پانچ ایام میں سے ایک ہے جن میں روزہ رکھنے کی ممانعت کی گئی ہے پس یوم تحر میں روزہ شروع کرتے ہی یہ شخص فعل منہی عنہ کا مرتکب ہو گیا ہے اور چونکہ فعل منہی عنہ کا ابطال واجب ہے اس لئے اس روزہ کا اتمام اور اسکی حفاظت واجب نہ ہوگی اور جب اس روزہ کا اتمام اور پورا کرنا واجب نہ رہا تو اس کی قضاء بھی واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ وجوب قضا روجوب اتمام پر بنی ہوتا ہے یعنی جس چیز کا اتمام واجب ہے فاسد کر دینے سے اس کی قضاء واجب ہو گی اور جس کا اتمام واجب نہیں اس کو اگر فاسد کر دیا جائے تو اس کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی پس ثابت ہوا کہ یوم نحر میں نفلی روزہ شروع کرنے کے بعد اگر فاسد کر دیا گیا تو اس کی قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی اور رہا یوم نحر کے روزے کی نذر کرنا تو نفس مذر سے فعل منہی عنہ کا مرتکب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یوم نحر میں روزہ رکھنا ممنوع ہے روزہ کی نذر کرنا ممنوع نہیں ہے اور یہ بھی مسلم ہے کہ نذر کے روزے کو واجب کرنے والی نذر ہے پس موجب صوم نذر ہے اور نفس نذار ے فعل منہی عنہ کا ارتکاب کرنا لازم نہیں آتا تو اس نذر کو پورا کرنا واجب ہے مگر چونکہ یوم نحر میں روزہ رکھنا گناہ ہے اس لئے اس نذر کے روزے کو کسی دوسرے دن ادا کرے۔
اسی طرح اوقات مکروہہ میں نماز شروع کر کے فاسد کر دینے کی صورت میں بھی قضاء واجب ہے کیونکہ نماز شروع کرتے ہی اس کو نمازی نہیں کہا جاتا بلکہ نماز کا اطلاق اس وقت ہوگا جبکہ ایک رکعت پوری ہو جائے یعنی ایک رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کر دیا ہو یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کہا کہ میں نفل نماز نہیں پڑھوں گا پھر اس نے نفل نماز کو شروع کیا تو محض شروع کرنے سے حانث نہ ہوگا پس جب وقت مکروہ میں نفل شروع کیا اور ابھی رکوع سجدہ نہیں کیا تو یہ نماز نہ کہلائے گی اور جب اس پر نماز کا اطلاق نہ ہوا تو اس وقت مکروہ فعل منیبی عنہ کا مرتکب بھی نہ ہوا اور جب فعل منہی عنہ کا مرتکب نہ ہوا تو مودی (یعنی جو حصہ ادا کیا گیا) کی حفاظت واجب ہے اور چونکہ جس کی حفاظت اور اتمام واجب ہوتا ہے فاسد کر دینے سے اس کی قضاء واجب ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس مؤدی کو اگر فاسد کر دیا تو اس کی قضاء واجب ہوگی اس تقریر سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر وقت مکروہ میں نفل نماز شروع کی اور ایک رکعت پوری کرنے کے بعد یعنی سجدہ کرنے کے بعد اس کو فاسد کر دیا تو اس کی قضاء واجب نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ ایک رکعت پوری ہونے کے بعد اس پر نماز کا اطلاق ہو جائے گا اور اس وقت مکروہ میں نما جز پڑھنا ممنوع ہے تو اس کا ابطال واجب ہوا اور جس کا ابطال واجب ہو فاسد کرنے سے اس کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اس صورت میں قضا واجب نہ ہوگی ۔
حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ اوقات مکروہہ میں نماز نفل شروع کر کے فاسد کر دینے کی صورت میں بھی قضا ، واجب نہ ہوگی لیکن امام صاحب کا قول اول زیادہ ظاہر ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب جمیل احمد عفی عنہ۔
Book of Fasting: Qada will be obligatory, like if someone vowed a fast on the days of prohibition, that fast will become obligatory on another day. And like if someone started a nafl prayer in a makruh time and then invalidated it, qada of that prayer will be obligatory. According to Imam Abu Hanifa's madhhab, the difference between vowing a fast on Yawm al-Nahr and starting a fast on Yawm al-Nahr, and between starting a fast on Yawm al-Nahr and starting a prayer in makruh times, is that as soon as one starts a fast, he is called a fasting person. So much so that if someone swore that he would not observe a nafl fast, and then started a fast with the intention of fasting on Yawm al-Nahr, he becomes a breaker of his oath immediately. So it is known that as soon as he started the fast on Yawm al-Nahr, he became one who is fasting. And it is known that Yawm al-Nahr is one of the five days on which fasting is prohibited. So by starting a fast on Yawm al-Nahr, this person has committed a forbidden act. Since it is obligatory to abandon a forbidden act, completing and preserving this fast is not obligatory. And when completing and preserving this fast is not obligatory, qada is also not obligatory, because the obligation of qada is based on the obligation of completion: that is, if completion of something is obligatory and it is invalidated, qada becomes obligatory; if completion is not obligatory and it is invalidated, qada is not obligatory. So it is established that if a nafl fast started on Yawm al-Nahr is invalidated, qada is not obligatory. As for vowing to fast on Yawm al-Nahr, the very act of vowing does not entail committing a forbidden act, because fasting on Yawm al-Nahr is prohibited, but vowing a fast is not prohibited. And it is established that the vow makes the fast obligatory, so the cause of obligation is the vow, and the vow itself does not necessitate committing a forbidden act. Thus fulfilling this vow is obligatory, but since fasting on Yawm al-Nahr is sinful, he should fulfill that vowed fast on another day.
Similarly, in the case of starting a prayer in a makruh time and then invalidating it, qada is obligatory, because immediately upon starting the prayer he is not called a praying person; rather, the term prayer applies only when one complete rak'ah is performed, i.e., one rak'ah with its sajdah. This is why if someone said, 'I will not pray a nafl prayer,' and then started a nafl prayer, he does not break his oath merely by starting. So if he started a nafl prayer in a makruh time and has not yet performed ruku' and sajdah, it is not called a prayer. And since it is not called a prayer, he has not committed a forbidden act in that makruh time. And when he has not committed a forbidden act, preserving what was performed is obligatory. And since qada becomes obligatory when what is obligatory to preserve and complete is invalidated, if he invalidates this performed part, qada is obligatory. From this explanation it is understood that if he starts a nafl prayer in a makruh time and completes one rak'ah, i.e., after performing sajdah, and then invalidates it, qada is not obligatory. Because after completing one rak'ah, it is called a prayer, and praying in a makruh time is prohibited, so its abandonment is obligatory. And when abandonment is obligatory, invalidating it does not require qada, so in this case qada is not obligatory.
There is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that in the case of starting a nafl prayer in a makruh time and then invalidating it, qada would not be obligatory. But the first opinion of Imam is more apparent. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and ruling with proof. It addresses whether qada (make-up) is obligatory for a nafl fast or prayer that is started in a prohibited or makruh time and then invalidated. The author, Jamil Ahmad, explains the Hanafi position (attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa) that for a fast on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), no qada is required because the very act of starting the fast is a forbidden act (since fasting on that day is prohibited), and forbidden acts must be abandoned, not completed. Therefore, neither completion nor qada is obligatory. In contrast, for a nafl prayer started in a makruh time before completing one rak'ah, qada is obligatory because the act is not yet considered a prayer (and thus not a forbidden act), so completion and qada are required. However, if a full rak'ah is completed, then it becomes a valid prayer in a prohibited time, making abandonment obligatory, so no qada. The passage also distinguishes the case of a vow (nazr) to fast on Yawm al-Nahr: the vow itself is valid and obligates the fast, but since the day is prohibited, it must be fulfilled on another day. Finally, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa is mentioned stating that even for prayer before a rak'ah, qada is not required, but the first opinion is preferred. The reasoning relies on qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference), emphasizing the distinction between acts where the prohibition is inherent in the act itself versus those where it is in the time.

Key Terms
یوم نحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice, one of the five days when fasting is prohibited.
فعل منہی عنہ (Fi'l manhi 'anhu): A forbidden act; an act that is prohibited by Shariah.
قضاء (Qada): The make-up of an obligatory act that was missed or invalidated. In this context, it refers to repeating a nafl act that was invalidated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone starts a nafl fast on Yawm al-Nahr and then intentionally invalidates it, is qada obligatory?
A) Yes, because every invalidated act requires qada.
B) No, because starting the fast itself is a forbidden act, so completion is not required.
C) Yes, but only if the fast was vowed.
D) No, because Yawm al-Nahr is not a prohibited day for nafl fasts.

Key Takeaway
Qada for an invalidated nafl act depends on whether completion was wajib; for acts that are forbidden from the start, neither completion nor qada is required.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
6 min
Definition and Ruling of I'tikaf: Sunnah Mu'akkada
Defines i'tikaf and establishes its ruling as sunnah mu'akkada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan and explain why it is sunnah mu'akkada and not wajib.

Core Idea
I'tikaf in Ramadan is sunnah mu'akkada: the Prophet's consistency without command makes it sunnah, not wajib.

The chapter on i'tikaf begins by defining the practice: staying in the mosque with intention for worship. The key legal question is the ruling of i'tikaf during the last ten days of Ramadan. Al-Quduri considered it mustahab, but the author of al-Hidayah establishes it as sunnah mu'akkada based on the Prophet's continuous practice. Understanding the distinction between consistency (muwazabah) and explicit command is crucial to grasping the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Define i'tikaf linguistically and technically
Recognize the Arabic root meaning (confining) and the Shariah definition: staying in the mosque with intention of worship (nabbat as-sabr fi al-masjid bi an-niyyah).
The linguistic origin is from 'kalafa' meaning to confine oneself.
2
Identify the two Hanafi opinions
Al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar stated i'tikaf is mustahab. The Hidayah corrects this, declaring it sunnah mu'akkada. Note that the dispute is within the Hanafi school; the reliance is on the Hidayah's view.
The text says 'wa as-sahihu sunnatun mu'akkadatan' (the correct is sunnah mu'akkada).
3
Examine the primary evidence
The Hadith of Aisha (رضي الله عنها) states that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) performed i'tikaf every last ten days of Ramadan from his arrival in Medina until he died. This continuous practice (muwazabah) is evidence of it being sunnah, not mustahab.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and supports sunnah, not wujub.
4
Address the objection of wujub
One might argue that consistency indicates obligation. However, the Hanafi principle holds that wujub requires explicit command and rebuke for abandonment, which are absent here. The Prophet ordered i'tikaf neither generally nor rebuked its abandonment. Additionally, he once abandoned i'tikaf when he saw his wives' tents, showing it is not wajib.
The text provides a counter-evidence: the Prophet's anger and cancellation of i'tikaf that year prove non-obligation.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan is sunnah mu'akkada. It is not wajib, nor merely mustahab. This is the view of al-Hidayah and subsequent Hanafi authorities.
Many Hanafi texts adopt this as the operative ruling.

Source Text

باب الاعتكاف
ترجمہ یہ باب اعتکاف کے بیان میں ہے
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
تشریح روزہ کو اعتکاف پر اس لئے مقدم کیا گیا ہے کہ روزہ اعتکاف کے لئے شرط ہے اور شر ط شئی شئی پر مقدم ہوتی ہے اس لئے روزہ
کوا تکاف پر مقدم کیا گیا۔
اعتکاف باب افتعال کا مصدر ہے مکلف سے ماخوذ ہے اور ملک متعدی ہے اور معلوف لا زم ہے شریعت کی اصطلاح میں اعتکاف
نیت کے ساتھ مسجد میں نصبر نے کا نام ہے۔
اعتکاف کی شرعی حیثیت
قَالَ الْإِعْتِكَافُ مُسْتَحَبُّ وَالصَّاحِبَحُ اللَّهُ سُنَةٌ مُوَكَدَةً لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَاطَبْ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْعَشْرِ الْأَوَاخِرِ مِنَ رَمَضَانَ وَالْمُوَاظَبَةُ دَلِيل السُّنَّةِ
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ اعتکاف مستحب ہے اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ اعتکاف سنت مؤکدہ ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے رمضان کے آخری عشرہ میں اعتکاف پر مداومت فرمائی ہے اور مداومت مسنون ہونے کی دلیل ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف مستحب ہے مگر صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف سنت مؤکدہ ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس پر مواظبت فرمائی ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے قَالَتْ عَائِشَةُ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهَا أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَآلِهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يَعْتَكِفُ فِى الْعَشْرِ الأخِيرِ مِن رَمَضَانَ حِينَ قَدِمَ الْمَدِينَةَ إلى أن تَوَفَّاهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم جیسے مدینہ تشریف لائے تا وفات رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف فرماتے رہے اور آپ کا کسی چیز پر مداومت فرمانا اس کے مسنون ہونے کی دلیل ہوتا ہے اس لئے رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف سنت مؤکدہ لیکن یہاں پر اعتراض ہو سکتا ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا مواظبت فرمانا واجب ہونے کی علامت ہے لہذا رمضان کے آخر کی عشرہ کا اعتکاف واجب ہونا چاہئے تھا اس کا جوابیہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ ہے جس چیز کو واجب قرار دینا چاہتے تو اس پر مواظبت فرماتے اور مواظبت کے بعد اس کو کرنے کا حکم فرماتے اور چھوڑنے والے پر نکیر فرماتے۔ حالانکہ آپ نے نہ تو لوگوں کو اس کا حکم فرمایا ہے اور نہ ہی اس کے ترک کرنے پر تکیہ فرمائی ہے پس اگر رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف واجب ہوتا تو آپ لوگوں کو اس کا حکم فرماتے اور ترک کرنے والے پر نکیر فرماتے پس ثابت ہوا کہ یہ غیر واجب ہے اعتکاف کے عدم وجوب کی دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اعتکاف کرنے کے لئے مسجد میں قبہ بنانے یعنی پر دو ڈالنے کا امر فرمایا پھر مسجد میں داخل ہوئے تو آپ نے دو تھے اور دیکھے ان کے بارے میں سوال کیا تو پتہ چلا کہ ایک قبہ عائشہ کا ہے اور ایک حصہ کا ہے یہ دیکھ کر آپ کو غصہ آیا ہوں آپ نے اپنا قبہ بنانے کا حکم دیا اور اس سال
انتکاف ترک فرمایا اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اعتکاف واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ وجوب کی دلیل بغیر ترک کے مواظبت کرنا ہے۔
Chapter of I'tikaf: Translation: This chapter is about the explanation of i'tikaf. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu sharh of Hidayah, Volume Three. Explanation: Fasting was placed before i'tikaf because fasting is a condition for i'tikaf, and the condition precedes the conditioned thing. Therefore fasting was placed before i'tikaf. I'tikaf is a masdar from bab ifti'al, derived from 'kalafa' meaning to confine, muta'addi (transitive) and ma'luf (familiar) are necessary. In Shariah terminology, i'tikaf is the name for staying in the mosque with intention. Legal status of i'tikaf: Al-Quduri said: I'tikaf is mustahab (recommended), and the correct view is that it is sunnah mu'akkada (emphasized sunnah) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) consistently performed it in the last ten days of Ramadan, and consistency is evidence of sunnah. Translation: Quduri said that i'tikaf is mustahab, and the correct is that i'tikaf is sunnah mu'akkada because the Prophet (peace be upon him) consistently performed i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan, and consistency is evidence of being sunnah. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan is mustahab, but the correct thing is that i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan is sunnah mu'akkada. The evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) consistently performed it. As narrated: 'Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) said: The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) used to perform i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan from when he came to Medina until Allah took his soul.' And the Prophet's consistent practice of something is evidence of it being sunnah. Therefore i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan is sunnah mu'akkada. But here an objection can be raised: The Prophet's consistency is a sign of obligation (wujub), so i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan should be wajib. The answer is that when the Prophet intended to make something wajib, he would consistently do it, and after consistency he would order people to do it and rebuke those who left it. However, he did not order people to do it nor did he rebuke anyone for leaving it. So if i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan were wajib, he would have ordered it and rebuked those who left it. So it is established that it is not wajib. Another evidence for the non-obligation of i'tikaf is that once the Prophet ordered a tent to be set up in the mosque for i'tikaf. Then he entered the mosque and saw some tents; he asked about them and was told that one was for Aisha and one for Hafsah. Seeing this, he became angry, ordered his own tent to be taken down, and abandoned i'tikaf that year. This also shows that i'tikaf is not wajib, because the evidence of obligation is consistent practice without ever leaving it.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement for i'tikaf. It begins the chapter on i'tikaf, explaining why the chapter on fasting was placed before it (because fasting is a condition for i'tikaf). It defines i'tikaf linguistically and technically: in Shariah, it means staying in the mosque with the intention of devotion. The main legal discussion is the status of i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan. Al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar stated it is mustahab, but the author of al-Hidayah (and the commentator here) declares the correct view is sunnah mu'akkada. The proof is the Prophet's consistent practice (muwazabah) of i'tikaf every year from his arrival in Medina until his death, as reported by Aisha. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: consistency usually indicates obligation (wujub), but here it is not wajib because the Prophet did not command it nor rebuke its abandonment. An additional proof is that once the Prophet began i'tikaf, then when he saw the tents of his wives, he became angry and did not complete it that year; this shows that if it were wajib, he would not have left it. The final ruling: i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan is sunnah mu'akkada, not wajib.

Key Terms
اعتکاف (I'tikaf): Staying in the mosque with the intention of worship, especially during the last ten days of Ramadan.
سنة مؤکدہ (Sunnah mu'akkada): An emphasized sunnah; an act that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged, but is not obligatory. Abandoning it without excuse is disliked (makruh tanzihi).
مستحب (Mustahab): Recommended; an act that is desirable but not obligatory or emphasized sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan considered sunnah mu'akkada and not wajib?
A) Because the Prophet never performed it consistently.
B) Because the Prophet performed it consistently but did not command others to do so nor rebuke those who left it.
C) Because the Prophet abandoned it one year, making it non-obligatory.
D) Because fasting, which is a condition, is not wajib.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan is sunnah mu'akkada, not wajib, because the Prophet's consistent practice (muwazabah) without command indicates sunnah.
