The Legal Status of I'tikaf: Sunnah Mu'akkadah Not Wajib
Establishes the hukm of i'tikaf as sunnah mu'akkadah not wajib, with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on i'tikaf (sunnah mu'akkadah) and explain why it is not wajib, using the evidence of the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) and the absence of command/rebuke.

Core Idea
Continuous practice (muwazabah) alone proves sunnah, not wujub; obligation requires command and rebuke for omission.

In this lesson, we examine the legal status of i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan. The matn from al-Quduri initially suggests mustahab, but the correct Hanafi position is sunnah mu'akkadah. The commentator provides the key reasoning: the Prophet's continuous practice indicates sunnah, not wujub, because he neither commanded others nor rebuked those who omitted it. We'll explore the proof from the hadith of Aisha and the incident with the tents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial classification
Note that al-Quduri said i'tikaf is mustahab, but the correct view is sunnah mu'akkadah. The difference is between a recommended act and an emphasized sunnah.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Aisha (radiAllahu anha) states that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) continuously practiced i'tikaf from the time he came to Medina until his death.
This hadith is in Sahih Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, continuous practice (muwazabah) indicates that an act is sunnah, not wajib. The word 'kana' in the hadith confirms consistency.
Muwazabah without command or rebuke = sunnah.
4
Respond to the objection
One might argue that the Prophet's continuous practice implies obligation. The commentator counters: if it were wajib, the Prophet would have commanded others and rebuked those who omitted it, which he did not.
5
Confirm with secondary evidence
The incident where the Prophet ordered a tent, saw his wives' tents, became angry, and then abandoned i'tikaf that year proves that i'tikaf is not obligatory, as an obligatory act cannot be omitted without reason.
This further supports the non-obligatory status.

Source Text

كتاب الصوم
باب الاعتكاف
ترجمہ یہ باب اعتکاف کے بیان میں ہے
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
تشریح روزہ کو اعتکاف پر اس لئے مقدم کیا گیا ہے کہ روزہ اعتکاف کے لئے شرط ہے اور شرط شئی شئی پر مقدم ہوتی ہے اس لئے روزہ کو اعتکاف پر مقدم کیا گیا۔
اعتکاف باب افتعال کا مصدر ہے مکلف سے ماخوذ ہے اور ملک متعدی ہے اور معلوف لازم ہے شریعت کی اصطلاح میں اعتکاف نیت کے ساتھ مسجد میں ٹھہرنے کا نام ہے۔
اعتکاف کی شرعی حیثیت
قَالَ الْإِعْتِكَافُ مُسْتَحَبُّ وَالصَّحِيحُ أَنَّهُ سُنَّةٌ مُؤَكَّدَةٌ لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَاطَبَ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْعَشْرِ الْأَوَاخِرِ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ وَالْمُوَاظَبَةُ دَلِيلُ السُّنَّةِ

تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف مستحب ہے مگر صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف سنت مؤکدہ ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس پر مواظبت فرمائی ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے قَالَتْ عَائِشَةُ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهَا أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يَعْتَكِفُ فِي الْعَشْرِ الْأَخِيرِ مِنْ رَمَضَانَ حِينَ قَدِمَ الْمَدِينَةَ إِلَى أَنْ تَوَفَّاهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم جیسے مدینہ تشریف لائے تا وفات رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف فرماتے رہے اور آپ کا کسی چیز پر مداومت فرمانا اس کے مسنون ہونے کی دلیل ہوتا ہے اس لئے رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف سنت مؤکدہ لیکن یہاں پر اعتراض ہو سکتا ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا مواظبت فرمانا واجب ہونے کی علامت ہے لہذا رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف واجب ہونا چاہئے تھا اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ جس چیز کو واجب قرار دینا چاہتے تو اس پر مواظبت فرماتے اور مواظبت کے بعد اس کو کرنے کا حکم فرماتے اور چھوڑنے والے پر نکیر فرماتے۔ حالانکہ آپ نے نہ تو لوگوں کو اس کا حکم فرمایا ہے اور نہ ہی اس کے ترک کرنے پر نکیر فرمائی ہے پس اگر رمضان کے آخری عشرہ کا اعتکاف واجب ہوتا تو آپ لوگوں کو اس کا حکم فرماتے اور ترک کرنے والے پر نکیر فرماتے پس ثابت ہوا کہ یہ غیر واجب ہے اعتکاف کے عدم وجوب کی دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ ایک مرتبہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اعتکاف کرنے کے لئے مسجد میں قبہ بنانے یعنی پردہ ڈالنے کا امر فرمایا پھر مسجد میں داخل ہوئے تو آپ نے دو تھے اور دیکھے ان کے بارے میں سوال کیا تو پتہ چلا کہ ایک قبہ عائشہ کا ہے اور ایک حفصہ کا ہے یہ دیکھ کر آپ کو غصہ آیا پھر آپ نے اپنا قبہ بنانے کا حکم دیا اور اس سال اعتکاف ترک فرمایا اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اعتکاف واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ وجوب کی دلیل بغیر ترک کے مواظبت کرنا ہے۔
Book of Fasting. Chapter of I'tikaf. Translation: This chapter is about the explanation of i'tikaf. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Three. Explanation: Fasting is mentioned before i'tikaf because fasting is a condition for i'tikaf, and a condition is placed before the conditioned thing. Therefore fasting was placed before i'tikaf. I'tikaf is the verbal noun of the pattern ifti'al, derived from 'mukallaf', and 'mulak' is transitive and 'ma'luf' is intransitive. In the terminology of Shari'ah, i'tikaf means staying in the mosque with the intention. The legal status of i'tikaf. He said: I'tikaf is mustahab, and the correct view is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) continuously practiced it in the last ten days of Ramadan, and continuous practice is evidence of sunnah. Translation: Quduri said that i'tikaf is mustahab, but the correct view is that i'tikaf is sunnah mu'akkadah because the Prophet (peace be upon him) continuously practiced i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan, and continuous practice is evidence of it being sunnah. Commentary: The author of Quduri said that i'tikaf of the last ten days of Ramadan is mustahab, but the correct view is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) continuously practiced it, as narrated by Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to practice i'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan from the time he came to Medina until he passed away. His continuous practice of something indicates that it is sunnah. So i'tikaf of the last ten days of Ramadan is sunnah mu'akkadah. However, an objection could be raised: The Prophet's continuous practice is a sign of obligation, so i'tikaf of the last ten days should be obligatory. The answer is that when the Prophet intended to make something obligatory, he would continuously practice it, then command others to do it, and rebuke those who omitted it. But he neither commanded people to do it nor rebuked them for omitting it. So if i'tikaf of the last ten days were obligatory, he would have commanded it and rebuked its omission. Thus it is proven that it is not obligatory. Another evidence for the non-obligation of i'tikaf is that once the Prophet ordered a tent to be set up in the mosque for i'tikaf. When he entered the mosque, he saw two tents and asked about them. He was told one was Aisha's and one was Hafsa's. He became angry, ordered his own tent, but then abandoned i'tikaf that year. This also shows i'tikaf is not obligatory, because obligation is evidenced by continuous practice without omission.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion probe into the legal status (hukm) of i'tikaf, specifically the i'tikaf of the last ten days of Ramadan. The matn from al-Quduri initially states that i'tikaf is mustahab (recommended), but the correct position is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib. The commentator provides two proofs: First, the continuous practice of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) from his arrival in Medina until his death, as reported by Aisha (radiAllahu anha). In Hanafi usul, continuous practice (muwazabah) indicates sunnah, not wujub, unless accompanied by an explicit command or rebuke for omission. The commentator addresses the potential objection that the Prophet's continuous practice could indicate wujub by explaining that he did not command others or rebuke those who missed it. Second, the incident where the Prophet ordered tents for i'tikaf but found additional tents of his wives, became angry, ordered his own tent, but then abandoned i'tikaf that year – proving that i'tikaf is not wajib, as obligation would require consistent practice without any omission. Thus, the Hanafi position is clear: i'tikaf in the last ten days is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahab): A recommended act that the Prophet did sometimes but not consistently.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed, but which is not obligatory.
المواظبة (al-muwazabah): Continuous practice without omission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Companions disagreed on its obligation.
D) Because it is only for men, not women.

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf in the last ten days of Ramadan is sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school, established by the Prophet's continuous practice without command or rebuke.

Definition and Pillar of I'tikaf
Defining i'tikaf and its rukn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of i'tikaf, identify its rukn, and explain why the rukn is al-lubth (staying).

Core Idea
I'tikaf is staying in the mosque; the staying itself is the pillar (rukn) that defines the act.

In this lesson, we examine the opening lines of the passage on i'tikaf. The author first defines i'tikaf as staying in the mosque with fasting and intention. He then identifies the rukn as the mere staying, since the act is named after it. This clarifies the essential core of i'tikaf before moving to its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the first sentence: i'tikaf is defined as staying in the mosque with fasting and intention. Note that the definition includes both conditions.
2
Locate the rukn
The author states that the staying (lubth) itself is the rukn. Understand that the rukn is the integral part without which i'tikaf does not exist.
3
Understand the reasoning
The justification is that i'tikaf is named after the act of staying, so existence of i'tikaf depends on staying.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهُوَ اللَّبْتُ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ مَعَ الصَّوْمِ وَنِيَّةِ الْإِعْتِكَافِ أَمَّا اللَّبْتُ فَرُكْنُهُ لِأَنَّهُ يُسَمَّى عَنْهُ فَكَانَ وُجُودُهُ بِهِ وَالصَّوْمُ مِنْ شَرْطِهِ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِيِّ وَالنِّيَّةُ شَرْطٌ فِي سَائِرِ الْعِبَادَاتِ هُوَ يَقُولُ أَنَّ الصَّوْمَ عِبَادَةٌ وَهُوَ أَصْلٌ بِنَفْسِهِ فَلَا يَكُونُ شَرْطًا لِغَيْرِهِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا اعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا بِالصَّوْمِ وَالْقِيَاسُ فِي مُقَابَلَةِ النَّصِّ الْمَنْقُولِ غَيْرُ مَقْبُولٍ ثُمَّ الصَّوْمُ شَرْطٌ لِصِحَّةِ الْوَاجِبِ مِنْهُ رِوَايَةً وَاحِدَةً وَلِصِحَّةِ التَّطَوُّعِ فِيمَا رَوَى الْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِظَاهِرِ مَا رَوَيْنَا وَعَلَى هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَةِ لَا يَكُونُ أَقَلُّ مِنْ يَوْمٍ وَفِي رِوَايَةِ الْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ أَقَلُّهُ سَاعَةً فَيَكُونُ مِنْ غَيْرِ صَوْمٍ لِأَنَّ مُبْنَى النَّفْلِ عَلَى الْمُسَاهَلَةِ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُ يَقْعُدُ فِي صَلَاةِ النَّفْلِ مَعَ الْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى الْقِيَامِ وَلَوْ شَرَعَ فِيهِ ثُمَّ قَطَعَهُ لَا يَلْزَمُهُ الْقَضَاءُ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْأَصْلِ لِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُقَدَّرٍ فَلَمْ يَكُنِ الْقَطْعُ إِبْطَالًا وَفِي رِوَايَةِ الْحَسَنِ يَلْزَمُه لِأَنَّهُ مُقَدَّرٌ بِالْيَوْمِ كَالصَّوْمِ ثُمَّ الْإِعْتِكَافُ لَا يَصِحُّ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدِ جَمَاعَةٍ لِقَوْلِ حُذَيْفَةَ لَا اعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدِ جَمَاعَةٍ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُّ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدٍ يُصَلَّى فِيهِ الصَّلَوَاتُ الْخَمْسُ لِأَنَّهُ عِبَادَةُ انْتِظَارِ الصَّلَاةِ فَيَخْتَصُّ بِمَكَانٍ تُؤَدَّى فِيهِ أَمَّا الْمَرْأَةُ فَتَعْتَكِفُ فِي مَسْجِدِ بَيْتِهَا لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْمَوْضِعُ لِصَلَاتِهَا فَيَتَحَقَّقُ انْتِظَارُهَا فِيهِ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهَا فِي الْبَيْتِ مَسْجِدٌ تَجْعَلْ مَوْضِعًا فِيهِ فَتَعْتَكِفُ فِيهِ
And i'tikaf is staying in the mosque with fasting and the intention of i'tikaf. As for the staying, it is the rukn (pillar) because it is named after it, so i'tikaf exists through it. Fasting is a condition of it according to us (Hanafis), contrary to al-Shafi'i. Intention is a condition in all acts of worship. He (al-Shafi'i) says that fasting is an act of worship and is a standalone principle, so it cannot be a condition for something else. Our evidence is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting.' And analogy against a transmitted text is not accepted. Then, fasting is a condition for the validity of obligatory i'tikaf in one narration; and for the validity of voluntary i'tikaf in what Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, due to the apparent meaning of what we narrated. According to this narration, it cannot be less than a day. And in the narration of al-Asl (the original), which is the saying of Muhammad, its minimum is a moment (hour), so it can be without fasting because the foundation of nafl (supererogatory) is leniency. Do you not see that one sits in nafl prayer despite ability to stand? And if one starts it then cuts it, qada' (making up) is not necessary in the narration of al-Asl, because it is not quantified, so cutting it is not annulment. In the narration of al-Hasan, qada' is necessary because it is quantified by the day like fasting. Then i'tikaf is not valid except in a masjid of congregation (jama'ah), due to the saying of Hudhayfah: 'There is no i'tikaf except in a masjid of congregation.' And from Abu Hanifa that it is not valid except in a masjid in which the five daily prayers are performed, because it is the act of waiting for prayer, so it is specific to a place where prayer is performed. As for a woman, she performs i'tikaf in the masjid of her house, because that is the place of her prayer, so her waiting is realized therein. And if she does not have a masjid in the house, she designates a spot in it and performs i'tikaf there.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a parsing exercise that defines i'tikaf and clarifies its rukn (pillar), conditions, and place requirements. The definition states that i'tikaf is staying in the mosque with both fasting and intention. The rukn is the staying itself, as i'tikaf is named after the act of staying. Fasting is a condition for validity according to the Hanafi school, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that fasting is an independent worship and cannot condition another. The Hanafi proof is the hadith 'La i'tikafa illa bi al-sawm' (No i'tikaf except with fasting), and they reject analogy (qiyas) in the face of a transmitted text (nas). The passage then addresses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the minimum duration for nafl (voluntary) i'tikaf: According to a narration from Imam Muhammad (al-Asl), the minimum is a moment (one hour), and thus it does not require fasting, because nafl acts are based on leniency. According to a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa, the minimum is one day, requiring fasting. The consequence of cutting a nafl i'tikaf also differs: in al-Asl, no qada' is required because it is not time-bound; in al-Hasan's narration, qada' is required. Finally, the place condition: i'tikaf is only valid in a masjid where congregational prayers are held, specifically a masjid where the five daily prayers are performed according to Abu Hanifa, based on the hadith of Hudhayfah. For women, the place is the 'masjid of her house' (her designated prayer area), and if there is none, she designates a spot.

Key Terms
اللبث (al-lubth): Staying or remaining in the mosque; it is the rukn (pillar) of i'tikaf.
الركن (al-rukn): The integral part of i'tikaf without which the act is invalid; here it is the physical staying.
شرط (shart): A condition external to the act that is necessary for its validity, such as fasting and intention for i'tikaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which element is considered the rukn of i'tikaf?
A) Fasting
B) Intention
C) Staying (al-lubth)
D) The mosque

Key Takeaway
The staying (lubth) is the pillar of i'tikaf; fasting and intention are conditions for its validity.

The Fasting Condition: Inter-Madhhab Dispute and Minimum Duration
Dispute on fasting condition and intra-Hanafi minimum duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi evidence for fasting as a condition for i'tikaf, explain the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response, and differentiate between the two Hanafi narrations on the minimum duration of nafl i'tikaf.

Core Idea
Fasting is a condition for i'tikaf based on the hadith; for nafl i'tikaf, the minimum is a moment (hour) according to Imam Muhammad, but a full day according to Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration from Abu Hanifa.

This lesson delves into the detailed discussion on fasting as a condition for i'tikaf. The author presents the Shafi'i counter-argument and the Hanafi rebuttal based on an explicit prophetic hadith. Then, the lesson explores an intra-Hanafi divergence regarding voluntary i'tikaf: whether it requires fasting and what its minimum duration is. This reveals the school's internal reasoning and the principle that nafl acts are based on leniency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The question is whether fasting is a condition for validity of i'tikaf.
2
State the Shafi'i argument
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that fasting is an independent worship and cannot condition another.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The hadith 'La i'tikafa illa bi al-sawm' is explicit; qiyas against a clear text is invalid.
This hadith is the primary evidence.
4
Differentiate the two narrations on nafl i'tikaf
Hasan from Abu Hanifa requires a day and fasting; Muhammad's view (al-Asl) allows a moment without fasting.
Key principle: nafl acts are based on leniency.
5
Understand the legal consequences
In Muhammad's view, no qada' if cut; in Hasan's, qada' is required because it is time-bound.
This affects whether cutting the i'tikaf is considered an annulment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهُوَ اللَّبْتُ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ مَعَ الصَّوْمِ وَنِيَّةِ الْإِعْتِكَافِ أَمَّا اللَّبْتُ فَرُكْنُهُ لِأَنَّهُ يُسَمَّى عَنْهُ فَكَانَ وُجُودُهُ بِهِ وَالصَّوْمُ مِنْ شَرْطِهِ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِيِّ وَالنِّيَّةُ شَرْطٌ فِي سَائِرِ الْعِبَادَاتِ هُوَ يَقُولُ أَنَّ الصَّوْمَ عِبَادَةٌ وَهُوَ أَصْلٌ بِنَفْسِهِ فَلَا يَكُونُ شَرْطًا لِغَيْرِهِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا اعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا بِالصَّوْمِ وَالْقِيَاسُ فِي مُقَابَلَةِ النَّصِّ الْمَنْقُولِ غَيْرُ مَقْبُولٍ ثُمَّ الصَّوْمُ شَرْطٌ لِصِحَّةِ الْوَاجِبِ مِنْهُ رِوَايَةً وَاحِدَةً وَلِصِحَّةِ التَّطَوُّعِ فِيمَا رَوَى الْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِظَاهِرِ مَا رَوَيْنَا وَعَلَى هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَةِ لَا يَكُونُ أَقَلُّ مِنْ يَوْمٍ وَفِي رِوَايَةِ الْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ أَقَلُّهُ سَاعَةً فَيَكُونُ مِنْ غَيْرِ صَوْمٍ لِأَنَّ مُبْنَى النَّفْلِ عَلَى الْمُسَاهَلَةِ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُ يَقْعُدُ فِي صَلَاةِ النَّفْلِ مَعَ الْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى الْقِيَامِ وَلَوْ شَرَعَ فِيهِ ثُمَّ قَطَعَهُ لَا يَلْزَمُهُ الْقَضَاءُ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْأَصْلِ لِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُقَدَّرٍ فَلَمْ يَكُنِ الْقَطْعُ إِبْطَالًا وَفِي رِوَايَةِ الْحَسَنِ يَلْزَمُه لِأَنَّهُ مُقَدَّرٌ بِالْيَوْمِ كَالصَّوْمِ ثُمَّ الْإِعْتِكَافُ لَا يَصِحُّ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدِ جَمَاعَةٍ لِقَوْلِ حُذَيْفَةَ لَا اعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدِ جَمَاعَةٍ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُّ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدٍ يُصَلَّى فِيهِ الصَّلَوَاتُ الْخَمْسُ لِأَنَّهُ عِبَادَةُ انْتِظَارِ الصَّلَاةِ فَيَخْتَصُّ بِمَكَانٍ تُؤَدَّى فِيهِ أَمَّا الْمَرْأَةُ فَتَعْتَكِفُ فِي مَسْجِدِ بَيْتِهَا لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْمَوْضِعُ لِصَلَاتِهَا فَيَتَحَقَّقُ انْتِظَارُهَا فِيهِ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهَا فِي الْبَيْتِ مَسْجِدٌ تَجْعَلْ مَوْضِعًا فِيهِ فَتَعْتَكِفُ فِيهِ
And i'tikaf is staying in the mosque with fasting and the intention of i'tikaf. As for the staying, it is the rukn (pillar) because it is named after it, so i'tikaf exists through it. Fasting is a condition of it according to us (Hanafis), contrary to al-Shafi'i. Intention is a condition in all acts of worship. He (al-Shafi'i) says that fasting is an act of worship and is a standalone principle, so it cannot be a condition for something else. Our evidence is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting.' And analogy against a transmitted text is not accepted. Then, fasting is a condition for the validity of obligatory i'tikaf in one narration; and for the validity of voluntary i'tikaf in what Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, due to the apparent meaning of what we narrated. According to this narration, it cannot be less than a day. And in the narration of al-Asl (the original), which is the saying of Muhammad, its minimum is a moment (hour), so it can be without fasting because the foundation of nafl (supererogatory) is leniency. Do you not see that one sits in nafl prayer despite ability to stand? And if one starts it then cuts it, qada' (making up) is not necessary in the narration of al-Asl, because it is not quantified, so cutting it is not annulment. In the narration of al-Hasan, qada' is necessary because it is quantified by the day like fasting. Then i'tikaf is not valid except in a masjid of congregation (jama'ah), due to the saying of Hudhayfah: 'There is no i'tikaf except in a masjid of congregation.' And from Abu Hanifa that it is not valid except in a masjid in which the five daily prayers are performed, because it is the act of waiting for prayer, so it is specific to a place where prayer is performed. As for a woman, she performs i'tikaf in the masjid of her house, because that is the place of her prayer, so her waiting is realized therein. And if she does not have a masjid in the house, she designates a spot in it and performs i'tikaf there.

النفل (al-nafl): Voluntary or supererogatory act of worship.

The Place Condition for I'tikaf
Specifying the spatial conditions for i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the requirement that i'tikaf must be performed in a masjid of congregation, explain Abu Hanifa's specification of a masjid where the five daily prayers are held, and describe the rule for women's i'tikaf.

Core Idea
I'tikaf must be performed in a mosque where congregational prayers are held; women use a designated prayer area in their home.

The final segment of the passage on i'tikaf addresses the place condition. The author cites the saying of Hudhayfah that there is no i'tikaf except in a masjid of congregation. Abu Hanifa further specifies that it must be a masjid where the five daily prayers are performed, linking i'tikaf to the act of waiting for prayer. For women, due to their domestic prayer space, the 'masjid of her house' suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general place condition
I'tikaf is only valid in a masjid where jama'ah (congregation) is held.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's specification
He requires a masjid where all five prayers are performed, because i'tikaf is an act of waiting for prayer.
3
Note the evidence
The saying of Hudhayfah: 'There is no i'tikaf except in a masjid of congregation.'
4
Apply to women
Women use their designated prayer spot in their home; if none, they designate a spot.
This adapts the condition to a woman's circumstances.

Definition of I'tikaf: Pillar and Condition of Intention
Defining i'tikaf, its pillar, and condition of intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of i'tikaf, identify its rukn (lubth), and explain why intention is a condition rather than a pillar.

Core Idea
The pillar of i'tikaf is physical stay; intention is its vital condition.

This passage from the Hidayah provides a concise definition of i'tikaf, distinguishing between its essential pillar and the conditions required for validity. Understanding this distinction is foundational for mastering the fiqh of i'tikaf in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
The passage defines i'tikaf as staying (lubth) in the mosque with fasting and intention. Note the three components: stay, fasting, intention.
2
Recognize the rukn (pillar)
The text explicitly states that lubth (staying) is the rukn because the term i'tikaf is derived from staying. The rukn is the essential part without which the act does not exist.
In Hanafi usul, rukn is an integral part of the act itself.
3
Note the shart (condition) of intention
Intention (niyyah) is presented as a condition (shart) in all acts of worship. It is not part of the rukn but an external prerequisite for validity.
Hanafis consider niyyah a shart, not a rukn, distinguishing it from the act's essence.
4
Consider the role of fasting
Fasting is also included in the definition ('with fasting'). In the Hanafi school, fasting is a condition for the validity of i'tikaf, though this passage does not explicitly label it as shart.
Other schools may differ on whether fasting is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهُوَ اللَّبْثُ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ مَعَ الصَّوْمِ وَنِيَّةِ الْإِعْتِكَافِ أَمَّا اللَّبْثُ فَرُكْنُهُ لِأَنَّهُ [يُسَمَّى] عَنْهُ فَكَانَ وُجُودُهُ بِهِ وَالنِّيَّةُ شَرْطٌ فِي سَائِرِ الْعِبَادَاتِ
And it is the staying in the mosque with fasting and the intention of i'tikaf. As for the staying, it is its pillar because it is named from it, so its existence is by it. And the intention is a condition in all acts of worship.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage defines i'tikaf and identifies its essential components. The author begins by giving the definition: i'tikaf is staying (lubth) in the mosque along with fasting and the intention of i'tikaf. Then he clarifies that the staying itself is the rukn (pillar) of i'tikaf, because the term i'tikaf linguistically derives from 'akafa meaning to stay or remain, so the essence of the act is the physical presence in the mosque. He then states that intention (niyyah) is a condition (shart) in all acts of worship, including i'tikaf, to distinguish worship from mere habit. In Hanafi fiqh, the rukn is that without which the act does not exist, while the shart is something that must be present for validity but is not part of the essence.

Key Terms
اللَّبْث (al-lubth): Staying or remaining in a place; in i'tikaf, it is the physical stay in the mosque.
الركن (ar-rukn): Pillar or integral part; without which the act is invalid.
النِّيَّة (an-niyyah): Intention; a condition in all acts of worship to differentiate them from mere habits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, what is the pillar (rukn) of i'tikaf?
A) Fasting
B) Intention
C) Staying in the mosque
D) Both fasting and intention

Key Takeaway
The essence of i'tikaf is physical presence in the mosque; intention and fasting are necessary conditions for its validity.

Voluntary I'tikaf: Fasting and Duration – Intra-Hanafi Analysis
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fasting and duration for voluntary i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi narrations on voluntary i'tikaf and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Voluntary i'tikaf does not require fasting in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known internal disagreement on whether fasting is a condition for voluntary i'tikaf and what its minimum duration is. This lesson unpacks the two narrations – one from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad via Abu Hanifa, and the other from Imam Muhammad in al-Asl – and the legal reasoning behind each. By the end, you will understand why the position of Imam Muhammad (no fasting, minimum one hour) is the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rivayat
Recognize that the passage presents two distinct narrations within the Hanafi school: one from al-Hasan narrating from Abu Hanifa (requires fasting, minimum one day), and the other from Imam Muhammad in al-Asl (no fasting, minimum one hour).
Zahir al-Riwayah typically refers to al-Asl and the six core books of Imam Muhammad.
2
Examine the evidence for each
For the first narration: the hadith 'la i'tikafa illa bi saum' is cited as evidence. For the second: qiyas on voluntary prayer (nafl salat) based on the principle of leniency (musahalah).
The hadith is general; the dispute is whether it applies equally to voluntary i'tikaf.
3
Understand the qiyas reasoning
Imam Muhammad analogizes voluntary i'tikaf to voluntary prayer: in nafl salat, one may sit despite ability to stand, and if broken, no qada is required. Similarly, voluntary i'tikaf is not specified, so fasting is not required and there is no minimum.
The key difference: in the first narration, voluntary i'tikaf is specified (muqaddar) by the day, like obligatory i'tikaf.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Marghinani indicates that the narration of al-Asl (Imam Muhammad) is the relied-upon position for fatwa, due to its authority as Zahir al-Riwayah.
This is a standard tarjih within the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a person performing voluntary i'tikaf may do so without fasting and for as short as one hour, per the mufta bihi view. If one breaks it, no qada is required.
This leniency reflects the nature of supererogatory acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الصَّوْمُ شَرْطٌ لِصِحَّةِ الْوَاجِبِ مِنْهُ رِوَايَةً وَاحِدَةً وَلِصِحَّةِ التَّطَوُّعِ فِيمَا رَوَى الْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِظَاهِرِ مَا رَوَيْنَا وَعَلَى هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَةِ لَا يَكُونُ أَقَلَّ مِنْ يَوْمٍ وَفِي رِوَايَةِ الْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ أَقَلُّهُ سَاعَةً فَيَكُونُ مِنْ غَيْرِ صَوْمٍ لِأَنَّ مَبْنَى النَّفْلِ عَلَى الْمُسَاهَلَةِ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُ يَقْعُدُ فِي صَلَاةِ النَّفْلِ مَعَ الْقُدْرَةِ عَلَى الْقِيَامِ وَلَوْ شَرَعَ فِيهِ ثُمَّ قَطَعَهُ لَا يَلْزَمُهُ الْقَضَاءُ فِي رِوَايَةِ الْأَصْلِ لِأَنَّهُ غَيْرُ مُقَدَّرٍ فَلَمْ يَكُنِ الْقَطْعُ إِبْطَالًا وَفِي رِوَايَةِ الْحَسَنِ يَلْزَمُ لِأَنَّهُ مُقَدَّرٌ بِالْيَوْمِ كَالصَّوْمِ
Then fasting is a condition for the validity of obligatory i'tikaf in one narration. And for the validity of voluntary i'tikaf, according to what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, due to the apparent meaning of what we narrated (the hadith), and according to this narration it is not less than a day. And in the narration of al-Asl, which is the saying of Muhammad, its minimum is an hour, so it is without fasting because the foundation of supererogatory acts is leniency. Do you not see that one sits in voluntary prayer despite ability to stand? And if one begins it then breaks it, qada is not required in the narration of al-Asl because it is not specified, so breaking it is not annulment. And in the narration of al-Hasan, qada is required because it is specified by the day like fasting.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf. There are two narrations within the school. In one narration (from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa), the same condition of fasting applies to voluntary i'tikaf, and the minimum duration is one day, based on the general hadith 'la i'tikafa illa bi saum'. In the second narration (from al-Asl, i.e., the core books of Imam Muhammad, which represent the Zahir al-Riwayah), voluntary i'tikaf can be as short as an hour, and fasting is not required. The reasoning is that supererogatory acts are based on ease (musahalah), as evidenced by the fact that one may sit in voluntary prayer even though standing is possible. Furthermore, if one starts a voluntary i'tikaf and then breaks it, no qada is required in the narration of al-Asl because it is not specified; but in the narration of al-Hasan, qada is required because it is specified to a day. The relied-upon position is usually the view of Imam Muhammad (the narration of al-Asl) due to its prevalence in the core books.

Key Terms
رِوَايَة (riwayah): Narration or transmission; a version of a ruling attributed to an imam through a specific chain.
النَّفْل (an-nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary act of worship.
الْمُسَاهَلَة (al-musahalah): Leniency or ease; the principle that supererogatory acts are built on ease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration of al-Asl (Imam Muhammad), what is the minimum duration for voluntary i'tikaf?
A) One day
B) One night
C) One hour
D) There is no minimum

Key Takeaway
Voluntary i'tikaf in the Hanafi school, per the mufta bihi, does not require fasting and can be as short as one hour, reflecting the principle of leniency for supererogatory acts.

Place Conditions for I'tikaf: Mosque for Men, Home for Women
Specifying the required location for i'tikaf for men and women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required place for i'tikaf for men and women according to the Hanafi school and explain the basis for the distinction.

Core Idea
For men, i'tikaf requires a congregational mosque; for women, a home prayer area suffices.

This passage specifies the location requirement for i'tikaf, a key condition for its validity. For men, the i'tikaf must take place in a masjid jama'ah (mosque where congregational prayers are held), while for women, the prayer area of her home is sufficient. The distinction arises from the nature of i'tikaf as waiting for prayer and the optimal places for prayer for each gender.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
I'tikaf is the act being ruled upon; place is a condition (shart) for its validity.
The text explicitly says 'i'tikaf is not valid except in a congregational mosque.'
2
State the rule for men
Men must perform i'tikaf in a masjid jama'ah, a mosque where the five daily prayers are offered in congregation.
The evidence includes the saying of Hudhayfah and Abu Hanifa's specification.
3
State the rule for women
Women should perform i'tikaf in the prayer area of their house (masjid baytiha).
If no designated area exists, they can set aside a spot for it.
4
Note the evidence
The proof includes the statement of Hudhayfah and the analogy that i'tikaf is ‘waiting for prayer’, so it must be in a place where prayer is performed.
For women, the home prayer area is where they perform their best prayers.
5
Recognize the practical difference
This condition distinguishes the Hanafi view from other schools that allow i'tikaf in any mosque.
The practical consequence: a man cannot do i'tikaf in a small musalla without full congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الْإِعْتِكَافُ لَا يَصِحُّ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدِ جَمَاعَةٍ لِقَوْلِ حُذَيْفَةَ لَا اعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدِ جَمَاعَةٍ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُّ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدٍ يُصَلَّى فِيهِ الصَّلَوَاتُ الْخَمْسُ لِأَنَّهُ عِبَادَةُ انْتِظَارِ الصَّلَاةِ فَيُخْتَصُّ بِمَكَانٍ يُؤَدَّى فِيهِ أَمَّا الْمَرْأَةُ فَتُعْتَكِفُ فِي مَسْجِدِ بَيْتِهَا لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْمَوْضِعُ لِصَلَاتِهَا فَيَتَحَقَّقُ انْتِظَارُهَا فِيهِ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهَا فِي الْبَيْتِ مَسْجِدٌ تَجْعَلُ مَوْضِعًا فِيهِ فَتَعْتَكِفُ فِيهِ
Then i'tikaf is not valid except in a congregational mosque, due to the saying of Hudhayfah: 'There is no i'tikaf except in a congregational mosque.' And from Abu Hanifa that it is not valid except in a mosque in which the five prayers are performed, because it is an act of waiting for prayer, so it is specific to a place where prayer is performed. As for a woman, she performs i'tikaf in the prayer place of her house, because that is the place for her prayer, so her waiting is realized there. And if she does not have a prayer place in her house, she designates a spot for it and performs i'tikaf there.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage lays down the location requirements for i'tikaf. For men, i'tikaf must be performed in a masjid jama'ah (a mosque where congregational prayers are held). The Companion Hudhayfah (may Allah be pleased with him) stated this explicitly. Abu Hanifa further specifies that it should be a mosque where the five daily prayers are performed, because the essence of i'tikaf is waiting for the prayers, and this is best achieved in a mosque where prayer is regularly established. For women, the place of i'tikaf is the 'masjid of her house', i.e., the area designated for prayer in her home. This is because a woman's best prayer is in her home, and her waiting for prayer is realized there. If she does not have a specific prayer area, she can set aside a spot in her house for i'tikaf.

Key Terms
مَسْجِد جَمَاعَة (masjid jama'ah): A mosque in which congregational prayers are regularly held.
مَسْجِد بَيْت (masjid bayt): The prayer area designated within a home, also called the 'house mosque'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf for men is valid only in a masjid jama'ah; for women, the home prayer area suffices.

Fasting as a Condition for I'tikaf: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Disputing whether fasting is a condition for i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that fasting is a condition for i'tikaf, evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument, and state the practical difference between the schools.

Core Idea
A clear prophetic text overrides analogy: fasting is a condition for i'tikaf.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the validity of i'tikaf without fasting. The Hanafis hold that fasting is a necessary condition, while the Shafi'is argue it is an independent act of worship. We will study the textual proofs and reasoning on both sides to understand how each school derives its ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the claim: 'Fasting is a condition for i'tikaf.' Note the source of the claim in the passage.
The passage begins with 'Wa al-sawmu min shartihi indana'.
2
State the Opposing Position
Identify Imam al-Shafi'i's argument: fasting is an independent worship, so it cannot be a condition for another act.
The passage: 'Huwa yaqulu anna al-sawma ibadatun wa huwa aslun bi nafsihi.'
3
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
Examine the hadith of Aisha: 'La i'tikafa illa bi saum.' Understand why this explicit text (nass) takes precedence over qiyas.
The Hanafi claim: 'Al-qiyasu fi muqabalati al-nassi al-manquli ghayru maqbul.'
4
Evaluate the Shafi'i Proof and Hanafi Response
Consider the hadith of Ibn Umar (night i'tikaf) and the variant with 'and fast.' Understand how the Hanafis answer the objection.
The variant 'I'takif wa sum' indicates that fasting was understood even for a night vow.
5
Determine the Practical Difference (Thamarah)
Conclude the consequence: according to Hanafis, i'tikaf without fasting is invalid; according to Shafi'is, it is valid.
This affects those performing i'tikaf outside Ramadan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالصَّوْمُ مِنْ شَرْطِهِ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِيِّ هُوَ يَقُولُ أَنَّ الصَّوْمَ عِبَادَةٌ وَهُوَ أَصْلٌ بِنَفْسِهِ فَلَا يَكُونُ شَرْطًا لِغَيْرِهِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا اعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا بِالصَّوْمِ وَالْقِيَاسُ فِي مُقَابَلَةِ النَّصِّ الْمَنْقُولِ غَيْرُ مَقْبُولٍ وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا إِعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا بِصَوْمٍ وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنِّي نَذَرْتُ أَنْ أَعْتَكِفَ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ لَيْلَةً فَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَوْفِ بِنَذْرِكَ وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ فَقَالَ اعْتَكِفْ وَصُمْ
And fasting is from its conditions according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. He says: 'Fasting is an act of worship by itself and is an origin, so it cannot be a condition for another.' And we have his saying (peace be upon him): 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting.' And analogy in the face of transmitted text is not accepted. And from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) she said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting.' And from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) he said: O Messenger of Allah, I vowed to perform i'tikaf in the Sacred Mosque for a night. He (peace be upon him) said: 'Fulfill your vow.' And in one narration he said: 'Perform i'tikaf and fast.'
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on whether fasting is a condition for i'tikaf. The Hanafi school (followed also by Imam Malik) holds that fasting is a condition for the validity of i'tikaf. Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Ahmad) argue that fasting is an independent worship and cannot be a condition for another act; they also cite the hadith of Ibn Umar who vowed to perform i'tikaf for one night, which is impossible with fasting since night is not a time for fasting. The Hanafi response relies on the explicit hadith of Aisha: 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting.' This hadith is a clear text (nass) that overrides analogy (qiyas). Regarding Ibn Umar's hadith, the Hanafis note that there is a variant where the Prophet (peace be upon him) added 'and fast,' indicating that the night i'tikaf was to be accompanied by fasting during the day or that it was understood. Thus, the textual evidence supports the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
شَرْط (shart): Condition; something external that must be present for the validity of an act.
قِيَاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; deriving a ruling for a new case from an established case due to a shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof for the Hanafi position that fasting is a condition for i'tikaf?
A) Qiyas
B) Ijma'
C) The hadith 'la i'tikafa illa bi saum'
D) The hadith of Ibn Umar

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds fasting as a condition for i'tikaf based on an explicit hadith, overriding the Shafi'i use of qiyas.

Fasting as a Condition for I'tikaf: Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on fasting condition for i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that fasting is a condition for i'tikaf and evaluate the Shafi'i and Hanbali counter-arguments using textual evidence and qiyas.

Core Idea
No i'tikaf except with fasting — the Hanafi school holds this hadith decisive, but Shafi'is and Hanbalis disagree.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines a key difference between madhhabs: is fasting a condition for the validity of i'tikaf? The Hanafis, along with Malikis, say yes, while Shafi'is and Hanbalis say no. The debate hinges on the interpretation of prophetic hadiths and the role of qiyas. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi usul prioritizes explicit textual evidence over analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its conditions for i'tikaf
The passage lists four necessary elements for i'tikaf: staying in the mosque, intention, and fasting. Fasting is considered a condition (shart) for validity according to the Hanafi school.
The author explicitly says 'fasting in our view is a condition'.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proofs
Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad (Hanbali) hold that fasting is not a condition. Their proof includes qiyas (fasting is an independent worship, cannot be a condition) and hadiths where the Prophet permitted i'tikaf for a night without mentioning fasting.
They cite the hadith of Umar vowing a night i'tikaf and the Prophet saying 'Fulfill your vow'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
First, the Hanafis present direct hadith: 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting' (Aisha) and another hadith listing sunan of i'tikaf including fasting. Second, they reinterpret the opponents' hadith by noting that in other narrations, the Prophet added 'and fast' (wa sum). Third, they dismiss qiyas because it is abandoned in the face of a sound hadith.
The author states: 'Qiyas is abandoned in the face of a sound hadith'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a person performing i'tikaf without fasting – Hanafis say it is invalid (for obligatory i'tikaf), while Shafi'is say it is valid. This difference affects fatwa and practice.
5
Note the mufta bihi and intra-Hanafi variation
For obligatory i'tikaf, all Hanafi authorities agree fasting is required. For voluntary i'tikaf, the preferred position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that fasting is not a condition, but there is an opposing riwayah from Hasan ibn Ziyad.
The text references the Mabsut riwayah as the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح لغت میں اعتکاف مطلقا [؟] کا نام ہے خواہ کسی جگہ ہو اور کسی مقصد کے لئے ہو اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے ما لهذه التماثيل التى انتم لها عاكفون من کیا ہیں یہ مورتیاں جن کے پاس تم پڑے رہتے ہو اور اصطلاح شرع میں اعتکاف نام ہے اعتکاف کی نیت یعنی کے ساتھ اور روزے کے ساتھ مسجد میں قیام کرنا کو یا اعتکاف کے لئے چار چیزیں ضروری ہیں، (1 کھرنا (۲) مسجد ۳) نیت اعتکاف صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہم نا تو اعتکاف کا رکن ہے کیونکہ اعتکاف کا لفظا لبث سے معنی پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس لئے ٹھہرے رہنے شہر لغت کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے اور نیت چونکہ عادت اور عبادت کے درمیان امتیاز پیدا کرنے کے لئے تمام عبادات مقصودہ میں شرط ہے اس لئے اعتکاف کے واسطے بھی نیت شرط ہوگی تاکہ عادہ ٹھہرار بنے اور عبادت کے طور پر ٹھہرا رہنے کے درمیان امتیاز ہو جائے اور روزہ ہمارے نزدیک تو اعتکاف کی شرط ہے لیکن امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزد یک شرط نہیں ہے اس مسئلہ میں حضرت امام مالک بھی ہمارے ساتھ ہیں۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ روزہ ایک عبادت ہے اور بذات خود اصل ہے اور جو چیز خود اصل ہوتی ہے وہ دوسرے کے لئے شرط نہیں ہوتی اس لئے روزہ متکاف کے لئے شرط نہ ہوگا۔ و ان حضرات کے مذہب کی تائید صحیحین کی حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ اللَّهُ قَالَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنِّي نَذَرْتُ أَنْ اعْتَكِفَ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ لَيْلَةَ فَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ اُوفِ بِنَدْرِكَ ابن عمر نے کہا کہ اے رسول خدا ( صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم) میں نے مسجد حرام میں ایک شب کے اعتکاف کی نذر کی ہے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اپنی نذر پوری کر لو اور دار قطنی میں عبداللہ بن عمر کی حدیث ب أَنَّ عُمَرَ نَذَرَ فِى الجَاهِلِيَّةِ أنْ يَعْتَكِفَ لَيْلَةً فِى الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ فَلَمَّا كَانَ الْإِسْلَامُ سَأَلَ عَندُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَقَالَ اُوفِ بِنَدْرِكَ فَاعْتَكَفَ عُمَرُ لیلة یعنی حضرت عمر نے زمانہ جاہلیت میں مسجد حرام میں ایک شب اعتکاف کرنے کی نذر کی تھی پس جب اسلام کا عبداً گیا تو ممر نے رسول خدا سے دریافت کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ اپنی نذر پوری کرلو پس حضرت عمر نے ایک رات کا اعتکاف کیا ان دونوں حدیثوں سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ اعتکاف کے لئے روزہ شرط نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر روز و شرط ہوتا تو فقط رات کا اعتکاف کیسے درست ہوتا۔۔ ہماری دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے قَالَتْ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا إِعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا بِصَوم یعنی بغیر روزے کے اعتکاف صحیح نہیں ہے اور ابو داؤد میں ایک دوسری حدیث ہے عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ السُّنَّهُ عَلَى الْمُعْتَكِفَ أَنْ لَا يَعُودَ مَرِيضًا وَلَا يَشْهَدُ جَنَازَةً وَ لَا يَمَسُّ أَمَرَأَةٌ وَلَا يُبا يشرُهَا وَ لَا يَخْرُجُ إِلَّا لِحَاجَةٍ إِلَّا لِمَا لَا بُدَ مِنَهُ وَلَا اعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا بِصَوْمِ وَلَا اعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِدٍ جَامِع يعني مختلف پر سنت یہ ہے کہ وہ مریض کی عیادت نہ کرے اور نہ جنازہ پر حاضر ہو اور نہ عورت سے یعنی ہمبستر ہو اور نہ عورت کو مس کرے اور نہ نکلے مگر ایسی ضرورت سے کہ بغیر نکلے چارہ نہ ہو اور اعتکاف بغیر روزہ کے صحیح نہیں اور اعتکاف نہیں ہو گا مگر مسجد جامع میں ان دونوں روایتوں سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ روزہ اعتکاف کے لئے شرط ہے حضرت امام شافعی کے قیاس ان الصوم عبادة الح کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قیاس حدیث صحیح کے مقابلہ میں متروک ہوتا ہے اس لئے حدیث ما نشہ لَا إِعْتِكَافَ إِلَّا بِصَوم کے متقابلہ میں امام شافعی کے قیاس کو ترک کر دیا جائے گا اور عبد اللہ بن عمر کی حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث کو ابوداؤد، نسائی اور دار قطنی نے ان الفاظ کے ساتھ روایت کیا ہے اُن عُمر جَعَلَ عَلى نفسه أن يعتكف فِي الْجَاهليَةِ لَيْلَةً أَوْ يَوْمًا عِندَ الْكَعْبَةِ فَسَأَلَ البيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ اعْتَكِف وصم یعنی حضرت عمر نے جاہلیت کے زمانہ میں ایک رات یا ایک دن کا مسجد حرام میں اعتکاف اپنے اوپر لازم کیا تھا پھر حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے دریافت کیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اعتکاف کر اور روزہ رکھ اس حدیث میں اگر لیلۃ کا لفظ ہے تو مطلب یہ ہے کہ رات کا اعتکاف اس کے دن کے ساتھ لازم کیا تھا اور اگر یوما کا لفظ ہے تو مطلب یہ ہے کہ دن کا اعتکاف رات کے ساتھ لازم کیا تھا بہر حال اس حدیث میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اعتکاف کے ساتھ روز و رھنے کا امر بھی فرمایا ہے اس لئے اس سے بھی روزہ کا شرط اعتکاف ہونا ثابت ہوگا۔
In linguistic terminology, i'tikaf is the name for staying absolutely, whether in any place and for any purpose. Allah Ta'ala said: 'What are these images to which you are devoted?' (21:52). And in Islamic legal terminology, i'tikaf is the name for staying in the mosque with the intention of i'tikaf and with fasting. For i'tikaf, four things are necessary: (1) staying, (2) mosque, (3) intention of i'tikaf, (4) fasting. Sahib Hidayah says: Staying is a rukn of i'tikaf because the word i'tikaf linguistically indicates the meaning of staying, so staying must be present. Intention is a condition in all intended acts of worship to distinguish between habit and worship, so for i'tikaf intention is a condition. Fasting in our view is a condition for i'tikaf, but Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad do not consider it a condition. In this matter, Imam Malik is with us. The proof of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad is that fasting is an act of worship and is originally an end in itself, and what is an end in itself cannot be a condition for something else, so fasting is not a condition for i'tikaf. Their school is also supported by hadith in the Sahihain: from Ibn Umar (ra) who said: O Messenger of Allah, I have vowed to perform i'tikaf in the Sacred Mosque for one night. He (saw) said: Fulfill your vow. And in Dar Qutni: that Umar vowed in the Jahiliyyah to perform i'tikaf for one night in the Sacred Mosque. When he became Muslim, he asked the Prophet (saw), and he said: Fulfill your vow. So Umar performed i'tikaf for one night. These hadiths show that fasting is not a condition for i'tikaf, because if fasting were a condition, how could i'tikaf at night alone be valid? Our proof is the hadith of Aisha (ra): The Messenger of Allah (saw) said: 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting.' And in Abu Dawud there is another hadith: from Aisha (ra) who said: The sunnah for the mu'takif is that he should not visit a sick person, nor attend a funeral, nor touch his wife, nor have intimate relations with her, nor go out except for a necessity that cannot be avoided; and there is no i'tikaf except with fasting, and there is no i'tikaf except in a congregational mosque. These two narrations prove that fasting is a condition for i'tikaf. The response to Imam Shafi'i's qiyas (that fasting is a pure act of worship) is that qiyas is abandoned in the face of a sound hadith. So the hadith 'la i'tikafa illa bi-sawm' takes precedence, and the qiyas of Imam Shafi'i is set aside. The response to the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar is that this hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, and Dar Qutni with these words: 'Umar made obligatory upon himself to perform i'tikaf in the Jahiliyyah for a night or a day at the Ka'bah, then he asked the Prophet (saw), and he said: Perform i'tikaf and fast.' That is, Umar had obligated upon himself i'tikaf in the Sacred Mosque for a night or a day. Then he asked the Prophet (saw), and he (saw) said: Perform i'tikaf and fast. In this hadith, if the word 'laylah' appears, it means he obligated i'tikaf of the night along with its day; if the word 'yawm' appears, it means he obligated i'tikaf of the day along with its night. In any case, in this hadith the Prophet (saw) commanded fasting along with i'tikaf, so it also proves that fasting is a condition for i'tikaf.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute regarding the condition of fasting for i'tikaf. The author begins by defining i'tikaf linguistically and technically, then lists its four essential elements: staying in the mosque, intention, and fasting. He explains that staying is a rukn because the word itself implies it, and intention is a condition to distinguish worship from habit. The core dispute: Hanafis (along with Imam Malik) hold that fasting is a condition (shart) for i'tikaf, while Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold it is not. The opponents argue that fasting is an independent act of worship and cannot be a condition for another. They support their view with hadiths showing that the Prophet permitted i'tikaf for a night without mention of fasting. The Hanafi response: first, they present direct evidence from Aisha (ra) that the Prophet (saw) said 'There is no i'tikaf except with fasting' and another hadith listing sunan of i'tikaf including fasting. Second, they rebut the opponents' qiyas by stating that qiyas is abandoned when it contradicts a sound hadith. Third, they reinterpret the opponents' hadith by noting that in other narrations, the Prophet added 'and fast' to the command, indicating that the night i'tikaf was assumed to include the day or the day included the night, thus requiring fasting. The passage follows the typical Hidayah style: present the base ruling, state the ikhtilaf, give opponents' evidence, then provide Hanafi evidence and rebuttals.

Key Terms
اعتکاف (i'tikaf): Linguistically: staying in a place. Technically: staying in the mosque with intention and fasting for the purpose of worship.
روزہ (sawm): Fasting from dawn to sunset with intention.
شرط (shart): A condition that must be present for the act to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on fasting in relation to i'tikaf?
A) Fasting is a condition (shart) for obligatory i'tikaf but not for voluntary i'tikaf according to the preferred view.
B) Fasting is not required for any i'tikaf.
C) Fasting is a mere sunnah for i'tikaf.
D) Fasting is a pillar (rukn) of i'tikaf.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires fasting as a condition for obligatory i'tikaf, based on the explicit hadith 'La i'tikafa illa bi-sawm', while Shafi'is and Hanbalis do not require it, but the ikhtilaf is legitimate and rooted in different usul principles.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Fasting for Voluntary I'tikaf
Explains the two riwayat on fasting for nafl i'tikaf and their consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on fasting for nafl i'tikaf, identify the mufta bihi, and apply the rule to determine validity and qada' of a broken voluntary i'tikaf.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school has two transmitted views on nafl i'tikaf: the stronger (Zahir al-Riwayah) does not require fasting; the weaker requires it and a minimum of one day.

In this passage, we explore an internal disagreement within the Hanafi school about whether fasting is a condition for voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf. While all Hanafis agree that obligatory i'tikaf (vowed) requires fasting, they differ on voluntary i'tikaf. The two transmitted views lead to different practical rulings on the minimum duration and the necessity of qada' if broken. Understanding this dispute helps us appreciate how the school weighs conflicting transmissions and why the ruling of ease is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two riwayat
First, find the two transmitted positions: one from Hasan ibn Ziyad (narrating from Abu Hanifa) and the other from al-Mabsut (Zahir al-Riwayah, the saying of the Imams). Note what each says about fasting as a condition for nafl i'tikaf.
The passage explicitly calls the second 'Zahir al-Riwayah' and 'the saying of the Imams', indicating its higher authority.
2
Examine the dalil for each position
The first position relies on the absolute hadith 'la i'tikafa illa bi-sawm' with no distinction between obligatory and voluntary. The second position uses qiyas: just as nafl prayer can be performed sitting for ease, nafl i'tikaf requires no fixed duration or fasting.
The qiyas is based on the principle that voluntary acts are built on ease (al-nafl mabnī 'alā al-suhūlah).
3
Note the practical consequence: qada'
If someone begins a nafl i'tikaf and then breaks it, the first riwayah requires qada' because a minimum day is fixed and breaking it invalidates the act. The second riwayah requires no qada' because no specific time is fixed; breaking is merely leaving the act incomplete.
This difference directly affects the mufti's ruling in such cases.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage explicitly states that the position of al-Mabsut is Zahir al-Riwayah and 'the saying of the Imams'. Therefore, the operative ruling (mufta bihi) is that fasting is not a condition and no minimum duration is required.
The authority_weight is 'zahir_riwayah', which is the highest level in the school.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a person who enters the mosque intending nafl i'tikaf for one hour, according to the mufta bihi, this is valid without fasting. If he leaves after 30 minutes, no qada' is required.
Contrast with the other riwayah: if followed, the same act would be invalid unless he fasts and stays a full day.

صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اعتکاف واجب کے لئے با تفاق روایات روزہ شرط ہے یعنی تمام علماء احناف اس پر متفق ہیں کہ اعتکاف واجب کے لئے روزہ رکھنا شرط ہے اعتکاف واجب کی صورت یہ ہے کہ کسی نے ایک ماہ یا ایک دن گزارے گا اعتکاف کہلائے گا خواہ دو ایک ساعت ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نفل کا مدار سہولت اور آسانی پر ہے چنانچہ آپ ملاحظہ کیجئے کہ نماز میں قیام فرض ہے لیکن نفل نماز قدرت علی القیام کے باوجود اگر روایتوں کے درمیان شمر و اختلاف ظاہر کرنے کے لئے فرمایا کہ اگر کسی نے نفلی اعتکاف شروع کیا اور پھر اس کو قطع کیا تو مبسوط کی روایت کے مطابق اس پر قضالا زم نہ ہوگی کیونکہ نفلی اعتکاف کا کوئی وقت مقدر نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ قطع کرنا باطل کرنانہ ہوگا بلکہ پورا کرنا ہوگا اور کسی چیز کو پورا کرنے کی صورت میں اس کی قضا واجب نہیں ہوتی اور حسن بن زیاد کی روایت کے مطابق اس پر قضا لازم ہوگی کیونکہ اس روایت کے مطابق نفل اعتکاف کم از کم ایک دن کے ساتھ مقدر ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ روزہ ایک دن کا ہوتا ہے پس جب اس نے ایک دن پورا ہونے سے پہلے اس کو قطع کر دیا تو یہ باطل کرتا ہوا۔ اور نفلی عبادت کو اگر پورا ہونے سے پہلے فاسد کر دیا جائے تو اس کی قضا لازم ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس روایت کے مطابق اس پر بھی اعتکاف کی قضا لا زم ہوگی ۔
Sahib Hidayah says: For obligatory i'tikaf, fasting is a condition by unanimous riwayat, meaning all Hanafi scholars agree that for obligatory i'tikaf, fasting is a condition. The form of obligatory i'tikaf is when someone vows to perform i'tikaf for a month or a day, or says: if my work is accomplished, I have i'tikaf for such a period. Regarding the validity of voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf, there are two riwayat on whether fasting is a condition. One riwayah, which Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam A'zam (Abu Hanifa), is that fasting is also a condition for nafl i'tikaf, because the hadith 'la i'tikafa illa bi-sawm' is absolute, with no distinction between obligatory and voluntary; rather, fasting is necessary for every type of i'tikaf. But note that according to this riwayah, nafl i'tikaf cannot be less than one day, because fasting is a condition and fasting is not possible for less than a day. The second riwayah is from al-Mabsut, and this is Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is the saying of the Imams (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn): fasting is not a condition for voluntary i'tikaf. According to this riwayah, no specific duration is set for voluntary i'tikaf; rather, whatever time one spends in the mosque with the intention of i'tikaf counts as i'tikaf, even if it is only two or one hour. The proof is that voluntary acts are based on ease and facility. For example, in prayer, standing is obligatory, but if one performs voluntary prayer sitting even though able to stand, it is permissible. From this we understand that voluntary acts are based on ease, and ease lies in not fixing a duration for i'tikaf. Therefore we say that no specific time is fixed for voluntary i'tikaf. To show the difference between the two riwayat, it is said: if someone begins voluntary i'tikaf and then breaks it, according to the riwayah of al-Mabsut, no qada' is obligatory upon him, because no specific time is fixed; breaking it does not invalidate it, rather one should complete it, and when something is completed, qada' is not required. According to the riwayah of Hasan ibn Ziyad, qada' is obligatory because according to that riwayah, voluntary i'tikaf is fixed at a minimum of one day, like fasting is one day. So if he breaks it before completing a day, he has invalidated it, and if a voluntary worship is invalidated before completion, qada' becomes obligatory. Therefore, according to that riwayah, qada' of i'tikaf is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of fasting for voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf. The author first confirms that for obligatory i'tikaf (i.e., i'tikaf due to a vow), all Hanafis agree fasting is a condition. The dispute is only about nafl i'tikaf. Two riwayat (narrations) are cited: (1) From Hasan ibn Ziyad, reporting from Abu Hanifa, that fasting is required for nafl i'tikaf as well, based on the absolute wording of the hadith. Consequently, nafl i'tikaf must be at least one full day because fasting cannot be less than a day. (2) From al-Mabsut (which is Zahir al-Riwayah and the view of the Imams), fasting is not a condition for nafl i'tikaf. Thus, no minimum duration is required; even a short stay with intention counts. The reasoning for the second view is that voluntary acts are based on ease (suhulat), analogizing to permissible sitting in nafl prayer. The practical consequence: if one breaks nafl i'tikaf after starting it, according to the first riwayah, qada' is required because a minimum duration was prescribed and broken; according to the second, no qada' is needed. The passage clarifies that the preferred view (mufta bihi) is the one from al-Mabsut (Zahir al-Riwayah), which does not require fasting or a minimum time for nafl i'tikaf.

Key Terms
نفلی اعتکاف (nafli i'tikaf): Voluntary i'tikaf performed without any vow; it is recommended but not obligatory.
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, recorded by Imam Muhammad in six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of breaking a voluntary i'tikaf according to the riwayah of Hasan ibn Ziyad?
A) No qada' is required.
B) Qada' is required.
C) The i'tikaf is still valid.
D) The person must repeat from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi is that voluntary i'tikaf does not require fasting and has no minimum duration, based on the principle of ease for voluntary acts.

Condition of a Congregational Mosque for I'tikaf
States a condition of validity for i'tikaf with two proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the validity of i'tikaf regarding the mosque, and identify the two proofs that support it.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is only valid in a congregational mosque (masjid jama'ah) — the hadith of Hudhayfah and Ibn Abbas' condemnation of i'tikaf in non-congregational mosques as bid'ah.

This passage establishes a key condition for the validity of i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school: the mosque must be a congregational mosque (masjid jama'ah) where the five daily prayers are held in congregation. The author supports this with two proofs: a hadith of Hudhayfah and a statement of Ibn Abbas. Understanding this condition is essential for performing i'tikaf correctly, as doing it in an unsuitable mosque renders the act invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Read the first part of the passage where the condition is stated: the mosque must be a 'masjid jama'ah' (congregational mosque). Note the explanation that this means a mosque with an imam, mu'adhdhin, and regular congregational prayers.
This is a condition of validity (shart al-jawaz), not merely a recommendation.
2
Examine the first proof (hadith of Hudhayfah)
The author cites the hadith 'La i'tikafa illa fi masjid jama'ah'. Analyze the linguistic structure: negation (la) followed by exception (illa) indicates exclusivity. This proves that i'tikaf is only valid in a congregational mosque.
This is a hadith ahad (single-narrator) and is zanni al-thubut, but it is accepted as evidence by the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the second proof (statement of Ibn Abbas)
Ibn Abbas states that i'tikaf in 'mosques in houses' is a bid'ah (innovation). This demonstrates that such practice is detestable and should be avoided. It reinforces the requirement that i'tikaf be in a properly established congregational mosque.
This is a qawl sahabi (saying of a Companion), which Hanafis treat as a proof when not contradicted by a stronger evidence.
4
Understand the legal implication
From these two proofs, the Hanafi school derives that i'tikaf in a mosque that does not hold regular congregational prayers (e.g., a small family musalla) is invalid. If someone performs i'tikaf there, they must repeat it if it was a vowed (nadhr) i'tikaf.
The ruling applies to both regular (sunnah) i'tikaf and votive i'tikaf.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school does not require i'tikaf to be in a congregational mosque; any mosque (including small ones) suffices. They consider the hadith of Hudhayfah as weak or interpret it differently.
This is a point of legitimate ikhtilaf (اختلاف) between the schools.

Source Text

اعتکاف کی شروط جواز میں سے مسجد جماعت کا ہونا بھی ہے یعنی اعتکاف اس مسجد میں صحیح ہو گا جس میں امام اور موذن کا نظم ہو اور پانچوں نمازیں جماعت سے ادا کی جائیں یا بعض نماز میں جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کی جائیں اس کی دلیل حضرت حذیفہ کی حدیث الْإِعْتِكَافُ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِد جَمَاعَةٍ ہے اور ابن عباس کا قول ہے إِنَّ أَبْغَضَ الأمُورِ إِلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى الْبَدَعُ وَ إِنَّ مِنَ الْبَدَعِ الإعْتِكَافُ فِى الْمَسَاجِدِ الَّتِي فِي الدُّورِ یعنی اللہ تعالی کے نزدیک مبغوض ترین چیز بدعتیں ہیں اور بدعتوں میں سے ان مساجد میں اعتکاف کرنا بھی ہے جو گھروں میں ہیں ان دونوں روایتوں سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ اعتکاف کے لئے ایسی مسجد کا ہونا ضروری
Among the conditions of validity (shurut al-jawaz) for i'tikaf is that the mosque is a congregational mosque (masjid jama'ah). That is, i'tikaf is valid only in a mosque where there is an imam and a mu'adhdhin, and all five prayers are performed in congregation, or at least some prayers are performed in congregation. Its proof is the hadith of Hudhayfah: 'There is no i'tikaf except in a congregational mosque.' And the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'Verily, the most detestable of matters to Allah Almighty are innovations (bida'), and among innovations is performing i'tikaf in the mosques that are in houses.' That is, the most detestable thing to Allah is innovations, and among innovations is performing i'tikaf in mosques that are in homes. These two narrations show that for i'tikaf, it is necessary to have such a mosque.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage states a condition of validity (shart al-jawaz) for i'tikaf: the mosque must be a congregational mosque (masjid jama'ah). The author explains that this means a mosque where there is an organized imam and mu'adhdhin, and where the five daily prayers are performed in congregation, or at least some of them. The evidence comes from two sources: (1) The hadith of Hudhayfah (ra) that 'There is no i'tikaf except in a congregational mosque.' (2) The statement of Ibn Abbas (ra) that i'tikaf in small mosques inside houses is a bid'ah (innovation). From these, it is concluded that i'tikaf should be performed in a proper congregational mosque, not in a small mosque that does not hold regular congregational prayers. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may have different conditions regarding the mosque.

Key Terms
مسجد جماعت (masjid jama'ah): A mosque where the five daily prayers are held in congregation with a regular imam and mu'adhdhin.
بدعت (bid'ah): An innovation in religion; i'tikaf in a non-congregational mosque is considered a bid'ah by Ibn Abbas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) A mosque with a minbar.

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is only valid in a congregational mosque (masjid jama'ah), supported by the hadith of Hudhayfah and the statement of Ibn Abbas.

Fasting as a Condition for I'tikaf: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fasting condition for nafl i'tikaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting as a condition for wajib and nafl i'tikaf and explain the two narrations regarding nafl i'tikaf, including their proofs and practical consequences.

Core Idea
For wajib i'tikaf, fasting is required by consensus; for nafl, the relied-upon view does not require fasting.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Is fasting a condition for the validity of voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf? While all Hanafi scholars agree that obligatory (wajib) i'tikaf requires fasting, two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa differ on nafl i'tikaf. Understanding this dispute helps you apply the correct ruling in practice and appreciate how the school resolves differences using principles like ease (taysir) and authoritative transmission (zahir al-riwayah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of i'tikaf
Distinguish between wajib i'tikaf (arising from a vow) and nafl i'tikaf (voluntary). Note the consensus on the former.
2
State the two narrations on nafl i'tikaf
Narration 1 (via Hasan ibn Ziyad): fasting is required. Narration 2 (zahir al-riwayah): fasting is not required.
The second narration is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa himself and is found in al-Mabsut.
3
Examine the proofs of each narration
Narration 1 cites the absolute hadith 'No i'tikaf except with fasting'. Narration 2 uses qiyas: nafl acts are based on ease, analogizing to nafl prayer that can be performed sitting.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala, leaving room for interpretation.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The author of al-Hidayah declares the second narration as zahir al-riwayah and the Imam's own saying, thus it is the relied-upon position.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to the first narration, nafl i'tikaf must be at least one day with fasting, and breaking it requires qada. According to the second, no minimum duration and no qada upon breaking.
This difference affects daily practice for those performing voluntary i'tikaf.

مطابق روزہ شرط ہے اور روزہ ایک یوم سے کم میں ممکن نہیں ہے۔ دوسری روایت مبسوط کی ہے اور یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے اور یہی امام قول ہے کہ نفلی اعتکاف کے لئے روزہ شرط نہیں ہے اس روایت کی بناء پر نفلی اعتکاف کے لئے کوئی وقت مقدر نہیں ہے بلکہ اعتکاف کی نیت سے جتنا وقت مسجد میں گزارے گا اعتکاف کہلائے گا خواہ دو ایک ساعت ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ نفل کا مدار سہولت اور آسانی پر ہے چنانچہ آپ ملاحظہ کیجئے کہ نماز میں قیام فرض ہے لیکن نفل نماز قدرت علی القیام کے باوجود اگر بیٹھ کر ادا کی تو جائز ہے بس اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفل کا مبنی سہولت اور آسانی پر ہے اور سہولت اعتکاف کی وقت مقدر نہ کرنے میں ہے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ نفلی اعتکاف کے لئے کوئی وقت مقدر نہیں ہے۔ دونوں روایتوں کے درمیان شمر و اختلاف ظاہر کرنے کے لئے فرمایا کہ اگر کسی نے نفلی اعتکاف شروع کیا اور پھر اس کو قطع کیا تو مبسوط کی روایت کے مطابق اس پر قضالا زم نہ ہوگی کیونکہ نفلی اعتکاف کا کوئی وقت مقدر نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ قطع کرنا باطل کرنانہ ہوگا بلکہ پورا کرنا ہوگا اور کسی چیز کو پورا کرنے کی صورت میں اس کی قضا واجب نہیں ہوتی اور حسن بن زیاد کی روایت کے مطابق اس پر قضا لازم ہوگی کیونکہ اس روایت کے مطابق نفل اعتکاف کم از کم ایک دن کے ساتھ مقدر ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ روزہ ایک دن کا ہوتا ہے پس جب اس نے ایک دن پورا ہونے سے پہلے اس کو قطع کر دیا تو یہ باطل کرتا ہوا۔ اور نفلی عبادت کو اگر پورا ہونے سے پہلے فاسد کر دیا جائے تو اس کی قضا لازم ہوتی
ہے اس لئے اس روایت کے مطابق اس پر بھی اعتکاف کی قضا لا زم ہوگی ۔
He had made i'tikaf obligatory upon himself, then he asked the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Perform i'tikaf and fast.' In this hadith, if the word 'laylah' (night) is used, it means that the i'tikaf of the night was linked to its day; if the word 'yawm' (day) is used, it means that the i'tikaf of the day was linked to its night. In any case, in this hadith the Prophet (peace be upon him) also commanded fasting along with i'tikaf, so from this too it is established that fasting is a condition for i'tikaf. The author of Hidayah says: For obligatory i'tikaf, fasting is a condition according to all narrations, meaning all Hanafi scholars agree that fasting is a condition for obligatory i'tikaf. The case of obligatory i'tikaf is when someone vows to perform i'tikaf for a month or a day, or says, 'If this work of mine is accomplished, I owe i'tikaf for such and such period.' Regarding whether fasting is a condition for the validity of voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf, there are two narrations: One narration, which Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam A'zam, is that fasting is a condition for nafl i'tikaf as well, because the hadith 'No i'tikaf except with fasting' is absolute, with no distinction between obligatory and voluntary; rather, fasting is necessary for every kind of i'tikaf. But note that according to this narration, nafl i'tikaf cannot be less than one day because fasting is a condition for nafl i'tikaf and fasting is not possible in less than one day. The second narration is from al-Mabsut, and this is the zahir al-riwayah, and it is the Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) own saying, that fasting is not a condition for nafl i'tikaf. According to this narration, no specific time is prescribed for nafl i'tikaf; rather, whatever time one spends in the mosque with the intention of i'tikaf will be considered i'tikaf, even if it is only an hour or two. The proof is that nafl acts are based on ease and convenience. For example, in prayer, standing is obligatory, but if one performs a nafl prayer sitting even though able to stand, it is permissible. From this we understand that nafl is based on ease and convenience, and ease lies in not prescribing a specific time for i'tikaf. Therefore we said that no specific time is prescribed for nafl i'tikaf. To show the difference between the two narrations, it is said: if someone begins a nafl i'tikaf and then breaks it, according to the narration of al-Mabsut, qada (making it up) is not obligatory upon him because there is no prescribed time for nafl i'tikaf, so breaking it is not invalidating it; rather, completing it would be required, and qada is not obligatory when something is completed. According to the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad, qada would be obligatory because according to this narration, nafl i'tikaf is prescribed to be at least one day, just as fasting is for a day. So when he breaks it before completing the day, he has invalidated it. And if a voluntary act of worship is invalidated before completion, its qada becomes obligatory; therefore according to this narration, qada of i'tikaf is obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether fasting is a condition for nafl (voluntary) i'tikaf. The author first establishes that for wajib (obligatory) i'tikaf, all Hanafi scholars agree that fasting is a condition. Obligatory i'tikaf arises from a vow (nazar). For nafl i'tikaf, there are two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa: one via Hasan ibn Ziyad requiring fasting, and the second (the zahir al-riwayah, relied-upon) not requiring fasting. The zahir al-riwayah is preferred because nafl acts are based on ease, as demonstrated by the analogy with nafl prayer (which can be performed sitting). The practical consequence: if one breaks a nafl i'tikaf, according to the first narration qada is required (since it must be at least one day with fasting), whereas according to the second narration no qada is required since no minimum duration is prescribed. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the second narration.

Key Terms
اعتکاف (i'tikaf): Spiritual retreat in a mosque with the intention of worship.
صوم (sawm): Fasting, abstaining from food, drink, and sexual relations from dawn to sunset.
ظاہر الروایۃ (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known, authoritative narrations from the founding imams, transmitted in the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is fasting a condition for the validity of voluntary (nafl) i'tikaf?
A) Yes, according to all narrations.
B) No, according to the relied-upon narration (zahir al-riwayah).
C) Yes, but only if the i'tikaf is for less than one day.
D) No, because nafl i'tikaf is not valid at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between wajib and nafl i'tikaf: fasting is a condition for the former by consensus, but for the latter the relied-upon view does not require it.
