Condition of the Mosque for I'tikaf
States that i'tikaf must be performed in a mosque where congregational prayers are held.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the mosque in i'tikaf and explain the inter-madhhab dispute over its validity.

Core Idea
I'tikaf requires a mosque with congregation – the Hanafi position is stricter than the absolute permission of other schools.

One of the key conditions for a valid i'tikaf is the type of mosque in which it is performed. The Hanafi school places a specific requirement that the mosque has a regular congregation, while other schools allow any mosque. This lesson unpacks the evidence and reasoning behind the Hanafi position and the contrasting views.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the condition as stated in the passage: i'tikaf must be in a 'masjid jama'ah' (a mosque with regular congregation, imam, and muadhdhin).
Note that there is a stricter narration from Abu Hanifa requiring all five prayers, but the relied-upon view is the more general condition.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), Imam Malik, and Imam Shafi'i hold that i'tikaf is valid in any mosque, regardless of congregation.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opposing schools rely on the absolute wording of Quran 2:187: 'while you are staying in the mosques' (mutlaq).
In Hanafi usul, a mutlaq text must be specified if there is evidence; here they do not see the need.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by citing the hadith of Hudhayfah (the exception 'except in a mosque of congregation') and the saying of Ibn Abbas condemning i'tikaf in house-mosques as bid'ah. I'tikaf is worship of waiting for prayer, so it should be in a place where prayer is offered.
This is an application of takhsis al-mutlaq (specification of the absolute).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to the Hanafi view, i'tikaf in a mosque without congregation is invalid; according to the opposing view, it is valid.
The passage does not explicitly tarjih, but the general Hanafi position (masjid jama'ah) is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتکاف کی شروط جواز میں سے مسجد جماعت کا ہونا بھی ہے یعنی اعتکاف اس مسجد میں صحیح ہو گا جس میں امام اور موذن کا نظم ہو اور پانچوں نمازیں جماعت سے ادا کی جائیں یا بعض نماز میں جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کی جائیں اس کی دلیل حضرت حذیفہ کی حدیث الْإِعْتِكَافُ إِلَّا فِي مَسْجِد جَمَاعَةٍ ہے اور ابن عباس کا قول ہے إِنَّ أَبْغَضَ الأمُورِ إِلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى الْبَدَعُ وَ إِنَّ مِنَ الْبَدَعِ الإعْتِكَافُ فِى الْمَسَاجِدِ الَّتِي فِي الدُّورِ یعنی اللہ تعالی کے نزدیک مبغوض ترین چیز بدعتیں ہیں اور بدعتوں میں سے ان مساجد میں اعتکاف کرنا بھی ہے جو گھروں میں ہیں ان دونوں روایتوں سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ اعتکاف کے لئے ایسی مسجد کا ہونا ضروری ہو جس میں باجماعت نماز ادا کی جاتی ہو اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ صحت اعتکاف کے لئے ایسی مسجد کا ہونا شرط ہے میں پانچوں نمازیں جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کی جاتی ہوں یہیں امام احمد کا قول ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتکاف نماز کے انتظار کی عبادت ہے پس عبادت اعتکاف ایسی جگہ کے ساتھ مختص ہو گی جہاں نماز ادا کی جاتی ہو یعنی ہر نماز ادا کی جاتی ہو۔ اور صاحبین اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ہر مسجد میں اعتکاف کرنا صحیح ہے خواہ اس میں جماعت کے ساتھ نماز ہوتی ہو یا جماعت کے ساتھ نماز نہ ہوتی ہو ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول وانتُمْ عَاكِفُونَ فِى الْمَسَاجِدِ مطلق ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے شرح طحاوی کے حوالہ سے تحریر کیا ہے کہ سب سے افضل اعتکاف مسجد حرام میں ہے پھر مسجد نبوی میں پھر مسجد اقصیٰ میں پھر ان بڑی مساجد میں جن میں لوگ زیادہ سے زیادہ آتے ہوں ۔
Among the conditions of permissibility for i'tikaf is that it be in a mosque with congregation (masjid jama'ah). That is, i'tikaf will be valid in a mosque that has an imam and a muadhdhin, and where all five prayers are offered in congregation, or at least some prayers are offered in congregation. The proof is the hadith of Hudhayfah: 'There is no i'tikaf except in a mosque of congregation,' and the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'The most hateful things to Allah are innovations, and among the innovations is performing i'tikaf in the mosques that are in houses.' These two reports show that for i'tikaf, a mosque is necessary where congregational prayer is held. And from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that for the validity of i'tikaf, it is a condition that the mosque is one where all five prayers are offered in congregation. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad. The proof is that i'tikaf is the worship of waiting for prayer; therefore the worship of i'tikaf will be specific to a place where prayer is offered, i.e., where every prayer is offered. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), Imam Malik, and Imam Shafi'i, i'tikaf in any mosque is valid, whether prayers are offered in congregation there or not. Their proof is the saying of Allah: '...while you are staying in the mosques' (al-Baqarah 2:187), which is absolute. The author of 'Inayah, citing Sharh al-Tahawi, wrote that the most excellent i'tikaf is in Masjid al-Haram, then in Masjid al-Nabawi, then in Masjid al-Aqsa, then in large mosques where many people come.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the condition of the mosque for i'tikaf. It first states the general Hanafi condition: i'tikaf must be in a 'masjid jama'ah,' a mosque with a regular congregation (imam and muadhdhin) where prayers are offered in congregation. This is supported by a hadith from Hudhayfah and a saying of Ibn Abbas. Then it presents a stricter narration from Imam Abu Hanifa (and also Imam Ahmad) requiring all five prayers in congregation. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), along with Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, hold that any mosque is valid, relying on the absolute Quranic verse (2:187). The passage does not explicitly prefer one, but the general condition (masjid jama'ah) is the understood Hanafi position. Finally, it ranks the best mosques for i'tikaf: Haram, Nabawi, Aqsa, then large mosques.

Key Terms
مسجد جماعت (masjid jama'ah): A mosque where congregational prayers are regularly held, with an imam and muadhdhin.
بدعت (bid'ah): An innovation in religion, disliked by Allah according to Ibn Abbas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where is i'tikaf valid?
A) In any mosque, regardless of congregation.
B) Only in Masjid al-Haram.
C) In a mosque where congregational prayers are held (masjid jama'ah).
D) Only in mosques with all five prayers in congregation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a mosque with a regular congregation (masjid jama'ah) for i'tikaf; a lone mosque without congregation is not sufficient.

Women's I'tikaf: Home Prayer Area vs. Mosque
Ruling that for women, the preferred i'tikaf is in their home prayer space, not the mosque.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on women's i'tikaf and explain why the home prayer area is preferred, using the Hanafi proof based on the definition of i'tikaf.

Core Idea
For women, i'tikaf at home is not just valid but better—her home prayer area is her mosque.

This passage addresses a key point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: where a woman should perform i'tikaf. In many communities, women may feel inclined to go to the mosque for i'tikaf, but the Hanafi school teaches that the home prayer area (masjid al-bayt) is actually superior. Understanding the reasoning behind this ruling will help you appreciate how the schools derive rulings from the same essential concept of i'tikaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling for women's i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school: what is the preferred place? What does 'afdal' mean here?
The text explicitly says 'afdal' (better), not obligatory.
2
Identify the opponent's position
Who disagreed (Imam al-Shafi'i), and what is his ruling? Does he permit i'tikaf in the home mosque for men or women?
Shafi'i rules that i'tikaf is only valid in a shari'i mosque for both genders.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is the Shafi'i proof? How does he argue that i'tikaf must be in a venerated place?
The Shafi'i proof is that i'tikaf requires honoring the place, which only a legal mosque provides.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut this? What is their key proof based on the definition of i'tikaf?
Hanafi defines i'tikaf as waiting for prayer; a woman waits at home, so her home prayer area is her mosque.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in ruling? How does this affect a woman's i'tikaf in real life?
Hanafi: valid at home (afdal); Shafi'i: invalid at home (must go to a mosque).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور عورت کے لئے ہمارے نزدیک افضل یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے گھر کی مسجد میں اعتکاف کرے یعنی گھر میں نماز کے لئے جو جگہ مقرر کر رکھی ہے اس میں اعتکاف کرنا عورت کے لئے افضل ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ مردوں اور عورتوں دونوں کے لئے مسجد جماعت میں اعتکاف کرنا جائز ہے گھر کی مسجد میں اعتکاف کرنا نہ مرد کے لئے جائز ہی اور نہ عورت کے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود اعتکاف زمین کے اس حصہ کی تعظیم ہے جس میں اعتکاف کیا جائے گا پس اعتکاف اس حصہ کے ساتھ مختص ہو گا جو شرعا بھی معظم و مکرم ہو اور شرعا مساجد تو معظم ہوتی ہیں مگر گھروں میں جو جگہ نماز پڑھنے کے لئے مقرر کر لی گی وہ اس درجہ معظم نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اعتکاف فقط مساجد کے اندر جائز ہوگا اور غیر مساجد یعنی مساجد بیوت میں جائز نہ ہوگا ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہم نے سابق میں کہا ہے کہ اعتکاف نماز کے انتظار کی عبادت ہے اور عورت مسجد بیت میں نماز کا انتظار کرتی ہے نہ کہ شرعی مساجد میں پس جب مسجد بیت میں انتظار صلوۃ کرتی ہے تو ا پیکاف بھی اسی میں کرے گا۔ اور اگر گھر میں نماز کے لئے کوئی جگہ مقرر نہ ہو تو کوئی ایک جگہ مقرر کر کے اس میں ایکاف کرلے۔
And for a woman, according to us, the better (afdal) is that she perform i'tikaf in the mosque of her house, i.e., in the place she has set aside for prayer in her home. Imam Shafi'i said that for both men and women, it is permissible to perform i'tikaf in a congregational mosque; i'tikaf in the home mosque is neither permissible for men nor women. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the purpose of i'tikaf is to honor the portion of land in which one performs i'tikaf. Therefore i'tikaf is specific to that portion which is legally honorable and venerated. Legally, mosques are venerated, but the place set aside for prayer in the home does not have that degree of veneration. Hence i'tikaf is only permissible inside mosques, not in other places, i.e., not in home mosques. Our proof is that we have previously said that i'tikaf is the worship of waiting for prayer, and a woman waits for prayer in her home mosque, not in the legal mosques. So since she waits for prayer in the home mosque, she will also perform i'tikaf there. And if there is no specific place for prayer in the home, she should designate a place and perform i'tikaf there.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the place of i'tikaf for women. The Hanafi position: it is superior (afdal) for a woman to perform i'tikaf in her home prayer area (masjid al-bayt), not in the congregational mosque. Imam Shafi'i holds that i'tikaf is only valid in a legal mosque (masjid in the shari'i sense), whether for men or women. The Shafi'i proof is that i'tikaf requires honoring the place, and only a shari'i mosque has that honor. The Hanafi response: i'tikaf is essentially waiting for prayer, and a woman waits for prayer in her home prayer area, so that place serves as her mosque for i'tikaf. If she has no designated prayer spot, she should set one aside and perform i'tikaf there.

Key Terms
مسجد بیت (masjid al-bayt): The area in a home designated for prayer, which functions as a mosque for women.
افضل (afdal): Better, more excellent, not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where is it afdal (better) for a woman to perform i'tikaf?
A) In a congregational mosque with jama'ah.
B) In her home prayer area (masjid al-bayt).
C) Only in Masjid al-Haram.
D) Anywhere she sits, even if not designated.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a woman's home prayer area is her mosque for i'tikaf, making home-based i'tikaf not only valid but superior.

Exiting I'tikaf for Necessity and Friday Prayer
Ruling on exiting i'tikaf with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits leaving i'tikaf for Friday prayer and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Leaving i'tikaf for Friday prayer is a permitted necessity—the Hanafi ruling does not invalidate it.

This lesson addresses a common dilemma for the mu'takif: when can he leave the mosque? The passage clarifies that leaving for a human need (like using the toilet) is allowed by explicit hadith. A more contested issue is leaving for Friday prayer. The Hanafi school holds that Friday prayer is a pressing need that permits departure, while Imam Shafi'i argues that it invalidates i'tikaf. We will examine the proofs and the practical impact of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that the mu'takif may leave the mosque for a human need (hajat al-insan) and for Friday prayer without invalidating i'tikaf.
The Hanafi ruling is based on necessity and the hadith of Aisha.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that leaving for Friday prayer invalidates i'tikaf because one could have chosen a jami' mosque from the start.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i rationale: i'tikaf in a non-jami' mosque is valid, but if one leaves for Friday, it is a departure from the condition of staying.
The Shafi'i school emphasizes the possibility of planning.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: i'tikaf is valid in any mosque, and since Friday is obligatory, the necessity to leave is absolute. The mu'takif may leave at the appropriate time and return after the prayer.
The Hanafi school gives priority to the Friday obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Hanafis, i'tikaf remains valid; according to Shafi'is, it becomes invalid. This affects whether the person must restart i'tikaf or may continue.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَخْرُجُ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ إلَّا لِحَاحَةِ الإِنسَانِ أوِ الْجُمَعَةِ أَمَّا لِحَاجَةِ لِحَدِيثِ عَائِشَةَ كَانَ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا يَخْرُجُ مِنْ مُعْتَكَفِ إِلَّا لِحَاجَةِ الْإِنسَانِ وَلِإِنَّهُ مَعَلُومُ وَقُوْعَهَا وَلَابُدَّ مِنَ الحُرُوحِ فِى تَقْضِيَّتِهَا فَيَصِيرُ الحُرُوجُ لَهَا مُسْتَنى وَلَا يَمَكُثُ بَعَدَ فَرَاغِةٍ مِنَ الطَّهَرُرِ لأَنَّ مَا ثَبَتَ بِالضَّرُورَةَ يَتَقَدَّرُ بِقَدْرِهَا وَأَمَّا الْجُمُعَةَ فَلَاتَهَا مِنْ أَهَم حَوَائِجِهِ وَهِيَ مَعْلُومُ وَقُوعُهَا وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ الْحُرُوجُ إِلَيْهَا مُفْسِدُ لِأَنَّهُ يُمَكِنَّهُ الْإِعْتِكَافُ فِي الْجَامِعِ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ الإِعْتِكَافُ فِى كُلِّ مَسْجِدٍ مَشْرُوعٌ وَإِذَا صَحَ الشَّرُوحُ فَالضَّرُورَةٌ مُطْلَقَةٌ فِى الحُرُوج وَيَخرُج حِينَ تَزُولُ الشَّمْسُ لِأَنَّ الْخِطَابَ يَتَوَجَّهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَنزِلُهُ بَعِيدًا عَنْهُ يَخْرُجُ فِي وَقَتٍ يُمْكِنُهُ إِدْرَاكَهَا وَيُصَلِّي قَبْلَهَا أَرْبَعًا وَ فِي روايَةٍ مَا الأرْبَعُ سُنةُ وَ رَكْعَتَانِ تَحِيَّةُ الْمَسْجِدِ وَ بَعْدَهَا أَرْبَعًا أو سِتَّاً عَلى حَسَب الاختلافِ فِى سُنَةِ الجُمُعَةِ وَ سَتْهَا تَرَابِع لَهَا فَالْحِقَتُ بِهَا وَلَوْ أَقَامَ فِى الْمَسْجِدِ الجَامِع أكثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ لَا يَفْسُدُ اعْتِكَافُهُ لِأَنَّهُ مَوْضِعُ اعْتِكَافٍ أنَّهُ لَا يَسْتَحَبَّ لأنه التَزمَ أَدارَهُ فِى مَسْجِدٍ وَاحِدٍ فَلَا يُتِمَّهَا فِي مَسْجِدَيْنِ مِنْ غَيْرَ ضَرُورَةٍ ترجمہ اور معلف مسجد سے نہ نکلے مگر انسانی ضرورت کے لئے یا جمعہ کے لئے بہر حال ضرورت انسانی کے لئے نکلنا تو حدیث عائشہ کی وجہ سے ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے اپنے معتکف سے نہیں نکلتے تھے مگر ضرورت انسانی کے لئے اور اس لئے کہ ضروریات انسانی کا واقع ہونا معلوم
And he should not leave the mosque except for a human need or for Friday prayer. As for necessity, due to the hadith of Aisha: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) would not leave his i'tikaf except for a human need.' And because it is known that such needs occur, and leaving is necessary to fulfill them, so leaving for them becomes permissible (mustathna). And he should not remain after completing his purification, because what is established by necessity is limited to its extent. As for Friday prayer, it is among his most important needs, and its occurrence is known. Imam al-Shafi'i said that going out for Friday invalidates i'tikaf because it is possible for him to perform i'tikaf in a congregational mosque (jami'). We (Hanafis) say: i'tikaf is prescribed in every mosque, and when the condition (shart) is valid, necessity is absolute in leaving. He should leave when the sun passes its zenith, because the address (of Friday) becomes directed. If his residence is far from the congregational mosque, he should leave at a time that enables him to reach it. He should pray before it four rak'ahs, and in one narration: the four are sunnah and two rak'ahs are tahiyyat al-masjid. After it, he should pray four or six, according to the difference regarding the sunnah of Friday prayer; and six is that four are for it, so they are attached to it. If he stays in the jami' mosque longer than that, his i'tikaf does not become invalid because it is a place of i'tikaf. However, it is not recommended because he has obligated himself to stay in one mosque, so he should not complete it in two mosques without necessity. Translation: And the mu'takif should not leave the mosque except for a human need or for Friday. As for human need, leaving is due to the hadith of Aisha, that the Prophet would not leave his i'tikaf except for a human need, and because the occurrence of human needs is known...
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on exiting the mosque during i'tikaf, along with an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Shafi'i regarding Friday prayer. The Hanafi position: the mu'takif may leave for necessary human needs (using the toilet, wudu, etc.) and for Friday prayer (if his mosque is not a jami' mosque where Friday is held). The proof is the hadith of Aisha. For Friday, he should leave at zawal (noon) and pray sunnah prayers before and after Friday according to the Hanafi sunnah (4 before, 4 or 6 after, plus tahiyyat al-masjid). He should not stay longer than necessary for these prayers. If he does, it does not invalidate i'tikaf, but it is not recommended because he has committed to one mosque. Imam Shafi'i holds that leaving for Friday invalidates i'tikaf because the mu'takif could have chosen a jami' mosque initially. The Hanafi response: i'tikaf is valid in any mosque, and if one starts i'tikaf in a non-jami' mosque, necessity allows leaving for Friday.

Key Terms
حاجة الانسان (hajat al-insan): A human need, specifically the need to relieve oneself (urine, defecation).
جمعہ (jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer, an obligation for men.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits otherwise prohibited actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person in i'tikaf leaves his mosque to attend Friday prayer in a jami' mosque, what happens to his i'tikaf?
A) His i'tikaf is invalidated.
B) His i'tikaf remains valid.
C) He must start his i'tikaf over.
D) He must sacrifice an animal.

Key Takeaway
Leaving i'tikaf for a human need or Friday prayer is permissible and does not invalidate i'tikaf in the Hanafi school.

Sawm — Fasting

Masjid Condition for I'tikaf: Congregational Mosque vs. Any Mosque
Explaining the intra-Hanafi dispute on masjid requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi positions on the masjid requirement for i'tikaf and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
I'tikaf is valid in any masjid, not only those with congregation.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the masjid requirement for i'tikaf. Imam Abu Hanifa is reported to require a masjid where all five prayers are performed in congregation, while the Sahibayn consider any masjid sufficient. The author explains the proofs and ultimately favors the Sahibayn's view, which is the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi narrations
Note the narration from Abu Hanifa that i'tikaf is only valid in a masjid with all five daily prayers in congregation, and the Sahibayn's view that any masjid suffices.
Also note the agreement with Imam Ahmad on the strict view.
2
Follow Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that i'tikaf is the worship of waiting for prayer (intizar al-salah), so it must be in a place where prayer is actually performed collectively.
This is a qiyas reasoning: waiting only makes sense where prayer occurs.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn cite the absolute Quranic verse 'while you are staying in the mosques' (2:187), which does not specify congregational mosques.
The absolute text includes all mosques.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator inclines towards the Sahibayn's view, and later Hanafi works adopt it as the relied-upon position.
This is the position for fatwa and practice.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a person makes i'tikaf in a small local masjid that does not hold all five congregations, it is valid according to the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الصوم
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
ہے جس میں باجماعت نماز ادا کی جاتی ہو اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ صحت اعتکاف کے لئے ایسی مسجد کا ہونا شرط ہے میں پانچوں نمازیں جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کی جاتی ہوں یہیں امام احمد کا قول ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتکاف نماز کے انتظار کی عبادت ہے پس عبادت اعتکاف ایسی جگہ کے ساتھ مختص ہو گی جہاں نماز ادا کی جاتی ہو یعنی ہر نماز ادا کی جاتی ہو۔ اور صاحبین اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ہر مسجد میں اعتکاف کرنا صحیح ہے خواہ اس میں جماعت کے ساتھ نماز ہوتی ہو یا جماعت کے ساتھ نماز نہ (البقرة: علام ہوتی ہو ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول وانتُمْ عَاكِفُونَ فِى الْمَسَاجِدِ مطلق ہے۔ صاحب عنا یہ نے شرح طحاوی کے حوالہ سے تحریر کیا ہے کہ سب سے افضل اعتکاف مسجد حرام میں ہے پھر مسجد نبوی میں پھر مسجد اقصیٰ میں پھر ان بڑی مساجد میں جن میں لوگ زیادہ سے زیادہ آتے ہوں ۔ اور عورت کے لئے ہمارے نزدیک افضل یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے گھر کی مسجد میں اعتکاف کرے یعنی گھر میں نماز کے لئے جو جگہ مقرر کر رکھی سے اس میں اعتکاف کرنا عورت کے لئے افضل ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ مردوں اور عورتوں دونوں کے لئے مسجد جماعت میں اعتکاف کرنا جائز ہے گھر کی مسجد میں اعتکاف کرنا نہ مرد کے لئے جائز ہی اور نہ عورت کے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود اعتکاف زمین کے اس حصہ کی تعظیم ہے جس میں اعتکاف کیا جائے گا پس اعتکاف اس حصہ کے ساتھ مختص ہو گا جو شرعا بھی معظم و مکرم ہو اور شرعا مساجد تو معظم ہوتی ہیں مگر گھروں میں جو جگہ نماز پڑھنے کے لئے مقرر کر لی گی وہ اس درجہ معظم نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اعتکاف فقط مساجد کے اندر جائز ہوگا اور غیر مساجد یعنی مساجد بیوت میں جائز نہ ہوگا ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہم نے سابق میں کہا ہے کہ اعتکاف نماز کے انتظار کی عبادت ہے اور عورت مسجد بیت میں نماز کا انتظار کرتی ہے نہ کہ شرعی مساجد میں پس جب مسجد بیت میں انتظار صلوۃ کرتی ہے تو ا پیکاف بھی اسی میں کرے گا۔ اور اگر گھر میں نماز کے لئے کوئی جگہ مقرر نہ ہو تو کوئی ایک جگہ مقرر کر کے اس میں ایکاف کرلے۔
Book of Fasting. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume Three. [A masjid] in which congregational prayer is performed, and there is a narration from Abu Hanifa that for the validity of i'tikaf, it is a condition that it be a masjid in which the five daily prayers are performed in congregation; this is also the saying of Imam Ahmad. Its proof is that i'tikaf is the worship of waiting for prayer, so the worship of i'tikaf will be specific to a place where prayer is performed, i.e., every prayer is performed. And according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), Imam Malik, and Imam Shafi'i, i'tikaf is valid in every masjid, whether congregational prayer is held in it or not. Their proof is that Allah's words 'While you are staying in the mosques' (2:187) are absolute. The author of al-'Inayah wrote, quoting Sharh al-Tahawi, that the most excellent i'tikaf is in al-Masjid al-Haram, then the Prophet's Mosque, then al-Masjid al-Aqsa, then in large mosques where people come most frequently. And for a woman, according to us, it is better that she make i'tikaf in the masjid of her house, i.e., in the place designated for prayer in her home; this is better for a woman. Imam Shafi'i said that it is permissible for both men and women to make i'tikaf in a congregational mosque; i'tikaf in the home prayer area is not permissible for men nor for women. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the purpose of i'tikaf is to honor the piece of land in which i'tikaf is performed, so i'tikaf is specific to that which is honored and revered by Shari'ah, and mosques are honored by Shari'ah, but the place designated for prayer in homes is not of that degree of honor; therefore i'tikaf is only valid within mosques, not in non-mosques, i.e., masajid al-buyut. Our proof is that we have said previously that i'tikaf is the worship of waiting for prayer, and a woman waits for prayer in her masjid al-bayt, not in the Shari'i mosques. So when she waits for prayer in the masjid al-bayt, she will also perform i'tikaf in it. And if there is no designated place for prayer in the house, then she should designate one place and perform i'tikaf in it.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage discusses two issues related to the place of i'tikaf. First, the requirement that a masjid have congregational prayer for the validity of i'tikaf, according to one narration from Imam Abu Hanifa and also Imam Ahmad. The reasoning is that i'tikaf is an act of waiting for prayer (intizar al-salah), and waiting only makes sense where prayer is actually performed. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), along with Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, hold that i'tikaf is valid in any masjid, even if no congregation is established, citing the absolute wording of the Quran 'while you are staying in the mosques'. The commentator then notes the preferred order of mosques for i'tikaf, based on al-'Inayah citing Sharh al-Tahawi: the best is Masjid al-Haram, then Masjid al-Nabawi, then Masjid al-Aqsa, then large and crowded mosques. Second, the ruling for women: according to the Hanafi school, a woman's i'tikaf is better in her home prayer area (masjid al-bayt), not in a public mosque. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, stating that i'tikaf is only valid in a Shari'i mosque, not in a designated home area. The Hanafi response reiterates that i'tikaf is essentially waiting for prayer, and a woman's designated prayer area in her home serves the same purpose. Thus, it is sufficient and even better for her. This ruling reflects the Hanafi emphasis on istihsan and practical ease for women.

Key Terms
مسجد (masjid): A place designated for prayer, including any building or space that is legally considered a masjid in the Shari'ah.
اعتکاف (i'tikaf): Spiritual retreat in a mosque with the intention of drawing closer to Allah, characterized by staying in the masjid and engaging in worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, which masjid is required for valid i'tikaf?
A) A masjid where all five daily prayers are performed in congregation
B) Any masjid, regardless of congregation
C) Only the three haram mosques
D) A masjid where at least one congregational prayer is held

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi allows i'tikaf in any masjid, making it accessible even in small mosques without full congregation.

Women's I'tikaf: Home Prayer Area vs. Public Mosque
Explaining the Hanafi vs. Shafi'i dispute on women's i'tikaf place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on women's i'tikaf and explain the difference with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A woman's i'tikaf is better in her home prayer area, not in a public mosque.

This passage continues with the ruling for women's i'tikaf. The Hanafi school holds that it is better (afdal) for a woman to perform i'tikaf in her home prayer area (masjid al-bayt), while Imam Shafi'i requires i'tikaf to be in a Shari'i mosque for both men and women. The Hanafi proof is based on the definition of i'tikaf as waiting for prayer, which a woman does at home.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on women's i'tikaf
According to the Hanafi school, a woman's i'tikaf is valid and better in her home prayer area (masjid al-bayt).
This is the mufta bihi.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
Imam Shafi'i holds that i'tikaf is only valid in a Shari'i mosque for both men and women; the home area does not suffice.
Imam Ahmad also agrees with Shafi'i on this? Not mentioned, but source says Shafi'i.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Shafi'i argues that i'tikaf is for honoring a place, and only mosques are honored by Shari'ah; home prayer areas are not at that level.
This is a talili reasoning based on the purpose of i'tikaf.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that i'tikaf is defined as waiting for prayer (intizar al-salah), not honoring the place. A woman waits for prayer at home, so her i'tikaf is valid there.
This is a rebuttal based on the ma'na of i'tikaf.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah is that Hanafis allow women to stay home for i'tikaf, while Shafi'is require them to go to a mosque.
This has implications for women's ease and privacy.

Source Text

Exiting the Masjid During I'tikaf: Necessities and the Jumu'ah Dispute
Explaining permissible reasons to leave the masjid during i'tikaf, including human needs and Friday prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two permissible reasons for leaving the masjid during i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki objection against leaving for Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
Leaving for human needs is an exception; leaving for Jumu'ah is a necessity that does not invalidate i'tikaf.

In this passage, the author of Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi position on when a mu'takif may exit the masjid. The general rule is that one may not leave except for two categories: unavoidable physical needs and the obligatory Friday prayer. The ruling appears straightforward, but a significant inter-madhhab dispute arises over the permissibility of leaving specifically for Jumu'ah. Let us analyse the proof and counter-proof.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two permissible reasons for leaving the masjid during i'tikaf according to the Hanafi school.
The text explicitly mentions 'hajat al-insan' and 'al-jumu'ah'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Determine which schools disagree on Jumu'ah exit and what they hold.
Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik consider leaving for Jumu'ah to invalidate i'tikaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the reasoning behind the opposing view.
They argue that leaving (khuruj) contradicts the essence of staying (lubth) and that one can choose a Jami' masjid initially.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine how the text rebuts the opponent's argument.
The Hanafi response: i'tikaf is valid in any masjid, and Jumu'ah is a major obligation necessitating exit.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of this difference in rulings for a mu'takif.
A Hanafi may leave and return; a Shafi'i must break i'tikaf or choose a Jami' masjid.

وَلَا يَخْرُجُ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ إلَّا لِحَاحَةِ الإِنسَانِ أوِ الْجُمَعَةِ أَمَّا لِحَاجَةِ لِحَدِيثِ عَائِشَةَ كَانَ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا يَخْرُجُ مِنْ مُعْتَكَفِ إِلَّا لِحَاجَةِ الْإِنسَانِ وَلِإِنَّهُ مَعَلُومُ وَقُوْعَهَا وَلَابُدَّ مِنَ الحُرُوحِ فِى تَقْضِيَّتِهَا فَيَصِيرُ الحُرُوجُ لَهَا مُسْتَنى وَلَا يَمَكُثُ بَعَدَ فَرَاغِةٍ مِنَ الطَّهَرُرِ لأَنَّ مَا ثَبَتَ بِالضَّرُورَةَ يَتَقَدَّرُ بِقَدْرِهَا وَأَمَّا الْجُمُعَةَ فَلَاتَهَا مِنْ أَهَم حَوَائِجِهِ وَهِيَ مَعْلُومُ وَقُوعُهَا وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ الْحُرُوجُ إِلَيْهَا مُفْسِدُ لِأَنَّهُ يُمَكِنَّهُ الْإِعْتِكَافُ فِي الْجَامِعِ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ الإِعْتِكَافُ فِى كُلِّ مَسْجِدٍ مَشْرُوعٌ وَإِذَا صَحَ الشَّرُوحُ فَالضَّرُورَةٌ مُطْلَقَةٌ فِى الحُرُوج وَيَخرُج حِينَ تَزُولُ الشَّمْسُ لِأَنَّ الْخِطَابَ يَتَوَجَّهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَنزِلُهُ بَعِيدًا عَنْهُ يَخْرُجُ فِي وَقَتٍ يُمْكِنُهُ إِدْرَاكَهَا وَيُصَلِّي قَبْلَهَا أَرْبَعًا وَ فِي روَايَةٍ مَا الأرْبَعُ سُنةُ وَ رَكْعَتَانِ تَحِيَّةُ الْمَسْجِدِ وَ بَعْدَهَا أَرْبَعًا أو سِتَّاً عَلى حَسَب الاختلافِ فِى سُنَةِ الجُمُعَةِ وَ سَتْهَا تَرَابِع لَهَا فَالْحِقَتُ بِهَا وَلَوْ أَقَامَ فِى الْمَسْجِدِ الجَامِع أكثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ لَا يَفْسُدُ اعْتِكَافُهُ لِأَنَّهُ مَوْضِعُ اعْتِكَافٍ أنَّهُ لَا يَسْتَحَبَّ لأنه التَزمَ أَدارَهُ فِى مَسْجِدٍ وَاحِدٍ فَلَا يُتِمَّهَا فِي مَسْجِدَيْنِ مِنْ غَيْرَ ضَرُورَةٍ
ترجمہ اور معلف مسجد سے نہ نکلے مگر انسانی ضرورت کے لئے یا جمعہ کے لئے بہر حال ضرورت انسانی کے لئے نکلنا تو حدیث عائشہ کی وجہ سے ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے اپنے معتکف سے نہیں نکلتے تھے مگر ضرورت انسانی کے لئے اور اس لئے کہ ضروریات انسانی کا واقع ہونا معلوم
ہے اور ان ضروریات کو پورا کرنے کے لئے نکلنا ضروری ہی پس ان حاجات کے لئے نکلنا مستثنی ہو جائے گا اور طہارت سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد نہ ٹھہرے کیونکہ جو چیز ضرور ہا ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ بقدر ضرورت مقدر ہوتی ہے اور رکعتیں پڑھے یا چھ رکعتیں جمعہ کی سنتوں میں اختلاف کے مطابق اور جمعہ کی سنتیں جمعہ اور کے تابع ہیں اس لئے ان کو جمعہ کے ساتھ لاحق کیا گیا ہے اور اگر معتکف نے جامع مسجد میں اس سے زیادہ قیام کیا تو اس کا اعتکاف فاسد نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ جامع مسجد بھی مقام اعتکاف ہے مگر یہ کہ مستحب نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس نے ایک مسجد میں اس کو ادا کرنے کا التزام کیا ہے اس لئے اسکو با ضرورت دو مسجدوں میں پورا نہ کرے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مختلف کے لئے مسجد اعتکاف سے نکلنا جائز نہیں ہے مگر دوخضر در توں سے ایک ضرورت طبعی سے جیسے بول و براز کی ضرورت ، دوم ضرورت دینی سے جیسے جمعہ اور غسل جنابت کی ضرورت بہر حال ضرورت طبعی اور ضرورت انسانی کے واسطے نکلنے کے جواز پر دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے یعنی كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا يَخْرُجُ مِنْ مُعْتَكَفِهِ إِلَّا لِحَاجَةِ الْإِنْسَانِ لين رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اپنے مختلف سے باہر تشریف نہ لیجاتے تھے مگر انسانی اور طبعی ضرورت پورا کرنے کے لئے یعنی بول و براز کے لئے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ضروریات انسانی کا واقع ہونا پہلے سے معلوم ہے اور یہ بھی معلوم ہے کہ ان کو پورا کرنے کے لئے نکلنا ضروری ہے اس کے بغیر چارہ نہیں تو ان ضرورتوں کے لئے نکلنا خود ہی مستی ہو گیا کیونکہ غیر اختیاری امور کا انسان مکلف نہیں ہوتا لیکن اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ انسانی ضرورت کو پورا کرنے کے بعد طہارت سے فارغ ہو کر فوراً اپنے معتکف میں چلا جائے طہارت سے فارغ ہو کر اپنے گھر میں نہ ٹھہرے کیونکہ حاجات انسانی کے لئے نکلنا ضرورۃ ثابت ہے اور جو چیز ضرور ثابت ہو تو وہ بقدر ضرورت ثابت ہوتی ہے اس لئے بقدر ضرورت مسجد اعتکاف سے باہر رہنے کی اجازت ہوگی اس سے زائد کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ اور رہا نماز جمعہ کے لئے نکلنا تو یہ ہمارا مذہب ہے اور امام شافعی اور امام مالک کے نزدیک جمعہ کے لئے نکلنا جائز نہیں ہے حتٰی کہ اگر نماز جمعہ کے لئے نکلا تو اعتکاف فاسد ہو جائیگا ان دونوں حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خروج، اعتکاف (لبث ) کی ضد ہے اور شئی اپنی ضد کے آجانے سے فاسد ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے اعتکاف ، خروج من المسجد سے فاسد ہو جائے گا ہاں ان صورتوں میں فاسد نہ ہوگا جن صورتوں میں خروج کی صورت محقق ہے جیسے بول براز کے لئے نکلنا اور نماز جمعہ کے لئے خروج کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر اس نے سات دن سے کم کا اعتکاف کیا ہے تو جس مسجد میں چاہے اعتکاف کرلے اور اگر سات دن یا زائد کا اعتکاف کیا ہے تو جامع مسجد میں اعتکاف کرے پس ان دونوں صورتوں میں ایسی ضرورت نہیں پائی گئی جو نماز جمعہ کے لئے خروج کو مباح قرار دینے والی ہو اور جب ایسی ضرورت
متحقق نہیں ہوئی تو نماز جمعہ کے لئے نکلنے کی بھی اجازت نہ ہوگی۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دلیل سے یہ بات ثابت ہو چکی ہے کہ اعتکاف ہر مسجد میں مشروع ہے جیسا کہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے
And he should not leave the masjid except for a human need or for Jumu'ah. As for need, due to the hadith of Aisha: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) would not leave his i'tikaf except for a human need.' And because its occurrence is known, and leaving is necessary to fulfill it, so leaving for it becomes an exception. And after completion of purification, he should not stay, because what is established by necessity is limited to its extent. And as for Jumu'ah, it is among his important needs and its occurrence is known. Imam Shafi'i said that leaving for it is invalidating because he can make i'tikaf in the Jami' mosque. And we say that i'tikaf is prescribed in every masjid, and when beginning is valid in any masjid, then necessity gives permission to leave. And he should leave when the sun declines because the address (Khutbah) is after zawal. And if his place is far from him, he should leave at a time that enables him to catch it, and he should pray four rak'ahs before it, and in one narration eight rak'ahs: four sunna and two tahiyyat al-masjid, and after it four or six according to the difference regarding the sunna of Jumu'ah. And its sunan are subordinate to Jumu'ah, so they are attached to it. And if he stays in the Jami' masjid more than that, his i'tikaf does not become invalid because it is a place of i'tikaf. But it is not recommended because he undertook to perform it in one masjid, so he should not complete it in two masjids without necessity. Translation: And the mu'takif should not leave the masjid except for a human necessity or for Jumu'ah. For human necessity, it is due to the hadith of Aisha that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would not leave his i'tikaf except for a human need. And because human needs are known to occur, and leaving is essential to fulfill them, so leaving for these needs becomes an exception. After finishing purification, he should not stay because what is established by necessity is limited to its extent. And as for leaving for Jumu'ah, it is our madhhab, and according to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, leaving for Jumu'ah is not permissible; rather, if he leaves for Jumu'ah, his i'tikaf becomes invalid. Their proof is that leaving (khuruj) is the opposite of i'tikaf (lubth), and a thing becomes invalid by its opposite, so i'tikaf becomes invalid by leaving the masjid, except in cases where leaving is necessitated, like for urine and stool. And leaving for Jumu'ah has no necessity because if he has made i'tikaf for less than seven days, he can make i'tikaf in any masjid he wants, and if for seven days or more, he should make i'tikaf in the Jami' masjid. So in both cases, there is no necessity that would permit leaving for Jumu'ah, and when no such necessity exists, leaving for Jumu'ah is not allowed. Our proof is that it has been established by evidence that i'tikaf is prescribed in every masjid, as Allah says...
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage rules on when a person in i'tikaf may leave the masjid. The general principle is that one may not leave except for two reasons: a human need (like urination or defecation) or Friday prayer (Jumu'ah). For human needs, the evidence is the hadith of Aisha (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) only left for such needs. The rationale is that these necessities are inevitable, and one is not held responsible for unavoidable acts. However, once the need is fulfilled and purification is complete, one must return immediately without lingering, because the permission is limited to the extent of necessity. Regarding Jumu'ah, the Hanafi position permits leaving for it, contrary to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, who consider it invalidating. Their reasoning is that leaving contradicts the essence of staying (lubth) in i'tikaf, and i'tikaf is spoiled by its opposite. They argue there is no necessity because one could choose a masjid where Jumu'ah is held. The Hanafi response is that i'tikaf is valid in any masjid, and since Jumu'ah is an important religious obligation, leaving for it is a necessity. The text also details the timing and prayers: one leaves after zawal (when the sun declines) for the khutbah, and one may pray the sunnah of Jumu'ah and tahiyyat al-masjid before and after. If the mu'takif's i'tikaf is in a non-Jami' masjid, he must leave in time to catch Jumu'ah. If he stays in the Jami' masjid longer, his i'tikaf does not break because it is also a place of i'tikaf, but it is not recommended to prolong stay without necessity, as he intended to stay in one masjid. The commentary clarifies that leaving for Jumu'ah is considered a religious necessity, akin to the human needs category.

Key Terms
حاجة الإنسان (hajat al-insan): A human need, specifically natural calls such as urination and defecation.
الخروج للجمعة (al-khuruj li al-jumu'ah): Leaving the place of i'tikaf to attend the Friday congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a mu'takif leaves the masjid to use the bathroom and then stays outside to talk for 10 minutes, what is the status of his i'tikaf?
A) Valid, because human needs permit exit.
B) Invalid, because he lingered after necessity was fulfilled.
C) Valid but makruh.
D) Invalid only if he intended to break i'tikaf.

Key Takeaway
Exiting the masjid during i'tikaf is only allowed for essential needs and Friday prayer, with the strict condition of immediate return.

Leaving I'tikaf for Natural Necessities: Permission and Limits
Explains the permissibility and limits of leaving i'tikaf for natural needs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of permissible exits from i'tikaf and apply the condition that limits the duration of exit to the extent of necessity.

Core Idea
Leaving for natural needs is permitted only as needed; extra time invalidates i'tikaf.

This passage clarifies a key exception to the general rule that a person in i'tikaf must remain in the mosque. It addresses the inevitable human needs, providing both textual and rational evidence, and sets the condition that the exit must be limited strictly to the time required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that leaving the mosque during i'tikaf is generally prohibited, but exceptions exist for necessities.
2
Locate the exceptions
Identify the two categories: natural needs (urination/defecation) and religious needs (Friday prayer, ghusl).
3
Analyze the proof
Examine the hadith of Aisha (ra) and the rational necessity argument that make this exception valid.
4
Apply the limitation
Apply the principle that what is established by necessity is limited to necessity: immediate return after purification is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ معتکف کے لئے مسجد اعتکاف سے نکلنا جائز نہیں ہے مگر دو ضرورتوں سے ایک ضرورت طبعی سے جیسے بول و براز کی ضرورت ، دوم ضرورت دینی سے جیسے جمعہ اور غسل جنابت کی ضرورت بہر حال ضرورت طبعی اور ضرورت انسانی کے واسطے نکلنے کے جواز پر دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے یعنی كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَا يَخْرُجُ مِنْ مُعْتَكَفِهِ إِلَّا لِحَاجَةِ الْإِنْسَانِ لان رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم اپنے معتکف سے باہر تشریف نہ لیجاتے تھے مگر انسانی اور طبعی ضرورت پورا کرنے کے لئے یعنی بول و براز کے لئے دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ضروریات انسانی کا واقع ہونا پہلے سے معلوم ہے اور یہ بھی معلوم ہے کہ ان کو پورا کرنے کے لئے نکلنا ضروری ہے اس کے بغیر چارہ نہیں تو ان ضرورتوں کے لئے نکلنا خود ہی مستثنیٰ ہو گیا کیونکہ غیر اختیاری امور کا انسان مکلف نہیں ہوتا لیکن اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ انسانی ضرورت کو پورا کرنے کے بعد طہارت سے فارغ ہو کر فوراً اپنے معتکف میں چلا جائے طہارت سے فارغ ہو کر اپنے گھر میں نہ ٹھہرے کیونکہ حاجات انسانی کے لئے نکلنا ضرورۃ ثابت ہے اور جو چیز ضرور ثابت ہو تو وہ بقدر ضرورت ثابت ہوتی ہے اس لئے بقدر ضرورت مسجد اعتکاف سے باہر رہنے کی اجازت ہوگی اس سے زائد کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔
Explanation of the case: The person in i'tikaf is not permitted to leave the mosque of i'tikaf except for two necessities: one, a natural need like urination and defecation; second, a religious need like Friday prayer and the need for ghusl from janabah. In any case, evidence for the permissibility of leaving for natural and human needs is the hadith of Aisha: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to not leave his i'tikaf except for human need. That is, he would only go out for human and natural needs, meaning for urination and defecation. The second evidence is that the occurrence of human necessities is known beforehand, and it is also known that leaving to fulfill them is necessary—there is no alternative. So leaving for these needs becomes itself excepted, because a person is not obligated to do involuntary acts. However, it is necessary that after fulfilling the human need, he should return immediately to his i'tikaf after completing purification, and not stay in his house. This is because leaving for human needs is established by necessity, and what is established by necessity is established to the extent of necessity. Therefore, permission to be outside the mosque of i'tikaf is only to the extent of necessity, not more than that.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation (tashrih) of the ruling on leaving the mosque during i'tikaf. It begins by stating the general principle: a person in i'tikaf may not leave the mosque except for two categories of needs: (1) natural necessities (hajat tabi'iyyah) such as urination and defecation, and (2) religious necessities (hajat diniyyah) such as Friday prayer and ghusl from janabah. The author then provides two proofs for the permissibility of leaving for natural needs. The first proof is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would only leave his i'tikaf for 'human need' (hajat al-insan), interpreted by the Hanafi scholars as natural bodily functions. The second proof is a rational argument: natural needs are inevitable and known to occur; since they cannot be avoided without hardship, leaving to fulfill them is an exception to the general prohibition of exiting the mosque. However, the author immediately qualifies this by stating that after fulfilling the need, the person must return to the mosque immediately after performing purification (istinja' or wudu) and should not delay by going home or engaging in other activities. This is based on the principle that 'what is established by necessity is limited to the extent of necessity' (ma thabita bi al-darurah yuqaddaru bi qadr al-darurah). Therefore, only the minimal time needed to relieve oneself and purify is permitted; any extra time invalidates the i'tikaf.

Key Terms
الحاجة الإنسانية (al-hajat al-insaniyyah): Human need, specifically natural bodily functions like urination and defecation, as per this text.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits an otherwise prohibited action, limited to the extent needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person in i'tikaf leaves the mosque for a natural need and then delays returning by visiting a friend?
A) I'tikaf becomes invalid
B) I'tikaf remains valid
C) It is makruh
D) It requires compensation

Key Takeaway
Leaving i'tikaf for natural needs is permitted only to the extent of necessity; immediate return after purification is required.

Leaving I'tikaf for Friday Prayer: Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Presents Hanafi position vs Shafi'i/Maliki on leaving i'tikaf for Jumu'ah, with proofs and details on timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on leaving i'tikaf for Friday prayer and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
Allah's obligation (Friday) overrides a human vow—so leaving i'tikaf for Jumu'ah is permissible.

In this passage, we examine a classical inter-madhhab dispute: can a person in i'tikaf leave the mosque to attend Friday prayer? The Hanafi school permits it, while the Shafi'i and Maliki schools invalidate i'tikaf if one leaves. We will explore the proofs, the Hanafi response, and the practical timing rules for exiting.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by identifying what the Hanafi school holds: leaving for Friday prayer is permissible and the i'tikaf remains valid.
The core is that divine obligation (Friday) takes precedence over a human vow (i'tikaf).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the Shafi'i and Maliki position: leaving for Friday invalidates i'tikaf because exit contradicts staying.
They argue there is no necessity since one could have chosen a mosque where Friday is held.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand their dalil: exit is the opposite of i'tikaf (lubth), so any deliberate exit nullifies it. They also claim no genuine necessity for Friday.
Their proof is based on the nature of i'tikaf as continuous stay.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the Quran (2:187) allows i'tikaf in any mosque, so the obligation of Friday does not require staying in a specific mosque. Moreover, Allah's obligation cannot be nullified by a human vow.
The key is the hierarchy of obligations: Allah's command over man's self-imposed duty.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In the Hanafi school, the mu'takif may leave, pray Friday and its sunnahs, and return with i'tikaf intact. In Shafi'i/Maliki, the i'tikaf becomes invalid and would need to be restarted.
The difference affects the validity of the entire i'tikaf period.

ایک مسجد میں ادائے اعتکاف اپنے اوپر لازم کیا تھا لہذا بلا ضرورت دو مسجدوں میں پورا نہ کرے اس عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر اس نے جامع مسجد میں پورا کر لیا یا زائد وقت ٹھہرا رہا تو اعتکاف تو ہو گیا مگر مکروہ ہوا۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ عذر کی وجہ سے ایک مسجد سے دوسری مسجد کی طرف منتقل ہونا جائز ہے مثلاً جس مسجد میں معتکف تھا اس کی چھت گر گئی یا اس میں جان کا خطرہ ہے تو اس سے منتقل ہو کر دوسری مسجد کی طرف جانا جائز ہے ۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
And as for leaving for Friday prayer, this is our madhhab, and according to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, leaving for Friday prayer is not permissible, to the extent that if one leaves for Friday prayer, his i'tikaf becomes invalid. The proof of these two scholars is that exiting (khuruj) is the opposite of i'tikaf (lubth), and a thing becomes invalid by the arrival of its opposite. Therefore, i'tikaf becomes invalid by exiting the mosque. However, it would not become invalid in cases where exit is unavoidable, like for urination/defecation. But leaving for Friday prayer has no necessity because if he made i'tikaf for less than seven days, he can make i'tikaf in any mosque; if he made i'tikaf for seven days or more, he should make it in the congregational mosque. In both cases, there is no necessity that would make exiting permissible for Friday. And when no necessity is established, there is no permission to leave for Friday. Our proof is that it has been established by evidence that i'tikaf is prescribed in every mosque, as Allah says: 'And do not have relations with them while you are in i'tikaf in the mosques.' So when i'tikaf is prescribed in every mosque, then leaving for Friday is an exception to his vowed i'tikaf just as leaving for human necessity is excepted, because neglecting Friday prayer to preserve i'tikaf is absolutely not permissible. Therefore, the obligation of i'tikaf due to a vow is inferior to the obligation of Friday prayer. And it is inferior because Friday prayer is made obligatory by Allah's volition, while i'tikaf is made obligatory by the servant's volition (by vowing). And the servant is not permitted to nullify an obligation imposed by Allah. So it is established that Friday prayer will not be neglected due to i'tikaf, and when Friday prayer is not neglected, permission to leave for Friday prayer exists. Now as to when he may leave: If his place of i'tikaf is near the congregational mosque, he leaves after zawal (sun past zenith) because the obligation of performing Friday prayer is directed after zawal. When this obligation is directed, then the need arises, and when the need arises, leaving for Friday becomes permissible. Since the need for performing Friday is realized after zawal, he leaves after zawal. But if his place of i'tikaf is far from the congregational mosque, he is permitted to leave early enough that he can attain Friday prayer including the khutbah, and before the khutbah he can pray four rak'ahs of sunnah. In one narration, he can pray six rak'ahs before Friday: four sunnah and two for tahiyyat al-masjid. And this mu'takif is permitted to pray four rak'ahs of sunnah after Friday in the congregational mosque, as is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, or six rak'ahs as Abu Yusuf says. His proof is that the sunan of Friday are subordinate to Friday, therefore these sunnahs are also annexed to Friday prayer, meaning just as the religious need for Friday prayer is established, similarly for its sunnahs the need is also established. From this clarification, it became clear that for a person making i'tikaf in a non-congregational mosque, it is permitted to stay in the congregational mosque to the extent of Friday prayer, khutbah, and its sunnahs. But if he stays longer than that, his i'tikaf does not become invalid, though it is contrary to what is better (khilaf al-awla) and not recommended (ghayr mustahab). It does not become invalid because the congregational mosque is also a place of i'tikaf. It is contrary to what is better because he had obligated himself to perform i'tikaf in one mosque; therefore he should not complete it in two mosques without necessity. From this phrase it is understood that if he completed it in the congregational mosque or stayed extra time, the i'tikaf is valid but makruh. And it is also understood that transferring from one mosque to another due to an excuse is permissible, e.g., if the mosque in which he was in i'tikaf had its roof collapse or there is danger to life, then it is permissible to transfer to another mosque. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, forgiven.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute regarding leaving the mosque for Friday prayer during i'tikaf. The Hanafi school, as represented by Abu Hanifa, holds that it is permissible to leave for Friday prayer, and if one does so, the i'tikaf remains valid. The proof is based on the Quranic verse (2:187) which mentions i'tikaf in 'masajid' (plural), indicating that i'tikaf is valid in any mosque. Therefore, if a person has vowed i'tikaf in a non-congregational mosque, he is not prevented from going to the Jumu'ah mosque because the obligation of Friday prayer takes precedence over his own vow. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools argue that exiting the mosque contradicts the essence of i'tikaf (which is staying in the mosque), so any deliberate exit invalidates it. They also claim that there is no necessity for Friday because one could have chosen a mosque where Friday is held. The Hanafi response is that the obligation of Friday is from Allah, while the i'tikaf obligation is from the human vow; the former takes precedence. The passage then details the practical rules: if the mosque where he is in i'tikaf is near the Jumu'ah mosque, he should leave after zawal; if far, he may leave earlier to catch the prayer and even perform the sunan. There is also a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the number of sunan after Friday. The passage concludes that staying longer than necessary in the Jumu'ah mosque does not invalidate i'tikaf but is makruh, and that transferring to another mosque due to an excuse is permissible.

Key Terms
وجوب (wujub): Obligation; here referring to the binding nature of Friday prayer (divine) versus vowed i'tikaf (human).
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship, making it obligatory on the person.
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered before Friday prayer, considered part of the Jumu'ah obligation.
اعتكاف (i'tikaf): Spiritual retreat in a mosque, often with a vow of stay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the obligation of Friday (from Allah) overrides the obligation of a vowed i'tikaf (from the servant).
C) Because the mosque for i'tikaf is always a congregational mosque.
D) Because the imam grants permission.

Key Takeaway
Leaving i'tikaf for Friday prayer is permissible in the Hanafi school because the divine obligation takes precedence over a human vow.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Leaving I'tikaf Without Excuse for a Short Time
Discusses the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a brief exit invalidates i'tikaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether a short exit invalidates i'tikaf, and identify the reliance on qiyas vs. istihsan.

Core Idea
A brief exit from i'tikaf: Abu Hanifa invalidates by qiyas; Sahibayn allow by istihsan for necessity.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute on a practical question: must a person in i'tikaf remain inside the mosque at all times, or is a short, necessary exit permitted? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that any exit without excuse invalidates i'tikaf, based on strict analogy (qiyas). His two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), take a more lenient view, using juristic preference (istihsan) to permit exits of less than half a day. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to see how Hanafi jurists balance textual principles with practical needs.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what each jurist says about leaving the mosque without excuse. Abu Hanifa says any exit invalidates; Sahibayn say it must be more than half a day to invalidate.
2
Identify the legal basis for each
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas: presence of al-manafi (the contradictory act of leaving) nullifies i'tikaf. Sahibayn use istihsan: a short exit is a practical necessity (darurah).
Qiyas = analogical reasoning; istihsan = juristic preference overriding qiyas.
3
Understand the underlying ‘illah (cause)
For Abu Hanifa, the ‘illah is any act that contradicts the essence of i'tikaf (lubth, staying). For Sahibayn, the ‘illah of necessity in small amounts prevents invalidation.
The difference is in how strictly the ‘illah is applied.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative position)
Later Hanafi works prefer the Sahibayn's view for ease, but the text does not give a tarjih. Recognize that both positions are valid within the school, and the mufta bihi is generally the more lenient one.
This is an example of ikhtilaf within the madhhab, not between schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بغیر عذر ایک گھڑی بھی مسجد سے نکلنا اعتکاف کے فاسد کر دیتا ہے، اقوال فقہاء لَوْ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ سَاعَةً بِغَيْرِ عُذْرٍ فَسَدَ اعْتِكَافُهُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِوُجُودِ الْمَنَافِي وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ وَقَالَا لَا حَتَّى يَكُونَ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ نِصْفِ يَوْمٍ وَهُوَ الْاِسْتِحْسَانُ لِأَنَّ فِي الْقَلِيلِ ضَرُورَةً ترجمہ اور اگر مسجد سے بغیر عذر تھوڑی دیر کے لئے نکلا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا اعتکاف فاسد ہو گیا کیونکہ منانی اعتکاف پایا گیا ہے اور یہی قیاس ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ فاسد نہ ہوگا یہاں تک کہ نصف یوم سے زائد ہو جائے اور یہیں استحسان ہے کیونکہ قلیل میں ضرورت
Leaving the mosque for even a moment without excuse invalidates i'tikaf according to Abu Hanifa, due to the existence of the contradictory (al-manafi), and this is qiyas (analogy). And the two (Sahibayn) said: It does not invalidate unless it is more than half a day, and this is istihsan (juristic preference), because in a small amount there is necessity. Translation: And if one leaves the mosque without excuse for a short time, according to Abu Hanifa his i'tikaf becomes invalid because the contradictor of i'tikaf has occurred, and this is qiyas. And the Sahibayn said: It does not invalidate until it exceeds half a day, and this is istihsan because in a small amount there is necessity.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), on the ruling of leaving the mosque without a valid excuse for a short duration during i'tikaf. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, any exit, even for a moment, invalidates i'tikaf. This is based on qiyas (analogy) because the very act of leaving contradicts the meaning of i'tikaf, which is staying (lubth) in the mosque. Since the presence of the contradictory (al-manafi) should nullify the act, the analogy is strict. The Sahibayn, however, use istihsan (juristic preference) to allow a short exit of less than half a day. They argue that a very brief exit is a practical necessity (‘illah of darurah) because it is difficult for a person to remain completely confined. Therefore, the minor exit does not invalidate i'tikaf. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is often the view of the Sahibayn due to ease, but the text does not specify tarjih here.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; used by Abu Hanifa to rule that any exit invalidates i'tikaf because there is a contradictory.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; used by the Sahibayn to permit short exits because of practical necessity.
المنافي (al-manafi): The contradictor; here it refers to the act of leaving which contradicts the state of i'tikaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the effect of leaving the mosque without excuse for a very short time during i'tikaf?
A) I'tikaf becomes invalid
B) I'tikaf remains valid
C) It is makruh
D) It requires compensation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on brief i'tikaf exits: Abu Hanifa follows qiyas to invalidate any exit, while the Sahibayn use istihsan to permit short exits of less than half a day, and this latter view is the mufta bihi.

Leaving I'tikaf for Jumu'ah: Divine vs Human Obligation
Ruling on leaving i'tikaf for Jumu'ah with timing details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving i'tikaf for Jumu'ah, distinguish between divine and human wujub, and apply the timing conditions based on distance.

Core Idea
Divine obligation always overrides human vow – Jumu'ah takes precedence over vowed i'tikaf.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a person has vowed to perform i'tikaf in a particular mosque, but Jumu'ah prayer is obligatory and must be attended. The Hanafi school establishes a clear hierarchy: the obligation from Allah (Jumu'ah) cannot be dropped for a self-imposed obligation (vowed i'tikaf). The text also provides detailed timing rules and notes a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf on the number of sunnah rak'ats after Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? A person in i'tikaf (especially a vowed one) leaving the mosque to attend Jumu'ah. The ruling is that it is wajib to leave, because Jumu'ah is a divine obligation.
The ruling is derived from the principle that divine obligation overrides human vow.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The primary evidence cited is Quran 2:187, which mentions i'tikaf in mosques. The verse implies i'tikaf is valid in any mosque, but Jumu'ah requires a congregational mosque, so leaving is necessary.
The dalil is also the broader usul principle: al-wajib al-ilahi aqwa min al-wajib al-nadhr (divine obligation is stronger than vowed obligation).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse's phrase 'في المساجد' (in the mosques) is general, allowing i'tikaf in all mosques. But Jumu'ah is only valid in a congregational mosque. Hence, to fulfill both, the mu'takif must leave his i'tikaf mosque for the congregational mosque.
This is a contextual interpretation (qarina) that prioritizes Jumu'ah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that after Jumu'ah, one prays 4 sunnah rak'ats; Imam Abu Yusuf holds 6 (including tahiyyat al-masjid). Both views are based on sunnah practice.
The ikhtilaf does not affect the main ruling; it is a secondary detail.
5
Determine the thamarah (practical consequence)
The main practical consequence is that the mu'takif may attend Jumu'ah and pray the sunnahs per his chosen view. The timing of leaving depends on distance: near mosque → after zawal; far mosque → early enough to catch sermon and sunnah.
Staying longer in the Jumu'ah mosque is makruh but does not invalidate i'tikaf.

Source Text

اسنتیں بھی نماز جمعہ کے ساتھ لاحق کی جائیں گی یعنی جس طرح نماز جمعہ کے لئے ضرورت دینی تحقیق ہے اسی طرح اس کی سنتوں کے لئے بھی متفق ہوگی ۔ اس تقریرت واضح ہو گیا کہ غیر جامع مسجد میں اعتکاف کرنے والے شخص کے لئے جامع مسجد میں نماز جمعہ ، خطبہ اور اس کی سنتوں کی بقدر قیام کرنے کی اجازت ہے لیکن اگر اس سے زائد قیام کیا تو اس کا اعتکاف فاسد تو نہ ہوگا البتہ خلاف اولی اور غیر مستحب ہے اعتکاف فاسد تو اس تھا اس کی چھت گر گئی یا اس میں جان کا خطرہ ہے تو اس سے منتقل ہو کر دوسری مسجد کی طرف جانا جائز ہے ۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Book of Fasting. 'And do not have sexual relations with them while you are secluded in the mosques.' So when i'tikaf is prescribed in every mosque, then leaving for Jumu'ah is an exception from the vow of i'tikaf just as leaving for human necessities is an exception, because to abandon Jumu'ah prayer for the protection of i'tikaf is absolutely not permissible. Therefore, the obligation of i'tikaf due to a vow is inferior to the obligation of Jumu'ah prayer, and it is inferior because Jumu'ah prayer is obligatory by Allah's making it obligatory, while i'tikaf became obligatory by the servant's making it obligatory in that he vowed i'tikaf. And the servant is not permitted to drop an obligation imposed by Allah. So it is established that Jumu'ah prayer will not be abandoned due to i'tikaf, and when Jumu'ah prayer is not abandoned, then leaving for Jumu'ah prayer will be permitted. Now, as for the time when leaving for Jumu'ah is permitted, its ruling is that if the place of i'tikaf is near the congregational mosque, then he should leave after midday, because the address for performing Jumu'ah is directed after midday. And when this address is directed, then the need arises, and when the need arises, then leaving for Jumu'ah is permitted. So since the need for performing Jumu'ah is realized after midday, he should leave after midday. But if the place of i'tikaf is far from the congregational mosque, then he is permitted to leave early enough that it is possible for him to reach Jumu'ah with the sermon, and to pray four rak'ats of sunnah before the sermon. And in one narration, he may pray six rak'ats before Jumu'ah: four sunnah and two tahiyyat al-masjid. And this mu'takif is permitted to pray four rak'ats of sunnah after Jumu'ah in the congregational mosque, as is the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa, or to pray six rak'ats as Abu Yusuf says. Its proof is that the sunnahs of Jumu'ah are subsidiary to Jumu'ah, so these sunnahs are also annexed to the Jumu'ah prayer. That is, just as religious need is realized for Jumu'ah prayer, similarly it will be agreed for its sunnahs. From this discussion it became clear that for a person performing i'tikaf in a non-congregational mosque, it is permitted to stay in the congregational mosque to the extent of Jumu'ah prayer, sermon, and its sunnahs. But if he stays more than that, his i'tikaf will not become invalid, but it is contrary to better and non-recommended. It is not invalid because the congregational mosque is also a place of i'tikaf, and it is contrary to better because he made it obligatory upon himself to perform i'tikaf in one mosque, so he should not complete it in two mosques without necessity. From this expression it is known that if he completed it in the congregational mosque or stayed extra time, the i'tikaf occurred but was disliked. And it is also known that due to an excuse, moving from one mosque to another is permitted, for example, if the roof of the mosque in which he was performing i'tikaf fell in, or there is danger to life, then moving from it to another mosque is permitted. And Allah knows best. Jameel Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah discusses the ruling of a mu'takif leaving the mosque to attend Jumu'ah prayer. The author begins by citing the Quranic verse (2:187) which prohibits conjugal relations during i'tikaf, establishing that i'tikaf is prescribed in all mosques. The key juristic point is that the obligation of Jumu'ah is from Allah (divine obligation), while the obligation of a vowed i'tikaf is from the servant (human obligation). Since divine obligation takes precedence, the mu'takif must leave for Jumu'ah. The passage then details the timing: if the mosque of i'tikaf is near the Jumu'ah mosque, he leaves after zawal (midday); if far, he leaves early enough to catch the sermon and pray sunnah. The author also notes a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the number of sunnah rak'ats after Jumu'ah — four vs six — with the reasoning that the sunnahs follow Jumu'ah. Finally, it clarifies that staying beyond the necessary time in the Jumu'ah mosque does not invalidate i'tikaf but is makruh, and that moving between mosques due to a valid excuse is permitted.

Key Terms
اعتکاف (i'tikaf): Seclusion in a mosque with the intention of worship, often for a specific period.
نذر (nazr): A vow by which a person makes an act of worship obligatory upon themselves.
وجوب (wujub): The quality of being obligatory; used to compare the strength of obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Early enough to catch the sermon and pray sunnah before it
C) At any time, regardless of distance
D) He should not leave at all, as it invalidates i'tikaf

Key Takeaway
Divine obligations override vowed obligations; the mu'takif must leave for Jumu'ah, and the timing depends on distance.

Leaving Mosque Without Excuse During I'tikaf: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on exit without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding short exits from i'tikaf and apply their qiyas and istihsan reasoning.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: any exit invalidates; Sahibayn: only if more than half a day.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of leaving the mosque without a valid excuse during i'tikaf. Understanding this disagreement reveals how the Hanafi school applies qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) within ibadat. The ruling differs in practice, and both views are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is i'tikaf, and the dispute is whether leaving the mosque without excuse for a short duration invalidates it. Note that both parties agree that a valid excuse (e.g., illness, attending Friday prayer) permits exit.
The dispute is only about exits without a recognized excuse.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that any exit, even for an hour, invalidates i'tikaf. His proof is qiyas: just as eating any amount invalidates fasting, and any hadath invalidates wudu, leaving the mosque (the contradiction of i'tikaf's pillar) invalidates i'tikaf regardless of duration.
The pillar (rukn) of i'tikaf is lubth fi al-masjid (staying in the mosque).
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that i'tikaf is not invalidated unless the absence exceeds half a day. Their proof is istihsan based on necessity (darurah) and analogy with the rule of intention in Ramadan: if one intends to fast after half the day, the fast is valid.
They set the boundary at half a day: what is less is considered qalil (small) and excused.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a mu'takif who steps out briefly without excuse must repeat the i'tikaf according to Abu Hanifa, but remains valid according to the Sahibayn as long as he returns within half a day.
Later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn for ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بغیر عذر ایک گھڑی بھی مسجد سے نکلنا اعتکاف کے فاسد کر دیتا ہے، اقوال فقہاء
لَوْ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ سَاعَةً بِغَيْرِ عُدْرٍ فَسَدَ اعْتِكَافُهُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ لِوُجُودِ الْمَنَافِي وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ وَقَالَا لَا حَتَّى يَكُونَ أكْثَرَ مِنْ نِصْفِ يَوْمٍ وَهُوَ الْإِسْتِحْسَانُ لِأَنَّ فِي الْقَلِيلِ ضَرُورَةٌ
ترجمہ اور اگر مسجد سے بغیر عذر تھوڑی دیر کے لئے نکلا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا اعتکاف فاسد ہو گیا کیونکہ منانی اعتکاف پایا گیا ہے اور یہی قیاس ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ فاسد نہ ہوگا یہاں تک کہ نصف یوم سے زائد ہو جائے اور یہیں استحسان ہے کیونکہ قلیل میں ضرورت لاحق ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مختلف اگر بلا عذر مسجد سے نکل گیا اگر چہ ایک ہی ساعت کے لئے نکلا ہو تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا اعتکاف فاسد ہو گیا اور قیاس بھی یہی ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اعتکاف فاسد نہ ہو گا ہاں اگر نصف یوم سے زائد بلا عذر مسجد سے باہر رہا تو فاسد ہو جائےگا اور استحسان بھی یہی ہے حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتکاف کا رکن لبت في المسجد ( مسجد میں ٹھہرنا ہے اور مسجد سے نکلنا اس کے منافی ہے اور شئی اپنے منافی اور ضد کے پائے جانے سے فوت ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے اعتکاف، خروج من المسجد سے فوت ہو جائے گا خروج خواہ تھوڑی دیر کے لئے ہو یا زیادہ دیر کے لئے ہو جیسے روزہ کی حالت میں کھانا روزے کو فاسد کر دیتا ہے خواہ تھوڑا کھایا ہو یا زیادہ کھایا ہو۔ اسی طرح جیسے مطلقاً حدث ناقض وضو ہے حدث تھوڑا ہو یا زیادہ ہو۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تھوڑی دیر کے لئے مسجد سے نکلنا دفع حرج کے لئے معاف ہے اور زیادہ دیر کے نکلنا معاف نہیں ہے اور قلیل وکثیر میں حد فاصل نصف یوم سے زائد ہے یعنی نصف یوم سے زائد کثیر کہلائے گا اور نصف یوم اور اس سے کم قلیل کہلائے گا ۔ جیسا کہ رمضان میں نصف یوم سے زائد میں اگر نیت پائی گئی تو روزہ معتبر ہوگا ورنہ نہیں۔
Leaving the mosque even for a moment without excuse invalidates i'tikaf, sayings of the jurists. If he left the mosque for an hour without an excuse, his i'tikaf becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa due to the presence of the contradicting factor, and this is qiyas. And they (the Sahibayn) said: not until it becomes more than half a day, and this is istihsan because in a small amount there is necessity. Translation: And if he left the mosque without an excuse for a short time, then according to Abu Hanifa his i'tikaf became invalid because the contradicting factor of i'tikaf was found, and this is qiyas. And the Sahibayn said: it will not become invalid until it exceeds half a day, and this is istihsan because in a small amount there is necessity. Explanation of the issue: That is, if a mu'takif left the mosque without an excuse, even if he left for just one hour, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa his i'tikaf becomes invalid, and this is qiyas. And the Sahibayn said: i'tikaf does not become invalid; yes, if he stayed outside the mosque without an excuse for more than half a day, then it becomes invalid, and this is istihsan. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the pillar of i'tikaf is staying in the mosque (lubth fi al-masjid), and leaving the mosque contradicts it, and a thing is lost due to the presence of its contradiction or opposite. Therefore, i'tikaf will be lost by leaving the mosque, whether the leaving is for a short time or a long time, just as eating during fasting invalidates the fast whether one eats a little or a lot. Similarly, just as hadath (ritual impurity) absolutely invalidates wudu, whether the hadath is small or large. The proof of the Sahibayn is that leaving the mosque for a short time is excused to ward off hardship, but prolonged leaving is not excused. And the boundary between small and large is exceeding half a day: what exceeds half a day is called large, and half a day or less is called small. Just as in Ramadan, if intention is found in more than half a day, the fast is valid, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of leaving the mosque without a valid excuse during i'tikaf. The text begins by quoting the Arabic ruling: if a mu'takif leaves the mosque for an hour without excuse, according to Imam Abu Hanifa his i'tikaf becomes invalid (fasid). This is based on the principle that the act of leaving the mosque (khuruj) contradicts the essence of i'tikaf (lubth fi al-masjid). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ: they say it only invalidates if the absence exceeds half a day. The commentary then explains the reasoning behind each position. Abu Hanifa applies qiyas: just as eating even a little nullifies fasting, and hadath (even small) nullifies wudu, so leaving the mosque even briefly nullifies i'tikaf. The Sahibayn apply istihsan: they consider the general need for short exits (e.g., for unavoidable human needs) and distinguish between qalil (small) and kathir (large) absence, setting the threshold at half a day. The analogy is drawn with the rule for intention in Ramadan: if one intends to fast after half the day has passed, the fast is valid; otherwise it is not. The passage does not explicitly declare which view is mufta bihi, but the fact that it presents both with reasoning suggests both are considered within the school.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here, Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to argue that any exit is like any amount of eating or hadath.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; here, the Sahibayn prefer to overlook small exits due to necessity, departing from qiyas.
منافی (munafi): Contradicting factor; something that goes against the essence of i'tikaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the threshold for a 'large' exit from i'tikaf according to the Sahibayn?
A) Any exit, regardless of duration
B) More than half a day
C) More than one day
D) More than one hour

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on the effect of short exits from i'tikaf, with Abu Hanifa applying strict qiyas and the Sahibayn applying lenient istihsan.
