Dispute on I'tikaf for Two Days: Inclusion of First Night
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dual form in i'tikaf vows

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the inclusion of the first night in a two-day i'tikaf vow, and state the mufta bihi position with its justification.

Core Idea
A vow for two days i'tikaf includes both nights — precaution in worship overrides grammatical analogy.

This passage presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of a specific vow: if someone vows i'tikaf for two days, are the nights automatically included? Imam Abu Hanifa (the relied-upon view) says yes, both nights are required. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that only the middle night is included due to the dual grammatical form. The disagreement turns on whether the dual (tathniyah) should be treated like the plural (jam') in legal obligations, especially in matters of worship where ihtiyat (precaution) is applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and disputed issue
The act is a vow (nadhr) of i'tikaf for two days. The dispute: does this obligation automatically cover the nights? Specifically, is the first night included?
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa (Zahir al-Riwayah): both nights are included (two days + two nights). Abu Yusuf: only the middle night is included (two days + one night).
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's linguistic proof
He argues that the dual (yawmayn) is grammatically distinct from the plural (ayyam). The singular (yawm) does not include the night, so by analogy the dual should not either. However, the middle night is necessary for continuity between the two days.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's counter-argument
The dual contains a meaning of plurality (Prophet said 'Two are a congregation'), so it should be treated like the plural, which includes nights. Additionally, caution (ihtiyat) in worship demands inclusion to ensure full discharge of the obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Under Abu Hanifa: two days and two nights required. Under Abu Yusuf: two days and one night (the middle). The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَوْجَبَ اعْتِكَافَ يَوْمَيْنِ يَلْزَمُهُ بِلَيَالِيهَا وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ لَا تَدْخُلُ اللَّيْلَةُ الْأُولَى لِأَنَّ الْمُثَنَّى غَيْرُ الْجَمْعِ وَالْمُتَوَسِّطَةُ ضَرُورَةُ الِاتِّصَالِ وَجْهُ الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّ فِي الْمُثَنَّى مَعْنَى الْجَمْعِ فَيُلْحَقُ بِهَا احْتِيَاطًا لِأَمْرِ الْعِبَادَةِ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ

ترجمہ: اور جس شخص نے دو یوم کا اعتکاف لازم کیا اس پر ان کی راتوں کے ساتھ لازم ہے اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ پہلی رات داخل نہ ہوگی کیونکہ تثنیہ تو جمع کے علاوہ ہے اور درمیان رات میں اتصال کی ضرورت ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ منی میں جمع کے معنی ہیں تو تثنیہ کو جمع کے ساتھ امر عبادت کی وجہ سے احتیاطاً لاحق کیا جائے گا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔

تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے دو یوم کے اعتکاف کی نذر کی تو اس پر دو یوم کا اعتکاف مع ان کی راتوں کے لازم ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ پہلی رات داخل نہ ہوگی تو گویا ابو یوسف کے نزدیک دو دن اور ایک رات کا اعتکاف لازم ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف دلیل یہ ہے کہ تثنیہ اور جمع کے درمیان مغایرت ہوتی ہے لہذا لفظ تثنیہ اور لفظ مفرد دونوں یکساں ہوں گے یعنی جو حکم لفظ مفرد کا ہو گا و ہی لفظ تثنیہ کا ہوگا اور لفظ مفرد یعنی یوما کہنے کی صورت میں پہلی رات نذر کے حکم میں داخل نہیں ہوئی یعنی فقط طلوع آفتاب سے غروب تک کا اعتکاف واجب ہوتا ہے اور رات کا واجب نہیں ہوتا پس اسی طرح لفظ تثنیہ یعنی یومین کہنے کی صورت میں بھی پہلی رات داخل نہ ہوگی رہی درمیانی رات تو وہ داخل ہو جائے گی کیونکہ اعتکاف کے لئے اتصال ضروری ہے اور اتصال اسی وقت ممکن ہے جبکہ درمیانی رات کا اعتکاف کیا جائے اس ضرورت اتصال کی وجہ سے درمیانی رات داخل ہو جائے گی اور یہ ضرورت چونکہ پہلی رات میں موجود نہیں اس لئے پہلی رات داخل نہ ہوگی۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ تثنیہ میں جمع کے معنی پائے جاتے ہیں یہی وجہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے الِاثْنَانِ فَمَا فَوْقَ جَمَاعَةٌ پس چونکہ تثنیہ میں جمع کے معنی ہیں اور اعتکاف ایک عبادت ہے اس لئے امر عبادت کی وجہ سے احتیاطاً تثنیہ کو جمع کے ساتھ لا کر دیا گیا اور جمع یعنی لفظ ایام کی صورت میں جتنے دنوں کا اعتکاف واجب ہوتا ہے اتنی ہی راتوں کا واجب ہوتا ہے لہذا تثنیہ کی صورت میں بھی دنوں کے ساتھ دو راتوں کا اعتکاف واجب ہوگا ۔ واللہ اعلم
And whoever makes obligatory the i'tikaf of two days, the i'tikaf with their nights becomes obligatory upon him. And Abu Yusuf said: The first night is not included, because the dual is not the plural, and the middle (night) is necessary for continuity. The position of the apparent (narrations) is that in the dual there is a meaning of plural, so it is annexed to the plural out of precaution for the matter of worship. And Allah knows best.

Translation: And whoever makes obligatory i'tikaf of two days, it becomes obligatory upon him with their nights. And Abu Yusuf said that the first night will not be included, because the dual is different from the plural, and the middle night is needed for continuity. And the reason of the apparent (riwayah) is that in the dual there is a meaning of plural, so the dual will be annexed to the plural out of precaution for the matter of worship. And Allah knows best what is correct.

Explanation: The issue is that if someone vows i'tikaf of two days, then i'tikaf of two days with their nights becomes obligatory. And Imam Abu Yusuf said that the first night will not be included, so according to Abu Yusuf, i'tikaf of two days and one night becomes obligatory. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that there is a difference between the dual and the plural; therefore the word in the dual and the word in the singular are the same, i.e., the ruling that applies to the singular word will also apply to the dual word. And in the case of the singular word 'yawma', the first night is not included in the ruling of the vow, meaning only i'tikaf from sunrise to sunset is obligatory, and the night is not obligatory. Similarly, in the case of the dual word 'yawmayn', the first night will not be included. As for the middle night, it will be included because continuity is necessary for i'tikaf, and continuity is only possible if the middle night's i'tikaf is performed. Due to this necessity of continuity, the middle night is included. And since this necessity does not exist for the first night, it will not be included. The reason for the apparent riwayah (the ruling of Abu Hanifa) is that in the dual there is a meaning of the plural. This is why the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Two (and more) are a congregation.' So since the dual has the meaning of plural, and i'tikaf is a form of worship, out of precaution for the matter of worship, the dual is treated like the plural. And in the case of the plural word 'ayyam', however many days' i'tikaf is obligatory, that many nights' i'tikaf is also obligatory. Therefore, in the case of the dual, i'tikaf of two nights along with the two days becomes obligatory. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the legal implications of a vow to perform i'tikaf for two days (yawmayn). It presents the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf. According to the Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon narrations attributed to Abu Hanifa), when someone makes a vow of i'tikaf for two days, both the nights corresponding to those days are included, so i'tikaf must be performed for two days and two nights consecutively. Imam Abu Yusuf differs, holding that the first night is not included; only the middle night (between the two days) is included due to the necessity of continuity. His reasoning is that the dual form (yawmayn) is grammatically distinct from the plural (ayyam), so it should be treated like the singular (yawm), which in a vow does not include the preceding night. However, the middle night is included because without it the two days would not be connected. The passage then explains the Hanafi position (the relied-upon view) which overrides Abu Yusuf's analogy based on caution in matters of worship. Since the dual has a connotation of plurality, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'Two are a congregation,' the dual is assimilated to the plural. Therefore, just as a vow for several days includes all corresponding nights, so does a vow for two days. This ruling reflects the principle of ihtiyat (precaution) in worship, preferring inclusion of the nights to ensure complete performance of the i'tikaf.

Key Terms
تَثْنِيَة (tathniyah): Dual grammatical form; in this context, 'yawmayn' (two days).
جَمْع (jam'): Plural grammatical form; in the previous lesson, 'ayyam' (days) includes nights.
احْتِيَاط (ihtiyat): Legal precaution; preferring the more comprehensive ruling in matters of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, how many nights of i'tikaf are required for a vow of two days i'tikaf?
A) Only the middle night.
B) No nights, because i'tikaf is only during the day.
C) Both the first and second nights (two nights).
D) Only the first night.

Key Takeaway
When someone vows i'tikaf for two days, the mufta bihi Hanafi ruling includes both nights, applying the principle of ihtiyat (precaution) in worship and recognizing the dual as carrying a meaning of plurality.

Ruling on Two Days of I'tikaf Including Nights
Intra-Hanafi dispute on night inclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that two days of i'tikaf include both nights and evaluate Abu Yusuf's counter-argument.

Core Idea
A vow of two days' i'tikaf obligates both nights — precaution in worship overrides linguistic distinction.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between the Zahir al-Riwayah position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf on the scope of a vow to perform i'tikaf for two days. At stake is whether the dual 'two days' includes both associated nights or only the intermediate one. The relied-upon view treats the dual like a plural for worship out of precaution (ihtiyat). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how linguistic categories and worship principles interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah: If someone vows two days of i'tikaf, both nights are wajib.
This is the mufta bihi view.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf holds that only the intermediate night is wajib; the first night is not included because the dual is not plural.
The opposing view is still within the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Abu Yusuf argues linguistically: the dual (muthanna) is distinct from the plural (jam‘); the vow starts at dawn, so the preceding night is not covered. The intermediate night is included only for continuity.
He relies on the literal meaning of 'two days'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Zahir al-Riwayah counters that the dual carries a nuance of plurality, as in the hadith 'two are a congregation'. Precaution (ihtiyat) in worship demands including both nights.
Worship principles can override strict linguistic categories.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under the mufta bihi, the person observes two full days and nights. Under Abu Yusuf, they observe two days and only the intermediate night, leaving before the first night.
The mufta bihi is more precautionary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَوْجَبَ اعْتِكَافَ يَوْمَيْنِ يَلْزَمُهُ بِلَيَالِيهَا وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا تَدْخُلُ اللَّيْلَةُ الْأُولَى لِأَنَّ الْمُثَنَّى غَيْرُ الْجَمْعِ وَاللَّيْلَةُ الْمُتَوَسِّطَةُ ضَرُورَةُ الِاتِّصَالِ وَجْهُ الظَّاهِرِ أَنَّ فِى الْمُثَنَّى مَعْنَى الْجَمْعِ فَيُلْحَقُ بِهِ احْتِيَاطًا لِأَمْرِ الْعِبَادَةِ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ
And whoever obligates i'tikaf of two days, it is necessary upon him with their nights. And Abu Yusuf said: The first night does not enter because the dual is not plural, and the intermediate night [enters] due to necessity of continuity. The view of Zahir al-Riwayah is that in the dual there is meaning of plural, so it is attached to it out of precaution for the matter of worship. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding i'tikaf (spiritual seclusion in the mosque). The ruling: if someone vows to perform i'tikaf for two days (yawmayn), according to the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah), both nights are included, meaning a full two-day-and-two-night i'tikaf is required. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the first night is not included because the dual (tathniyah) is distinct from the plural (jam'). In the plural, nights are included by default, but in the dual, only the intermediate night is included due to the necessity of continuity (i.e., the two days must be connected without a break). Abu Yusuf's reasoning: if someone says 'two days,' the first day starts at dawn, so the first night before dawn is not part of the vow; the intermediate night between the two days is included to maintain continuity. The Zahir al-Riwayah position, attributed to Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa, holds that the dual carries a meaning of plurality (as in the hadith 'al-ithnani fama fawqahuma jama'ah'), so by precaution (ihtiyat) in worship, the dual is treated like the plural, thus both nights are included. The mufta bihi (operative view) is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Key Terms
مثنى (muthannā): Dual number in Arabic grammar, referring to two of something.
جمع (jam‘): Plural number, three or more.
اتصال (ittiṣāl): Continuity; the requirement that i'tikaf be performed without interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, if someone vows i'tikaf for two days, how many nights are included?
A) Only the first night
B) Only the intermediate night
C) Both nights
D) No nights

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a vow of i'tikaf for two days obligates both nights — precaution (ihtiyat) overrides a strict linguistic distinction between dual and plural.

Sawm — Fasting
beginner
5 min
Fasting for Hunting Penalty Valid Anywhere
Brief ruling that fasting as compensation is valid anywhere

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that fasting for hunting compensation is valid anywhere and explain the underlying principle that rational acts of worship are not place-restricted.

Core Idea
Fasting for jaza al-sayd is valid anywhere — place is not a condition.

This lesson presents a concise ruling from the matn: fasting as compensation for hunting in ihram is not limited to Makkah. The reason is that fasting is an act of worship (qurbah) that is valid in any location, unlike sacrifice which requires the Haram. This ruling illustrates a general Hanafi principle about 'ibada ma'qula.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled? Fasting as one of the three options for jaza al-sayd (compensation for hunting in ihram). The ruling: it is valid (sahih) even outside Makkah.
2
Locate the reason (ta'lil)
The text gives the reason: 'because it is an act of worship in every place'. This is a concise ta'lil. Why does this matter? It connects the ruling to a general principle.
The Arabic phrase: لِأَنَّهُ قُرْبَةٌ فِي كُلِّ مَكَانٍ
3
Apply the principle to other cases
The same principle applies to any act of worship that is ma'qula (rational) — e.g., prayer is valid anywhere pure, fasting anywhere, etc. Contrast with sacrifice which is confined to the Haram.
Highlight: The Hanafi view that fasting is a bodily worship not tied to a location.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
روزہ رکھنے کے لئے جگہ متعین نہیں
وَالصَّومُ يَجُوزُ فِى غَيْرِ مَكَةِ لِأُتَهُ قُرَبَةٌ فِي كُلِّ مَكَانٍ
ترجمہ اور روزہ غیر مکہ میں جائز ہے کیونکہ روزہ ہر جگہ عبادت ہے۔
No specific place is designated for keeping the fast. And fasting is permissible outside of Makkah because it is an act of worship in every place. Translation: And fasting is permissible outside Makkah, because fasting is an act of worship in every place.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This is a concise ruling statement from the matn. The author (Al-Quduri) states that fasting as a compensation for hunting is not restricted to any specific location. The reason given is that fasting, like other rational acts of worship, is valid everywhere. This is consistent with the general Hanafi principle that acts of worship that are ma'qula (rational) are not confined to particular places unless specified by a clear text. Fasting in this context is a form of 'ibada that can be performed by any Muslim in any clean place, so it is valid outside of Makkah.

Key Terms
صوم (sawm): Fasting, as one of the three options for compensation (jaza) for hunting in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi matn, where is fasting for hunting compensation valid?
A) Only in Makkah.
B) Only in the Haram.
C) Anywhere.
D) Only in the city where the hunting occurred.

Key Takeaway
Fasting as compensation for hunting is not place-restricted; it is valid anywhere because it is an act of worship.
